# Pokemon Player

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

name: pokemon-player-v2
description: Play Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow via headless emulator and RAM reads — optimized for spatial reasoning and warp handling

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (key matchups)
- Water beats Fire, Ground, Rock
- Fire beats Grass, Bug, Ice
- Grass beats Water, Ground, Rock
- Electric beats Water, Flying
- Ground beats Fire, Electric, Rock, Poison
- Psychic beats Fighting, Poison (dominant in Gen 1!)

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock) → use Water/Grass
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (CRITICAL — differs from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference this when giving type matchup advice for Gen 1 games. Modern type charts (Gen 2+) are DIFFERENT.**

#### Super-effective relationships in Gen 1 ONLY:
- **Bug is super-effective against Poison** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison is super-effective against Bug** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Psychic** (removed in Gen 2+, but Gen 1 has a bug where Psychic is immune to Ghost)
- **Ice is NOT very effective against Fire** (wait, actually it is — Ice is SE against Grass, Ground, Flying, Dragon)
- **Poison resists Bug in Gen 1** (no, actually Poison does NOT resist Bug in Gen 1 — Poison resists Bug starting Gen 2)
- **Psychic is immune to Ghost in Gen 1** (due to programming bug, despite Ghost being SE against Psychic on the type chart)
- **Normal and Fighting are immune to Ghost** (Ghost moves do NOT affect Normal types; Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types)

#### Key Gen 1 type chart for common matchups:
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but bugged) | 0x (immune) |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | 2x (SE on Rock, SE on Ground = 4x total?) | Actually Rock resists Normal, not Grass in Gen 1 — Grass is 2x on Rock? Wait: |
| **VERIFY:** | Rock takes 2x from Water, Grass, Ground, Fighting, Steel? No Steel in Gen 1 | Rock resists Normal, Fire, Poison, Flying |
| **VERIFY:** | Ground takes 2x from Water, Grass, Ice | Ground resists Poison, Rock |
| **Therefore:** | Water vs Rock/Ground = 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| **Grass vs Rock/Ground** | = 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| Ground → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fighting → Normal | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Normal → Rock | 0.5x (NVE) | 0.5x (NVE, same) |
| Electric → Ground | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) — Poison resists Psychic in Gen 1? **No, Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1** | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |
| Psychic → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has)
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged, use Dark-type bites early or just overpower with physical)
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (key matchups)
- Water beats Fire, Ground, Rock
- Fire beats Grass, Bug, Ice
- Grass beats Water, Ground, Rock
- Electric beats Water, Flying
- Ground beats Fire, Electric, Rock, Poison
- Psychic beats Fighting, Poison (dominant in Gen 1!)

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Critical Game Knowledge (Gen 1 Specific)

### HM03 Surf — Locations and Acquisition
HM03 Surf can be obtained in TWO ways:
1. **Safari Zone entrance building** (north of Fuchsia City Pokemon Center) — Talk to the man in the back. **Requires Gold Teeth item** found inside Safari Zone Area 3 (secret house).
2. **From Koga's assistant** — After defeating Koga (Fuchsia Gym) and earning the Soul Badge, his assistant outside the gym gives you HM03 Surf.

### Teaching Surf
- Surf is an HM (Hidden Machine)—it persists on the Pokemon after use
- Can be used outside battle to cross water by pressing A while facing water
- Water-type Pokemon (especially Blastoise, Gyarados, Lapras) learn Surf naturally
- STAB (Same Type Attack Bonus) applies: Water type gets 1.5x damage from Surf
- If the target Pokemon has 4 moves, you must delete one. Safe deletions: Tackle, Tail Whip, Growl, Leer. Keep coverage moves like Water Gun, Hydro Pump, Ice Beam.
- No Move Deleter exists in Gen 1—once replaced, a move is gone forever. Be deliberate.

### Misty Pre-Battle Strategy (Cerulean Gym)
Before entering Cerulean Gym to face Misty:
1. **Save game** — always `POST /save name="before_cerulean_gym"`
2. **Visit Cerulean Pokemon Center** — heals HP and PP; buy extra Potions (3 may not be enough against Starmie's Water Pulse)
3. **Check for Grass or Electric type** — Misty uses Staryu (Lv18, Water) and Starmie (Lv21, Water/Psychic). Without super-effective moves, the battle is very difficult.
4. **If lacking type advantage** — catch Oddish or Bellsprout on Routes 5/24 (north of Cerulean), or train Pikachu to Thunderbolt (Lv26)
5. **Buildings and sidestep** — after leaving Pokemon Center/Mart/Safari Zone entrance, you are on the door tile. **MANDATORY: walk_left x2 or walk_right x2** before going north, or you will re-enter the building.
6. **Memory update**: `PKM:STRATEGY Need Grass/Electric to counter Water types in Cerulean Gym`

### Post-Battle Dialog Handling
When `a_until_dialog_end` fails to clear a long post-battle dialog (trainer speech, story text):
1. **Immediately take a screenshot** to visually confirm what is on screen
2. **Use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern 2-3 times** — holding B speeds through text scrolling, A advances to next text box
3. **Take another screenshot after each cycle** to verify dialog cleared
4. **If yes/no prompt appears** (e.g., "Use X item?"), press_a for yes, press_b for no
5. **Once overworld shows no text box**, proceed with normal gameplay
6. **Record**: `PKM:STUCK Post-battle dialog at [location] — used hold_b_120 pattern to clear`
7. **Key insight**: `a_until_dialog_end` only checks RAM dialog flag, which misses partial/scrolling text. Holding B gives time to render each chunk.

## Vending Machines in Pokemon Centers
In Gen 1, nearly every Pokemon Center has a vending machine in the back that sells:
- **Fresh Water** (200 Poke Dollars) — restores 50 HP
- **Soda Pop** (300 Poke Dollars) — restores 60 HP
- **Lemonade** (350 Poke Dollars) — restores 80 HP
These are cheaper per HP than Potions (Super Potion is 700 for 50 HP). Useful budget option.

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- HM03 Surf can be obtained via Safari Zone (requires Gold Teeth) OR after beating Koga — prioritize whichever path is faster given current progress
- When teaching Surf, there is no Move Deleter in Gen 1 — once a move is forgotten, it's gone forever. Do not delete important coverage moves.

name: pokemon-player-v2
description: Play Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow via headless emulator and RAM reads — optimized for spatial reasoning and warp handling

# Pokemon Player v2 — Enhanced Decision Protocol

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
`pokemon-agent serve --rom roms/pokemon_red.gb --port 9876`
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add `--load-state <save_name>`.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with:
`ssh -R 80:localhost:9876 nokey@localhost.run`
Redirect output to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log
for the `.lhr.life` URL. Give the user the URL with `/dashboard/` appended.

## Save and Load — CRITICAL for preventing progress loss

### When to save (MANDATORY checkpoints)
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about
- Before using a Pokemon Center (in case you need to reset)
- Before teaching an HM (no Move Deleter in Gen 1)

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name.
Good examples: `before_brock`, `route1_start`, `mt_moon_entrance`, `got_cut`

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use `--load-state` flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT — Apply strict priority hierarchy
**Priority order (MUST follow this exact order):**
1. **Poison/Burn status on lead Pokemon** → heal immediately (Antidote/Burn Heal or Pokemon Center). Poison ticks HP damage every step in overworld AND every turn in battle. This is life-threatening.
2. **Any party member at critical HP (< 30%)** → heal at Pokemon Center or use Potion
3. **Dialog/text on screen** → advance it using `hold_b_120 + press_a` pattern 2-3 times, verify with screenshot
4. **In battle (wild)** → Run if not needed, else FIGHT with type advantage
5. **In battle (trainer/gym)** → FIGHT using best moves
6. **Party PP low** → visit Pokemon Center
7. **Near story objective** → navigate carefully toward it
8. **Training to level up** → if underleveled for next gym (+3 levels below gym leader's ace)

### Step 3: DECIDE
Output decision in this exact format:
```
DECISION: [action type e.g., Heal/Travel/Battle/Explore]
REASON: [why this action was chosen based on priority]
EXACT ACTIONS (max 4):
1. [action with exact in-game button sequence]
2. [action]
3. [action]
4. [action]
SAVE POINT: [save name if applicable]
MEMORY: PKM:[prefix] [detail]
```

### Step 4: ACT
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY
Take a screenshot after every move sequence and use vision_analyze
to confirm you moved where intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory
Use PKM: prefix format. Required after every major action.

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- `press_a` — confirm, talk, select
- `press_b` — cancel, close menu
- `press_start` — open game menu
- `walk_up/down/left/right` — move one tile
- `hold_b_120` — hold B for 120 frames (use for speeding through text)
- `wait_60` — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- `a_until_dialog_end` — press A repeatedly until dialog clears (UNRELIABLE)

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol — EXACT TIMING

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black.
During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER — DO NOT DEVIATE)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send exactly: wait_60, wait_60, wait_60** in sequence (~3 seconds). Do not use `wait_180` — the emulator may not support long waits.
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning.
4. **GET /state** — confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol IMMEDIATELY.
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol — GEN 1 SPECIFIC (MANDATORY)
When you appear outside ANY building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house, Safari Zone entrance, Silph Co., etc.):
- **You are standing ON the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **FIRST ACTION MUST BE:** `walk_left x2` OR `walk_right x2`.
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

Failure to sidestep will cause an infinite loop of re-entering the building.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch:
- Scrolling text (partial text boxes being revealed)
- Nickname entry screens
- Yes/no prompts
- Battle text animations
If dialog seems stuck:
1. Take screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use `hold_b_120 + press_a` pattern 2-3 times
3. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
4. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy — EXACT SEQUENCES

### Decision Tree (follow this order)
1. In battle with wild Pokemon you want to catch? → Weaken to low HP, throw Poke Ball
2. In battle with wild Pokemon you don't need? → RUN
3. In battle with trainer/gym leader? → Check type advantage
4. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
5. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
6. Low HP on current battler? → Switch to healthier Pokemon or use Potion

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. `press_down` (moves cursor to second row left)
2. `press_right` (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. `press_a` to confirm RUN
4. `hold_b_120` to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. `press_a` (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. Wait 60 frames, then `press_a` (select first move from move list)
3. `hold_b_120` (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat `hold_b_120 + press_a` until battle ends

## Health Status Handling — EXACT PRIORITY (GEN 1 MECHANICS)

### Poison and Burn (Life-Threatening)
- **Poison**: Ticks 1/16 max HP damage every step in overworld, plus every turn in battle
- **Burn**: Ticks 1/16 max HP damage per turn in battle, plus halves Attack stat
- **ACTION**: Heal IMMEDIATELY before any other action. Use Antidote/Burn Heal or visit Pokemon Center.
- **VERIFY**: After healing, take screenshot of status screen to confirm condition is cured.

### Low HP (< 30% of max)
- Use Potion/Super Potion if in dungeon or route
- Visit Pokemon Center if in town
- Do not enter battles with low HP lead

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking — NEVER SEND MORE THAN 4
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question:
  - "Where am I relative to my destination?"
  - "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
  - "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game: POST /save stuck_recovery_[location]
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me?"
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record: PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Memory Conventions — ALWAYS RECORD AFTER MAJOR ACTIONS
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:HEALTH | Status conditions | Squirtle poisoned at Route 3 |

## Progression Milestones — EXACT ORDER
1. Choose starter (Squirtle/Charmander/Bulbasaur)
2. Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
3. **Boulder Badge** — Brock (Rock) → use Water/Grass. His Geodude (Lv12) and Onix (Lv14) are weak to Water and Grass.
4. **Cascade Badge** — Misty (Water) → Staryu (Lv18) + Starmie (Lv21, Water/Psychic). Starmie's Water Pulse hits hard. Need Grass/Electric.
5. **Thunder Badge** — Lt. Surge (Electric) → Pikachu (Lv18) + Raichu (Lv24). Use Ground type. Diglett or Dugtrio from Diglett's Cave.
6. **Rainbow Badge** — Erika (Grass) → Victreebel (Lv29), Tangela (Lv24), Vileplume (Lv29). Fire/Ice/Flying types.
7. **Soul Badge** — Koga (Poison) → Koffing (Lv37), Muk (Lv39), Koffing (Lv37), Weezing (Lv43). Ground/Psychic types.
8. **Marsh Badge** — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym. Kadabra (Lv38), Mr. Mime (Lv37), Alakazam (Lv43). Dark types not available in Gen 1 — use high HP + Special.
9. **Volcano Badge** — Blaine (Fire) → Growlithe (Lv42), Ponyta (Lv40), Rapidash (Lv42), Arcanine (Lv47). Water/Ground types.
10. **Earth Badge** — Giovanni (Ground) → Dugtrio (Lv50), Persian (Lv53), Nidoqueen (Lv53), Nidoking (Lv55), Rhydon (Lv55). Water/Grass/Ice types.
11. **Elite Four** → Lorelei (Ice), Bruno (Fighting), Agatha (Ghost), Lance (Dragon), then Champion (Blue/Green).

## Critical Game Knowledge (Gen 1 Specific) — MEMORIZE THESE

### HM03 Surf — TWO Ways to Obtain
**Method 1: Safari Zone (Fastest early)**
- Go to Safari Zone (north of Fuchsia City)
- Find the Warden's Gold Teeth in Area 3 (secret house)
- Return to Warden at Safari Zone entrance for HM03 Surf
- **Requires**: Poke Doll (for Snorlax blocking route) or bypass via Route 12

**Method 2: Koga's Assistant (Guaranteed, later)**
- After defeating Koga (Fuchsia Gym) and earning Soul Badge
- His assistant stands outside the gym
- Talk to him for HM03 Surf

### Teaching Surf — NO MOVE DELETER EXISTS IN GEN 1
- Surf is an HM — it persists on the Pokemon permanently
- Once a move is deleted to make room, it is GONE FOREVER
- Safe deletions: Tackle, Tail Whip, Growl, Leer, String Shot, Sand Attack
- DO NOT delete: Water Gun, Hydro Pump, Ice Beam, Thunderbolt, Flamethrower, Body Slam, Psychic
- Water-type Pokemon learn Surf naturally (Blastoise, Gyarados, Lapras, Vaporeon, Slowbro, Starmie)
- STAB (Same Type Attack Bonus): Water type gets 1.5x damage from Surf

### Misty Pre-Battle — EXACT PROTOCOL (Cerulean Gym)
Before stepping into Cerulean Gym:
1. **POST /save name="before_cerulean_gym"** — ALWAYS save first
2. **Visit Cerulean Pokemon Center** — heal HP/PP fully
3. **Buy Potions** — 3 Potions is NOT enough. Buy 5-6 Super Potions (700 each) or use vending machine Fresh Water (200 for 50 HP — cheaper)
4. **Check your team for type advantage:**
   - Grass (Oddish/Bellsprout on Routes 5/24) 4x effective against Starmie
   - Electric (Pikachu on Route 24, 5% encounter rate) 4x effective
   - If using Squirtle/Wartortle: tough fight, expect 3+ Potions used
   - If using Charmander/Charmeleon: VERY dangerous, Fire is weak to Water. MUST catch backup
5. **If lacking Grass/Electric**: go catch Oddish or Bellsprout on Routes 5/24 north of Cerulean
6. **Building exit protocol**: After leaving Pokemon Center, walk_left x2 or walk_right x2 before going north
7. **Save again**: POST /save name="cerulean_gym_enter"
8. **Memory**: PKM:STRATEGY Need Grass/Electric to counter Water types in Cerulean Gym

### Post-Battle Dialog Handling — ACCELERATED TEXT
When `a_until_dialog_end` fails to clear dialog:
1. Take screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. Use `hold_b_120 + press_a` pattern 2-3 times — holding B speeds through text scrolling
3. Take another screenshot after each cycle to verify dialog cleared
4. If yes/no prompt appears: press_a for yes, press_b for no
5. Once overworld shows no text box, proceed normally
6. Record: PKM:STUCK Post-battle dialog at [location] — used hold_b_120 pattern to clear

### Vending Machines — BUDGET HEALING
Every Pokemon Center in Gen 1 has a vending machine selling:
- **Fresh Water** (200 Poke Dollars) — restores 50 HP (4.0 HP per Pokedollar)
- **Soda Pop** (300 Poke Dollars) — restores 60 HP (5.0 HP per Pokedollar)
- **Lemonade** (350 Poke Dollars) — restores 80 HP (4.38 HP per Pokedollar)
- Compare: Potion (300 for 20 HP = 15 HP per dollar), Super Potion (700 for 50 HP = 14 HP per dollar)
- **Verdict**: Vending machines are cheaper per HP. Buy Fresh Water when low on funds.

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

- NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask user

name: pokemon-battle-tactician-v3
description: Optimize battle decision-making in Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow using Gen 1 mechanics, type chart, and AI behavior patterns

# Pokemon Battle Tactician v3

Provide battle strategy advice for Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow based on exact Gen 1 mechanics, including AI logic, stat stages, critical hit rates, and glitch exploitation.

## When to Use
- User asks "how to beat [gym leader/rival/wild Pokemon]"
- User is in battle and needs move selection advice
- User wants to catch or flee from a wild Pokemon
- User asks about type matchups, damage calculation, or Gen 1 battle quirks

## Core Battle Mechanics (Gen 1 Specifics)

### Damage Formula (Simplified)
`Damage = ((2 * Level * Critical / 5 + 2) * Power * A/D / 50 + 2) * STAB * Type * Random(217-255)/255`

- **Critical hits**: Based on base Speed of Pokemon. High Speed = higher crit rate. Moves with high crit rate (Slash, Razor Leaf, Crabhammer) have a boosted crit rate that is bugged in Gen 1 — they ALWAYS crit if the user's Speed stat is higher than the target's. This makes Slash exceptionally powerful.
- **STAB**: Same-type attack bonus = 1.5x multiplier
- **Type effectiveness**: Use the Gen 1 type chart (see below). Note: In Gen 1, Ice-type moves are super-effective against Fire (bug — removed in later gens)
- **Random factor**: 217-255/255 (about 85%-100% damage)

### Stat Stage System (Unique to Gen 1)
- Stat stages range from -6 to +6
- **Stage multiplier for Attack/Defense/Speed/Special**:
  - +1 = 1.5x, +2 = 2.0x, +3 = 2.5x, +4 = 3.0x, +5 = 3.5x, +6 = 4.0x
  - -1 = 2/3x, -2 = 1/2x, -3 = 2/5x, -4 = 1/3x, -5 = 2/7x, -6 = 1/4x
- **Evasion/Accuracy**: Different multiplier table — stacks multiplicatively with other stages
- **Critically important**: Stat boosts can be passed to a switched-in Pokemon via Baton Pass? NO — there is NO Baton Pass in Gen 1. Stat changes are lost on switch.

### AI Behavior Patterns
Gen 1 AI is simple but exploitable:

1. **Wild Pokemon AI**: Random move selection (uniformly random among known moves). No strategy.
2. **Trainer AI (Gym Leaders/Rival)**: Weighted random based on move effectiveness:
   - 60% chance to use super-effective move if available
   - 40% chance to use any other move
   - Will NOT switch Pokemon unless forced (no switching in Gen 1 trainer battles)
3. **AI does not predict your switches**: If you switch, the AI targets the new Pokemon with whatever move it already selected
4. **AI glitch**: If a trainer's Pokemon has 4 moves and one is disabled/sleep talk, the AI may get stuck trying to use a disabled move — exploit by disabling their best move

### Battle Glitches to Exploit
- **1/256 miss glitch**: Every move has a 1/256 chance to miss, even guaranteed-hit moves like Swift. Plan around this — never rely on a single move to win.
- **Focus Energy bug**: Focus Energy actually DECREASES your crit rate by making it 0% (code bug). NEVER use Focus Energy in Gen 1.
- **Badge stat boosts**: Each Kanto gym badge gives a 12.5% stat boost to ALL your Pokemon (not just those that fought). E.g., after 4 badges: Attack +50%, Defense +50%, Speed +50%, Special +50%. This is PERMANENT and stackable.
- **Substitute glitch**: Using Substitute when HP is low can cause the game to freeze or behave oddly. Avoid.
- **Psychic-type special split**: In Gen 1, all Ghost-type moves are Physical (based on Attack) and all Poison-type moves are Special (based on Special). Also, Ghost moves do NOT affect Psychic types due to a programming bug (instead of being super-effective, they have 0 effect).

## Gen 1 Type Chart (Complete)

| Attacking Type | Super Effective Against | Not Very Effective Against | No Effect Against |
|----------------|------------------------|---------------------------|-------------------|
| Normal | — | Rock, Ghost (0x) | Ghost |
| Fire | Grass, Ice, Bug | Water, Rock, Fire | — |
| Water | Fire, Ground, Rock | Water, Grass, Dragon | — |
| Electric | Water, Flying | Electric, Grass, Dragon | Ground |
| Grass | Water, Ground, Rock | Fire, Grass, Poison, Flying, Bug, Dragon | — |
| Ice | Grass, Ground, Flying, **Fire (Gen 1 bug)** | Water, Ice | — |
| Fighting | Normal, Ice, Rock, Dark (none in Gen 1) | Poison, Flying, Psychic | Ghost |
| Poison | Grass, Bug | Poison, Ground, Rock, Ghost | — |
| Ground | Fire, Electric, Rock, Poison | Grass, Bug | Flying |
| Flying | Grass, Fighting, Bug | Electric, Rock | — |
| Psychic | Fighting, Poison | Psychic | **Ghost (0x due to bug)** |
| Bug | Grass, Psychic | Fire, Fighting, Poison, Flying, Ghost | — |
| Rock | Fire, Ice, Flying, Bug | Water, Grass, Fighting, Ground | — |
| Ghost | **Ghost (only with Lick/Night Shade)** | **Psychic (0x bug, should be 2x)** | Normal |
| Dragon | Dragon | — | — |

## Battle Decision Priority

### Move Selection Algorithm (for your Pokemon)
1. **KO check**: Can any move OHKO (guaranteed kill)? Use it.
2. **Super-effective**: Use move that is 2x or 4x effective
3. **STAB damage**: Use same-type high power move
4. **Status move**: Only if it significantly helps (e.g., Thunder Wave to paralyze fast threat, Growl to reduce Physical damage)
5. **High base power**: Use strongest neutral move
6. **Run**: If wild and not needed, or outmatched

### Against Specific Threats

#### Brock (Rock/Ground)
- **Strategy**: Use Water or Grass moves
- **Best Pokemon**: Squirtle (Water Gun), Bulbasaur (Vine Whip)
- **Avoid**: Normal, Electric (no effect on Geodude), Fire
- **His Pokemon**: Geodude Lv10 (Rock/Ground), Onix Lv14 (Rock/Ground) — Onix has pathetic Special Defense, Water/Grass hits hard

#### Misty (Water)
- **Strategy**: Electric or Grass moves
- **Best Pokemon**: Pikachu (if starter), Oddish/Bellsprout caught on Routes before
- **Danger**: Starmie Lv21 has high Speed and Water Pulse (60 BP). If your Pokemon is slower, you may get KO'd before attacking.
- **Tip**: Paralyze Starmie with Thunder Wave first if possible

#### Lt. Surge (Electric)
- **Strategy**: Ground moves (Dig, Magnitude), or Normal-type tank
- **Best**: Dig from any Pokemon that learns it (TM 28), Dugtrio
- **Danger**: His Raichu has high Speed and Thunderbolt — if your Ground type is slow, it gets hit hard
- **Note**: All his Pokemon are pure Electric except Pikachu (pure Electric). Dig is immune to Electric for one turn.

#### Erika (Grass)
- **Strategy**: Fire, Ice, Flying, or Poison moves
- **Best**: Pidgeotto (Wing Attack), Growlithe/Vulpix, any Ice move
- **Her Pokemon**: Victreebel (Grass/Poison), Tangela (Pure Grass), Vileplume (Grass/Poison)
- **Note**: Victreebel has Razor Leaf (high crit) — dangerous if you use Water types

#### Koga (Poison)
- **Strategy**: Psychic, Ground moves
- **His Pokemon**: Koffing x2 (Poison), Muk (Poison), Weezing (Poison) — all mono-Poison
- **Note**: His Pokemon use self-destruct and minimize. Use Psychic for 2x damage; Ghost moves do NOT hit (bug)

#### Sabrina (Psychic)
- **Strategy**: Use Dark/Ghost moves? **Ghost does 0x damage (bug)**. Use Bug or (unreliable) exploit.
- **Best**: Physical Normal types with strong moves (Body Slam, Hyper Beam). Or use special wall — Snorlax is ideal.
- **Her Pokemon**: Kadabra (Lv38), Mr. Mime (Lv37), Venomoth (Lv38), Alakazam (Lv43)
- **Alakazam** has insane Special (base 135, boosted by badges and stats) — your best bet is a physical attacking Normal type that can survive a Psychic/Miracle Berry

#### Blaine (Fire)
- **Strategy**: Water, Ground, or Rock moves
- **His Pokemon**: Growlithe (Lv42), Ponyta (Lv42), Rapidash (Lv45), Arcanine (Lv47)
- **Note**: All mono-Fire. Water/Ground/Rock all hit hard. His Arcanine knows Fire Blast (120 BP, 85% accuracy)

#### Giovanni (Ground)
- **Strategy**: Water, Grass, Ice moves
- **His Pokemon**: Dugtrio (Lv50), Persian (Lv53), Nidoqueen (Lv53), Nidoking (Lv55), Rhydon (Lv55)
- **Danger**: Dugtrio is fast (base 120 Speed) and knows Dig. Rhydon has high Defense but poor Special — use Grass/Water/Special moves

## Catching Wild Pokemon

### Catch Rate Formula (Gen 1)
`Catch = floor((3 * MaxHP - 2 * CurrentHP) * Rate * Ball) / (3 * MaxHP) * Status`

- **Rate**: Species-specific (e.g., Mewtwo = 3, common Pokemon = 255)
- **Ball modifiers**: Poke Ball = 1.0x, Great Ball = 1.5x, Ultra Ball = 2.0x, Master Ball = infinite
- **Status modifiers**: Frozen/Sleep = 1.6x, Paralyzed/Burned/Poisoned = 1.0x
- **Strategy**: Weaken to red HP (~10-20%), apply Sleep (best) or Freeze, throw Ultra Ball
- **Never use**: Timer Ball, Repeat Ball (not in Gen 1)

### When to RUN from Wild Battles
- Pokemon is not needed for your team
- You have already caught it
- Your party is low HP and risk of fainting
- The wild Pokemon is faster and can KO your lead
- Use the exact cursor navigation: press_down → press_right → press_a (from default FIGHT cursor)

## Save and Reload Strategy
- **Save before every Gym Leader, Rival fight, and legendary encounter**
- **Save after catching a rare Pokemon**
- **If a battle goes badly**: reload save and try a different strategy (different moves, different Pokemon order)

## Example Battle Scenario Response Format

When answering a battle question, use this structure:

```
## Situation Analysis
[Current party, opponent, health, status conditions]

## Recommended Strategy
[Type advantage, target order, move selection]

## Specific Actions
[Step-by-step move / switch commands]

## Backup Plan
[What to do if plan fails — switch, heal, run]

## Save Point
[Reminder to save before battle]
```

## Memory Conventions for Battle Context
```
PKM:BATTLE | Current fight details (opponent, HP remaining, status)
PKM:STRATEGY | Team build advice for upcoming gym
PKM:TACTICS | Specific move sequences that worked
PKM:GLITCH | Exploitable Gen 1 bugs to use
```

## Pitfalls to Avoid
- **Do NOT use Focus Energy** (bugged — reduces crit rate to 0%)
- **Do NOT rely on Ghost moves vs Psychic** (bug — 0x damage)
- **Do NOT use Substitute at low HP** (risk of freeze)
- **Do NOT assume AI will switch** (trainers never switch in Gen 1)
- **Always account for 1/256 miss glitch** — have a backup plan
- **Badge stat boosts stack over time** — early badge rush gives huge advantage

## When to Stop and Re-evaluate
- If a Pokemon faints and you have no good switch-in
- If a Gym Leader's Pokemon out-speeds and 2HKOs you
- If you miss 3+ moves in a row (1/256 glitch streak)
- **Save and reload**, try a different approach (different lead Pokemon, different moves)

# Pokemon Player v3

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone
6. Record any dialog hang: PKM:STUCK with location and solution found

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (key matchups)
- Water beats Fire, Ground, Rock
- Fire beats Grass, Bug, Ice
- Grass beats Water, Ground, Rock
- Electric beats Water, Flying
- Ground beats Fire, Electric, Rock, Poison
- Psychic beats Fighting, Poison (dominant in Gen 1!)
- Normal (Tackle, Quick Attack) is NEVER super effective — only use if no better option
- Ghost has ZERO effect on Normal types (Gen 1 bug)

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

### PP Conservation Strategy (CRITICAL)
Pokemon Centers restore PP for free. Dungeons (Mt. Moon, Rock Tunnel, etc.) have NO centers inside.
When low on PP for your primary attack:
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** while in a dungeon — they drain PP unnecessarily
2. **Reserve STAB moves for emergencies only** (super-effective against Rock/Ground/Fire types, or trainer ace Pokemon)
3. **Use weak Normal-type moves (Tackle, Scratch, etc.) as default** against wild Pokemon or weak trainers — they have infinite PP
4. **Save 1-2 PP of your best move** for the dungeon exit/boss
5. **Immediately heal at the nearest Pokemon Center** after exiting the dungeon — this restores ALL PP (including moves that were empty)
6. Record PP status: PKM:STRATEGY with current PP counts and planned usage

### Speedrunning Advice for Dungeon Exits
When low on resources (HP or PP) deep in a dungeon:
- Navigate toward the exit directly — avoid exploration
- Take the shortest path even if it means skipping optional items/trainers
- If your Pokemon faints, your last usable Pokemon will auto-lead for the next battle
- Consider using a Repel if available to reduce wild encounters

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team/PP plans | Need Grass type before Misty; Squirtle Water Gun 2/25 PP |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations + solution | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass; dialog hang at Mt.Moon used hold_b_120 |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Water Gun (2/25), Tackle (35/35), Tail Whip (30/30) |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock) → use Water/Grass
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- Normal-type moves are NEVER super effective — don't waste them on type advantage situations
- In dungeons, running from wild Pokemon conserves PP for trainers and bosses
- Always track PP counts for special moves — running out mid-dungeon with no Ethers can force a reset
- Pokemon Centers fully restore PP for ALL moves, even moves that were at 0 PP

# Pokemon Player v3

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks strategic questions about Gen 1 mechanics or gameplay decisions

## CRITICAL: Domain-Specific Gen 1 Mechanics (These differ from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference these Gen 1 specific rules when giving advice. Modern players may give incorrect advice based on Gen 2+ mechanics.**

### Type Chart Differences from Modern Games
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect (Gen 2+) |
|------------------------------|--------------|----------------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (super-effective) | 0.5x (not very effective) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (super-effective) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (super-effective, but bugged — Psychic is immune in practice) | 0x (immune) |
| Poison → Psychic | 1x (neutral — Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1) | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (same as modern) | 2x (same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |

### Battle Damage Calculation Nuances for Gen 1
When calculating effective damage, consider ALL multipliers:
1. **Type effectiveness** (use Gen 1 chart above)
2. **STAB (Same-Type Attack Bonus)** — 1.5x if move type matches Pokemon type
3. **Base power of the move**
4. **Level difference**

**Formula reference:** Effective Power = Base Power × STAB (1.5 if applicable) × Type Effectiveness
- Leech Life (20 base, Bug, STAB for Bug types) vs Koffing (Poison): 20 × 1.5 × 2 = 60 effective
- Scratch (40 base, Normal, no STAB) vs Koffing (Poison): 40 × 1 × 1 = 40 effective

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends
