### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move (reference Gen 1 specific chart)
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move (calculate effective power)
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### When Giving Strategic Advice (Not Executing Actions)
- **Provide clear, actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step battle/navigation plan
- **Calculate effective damage explicitly** using the formula: Base Power × STAB × Type Effectiveness
- **Reference Gen 1 specific mechanics** when they differ from modern games
- **Address potential incorrect advice from users** who may cite modern game rules
- **Include resource management considerations** (PP, HP, items) in every plan
- **Specify exact button sequences** (e.g., "press_down, press_right, press_a to select RUN")

### Gen 1 Type Chart (CRITICAL — differs from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference this when giving type matchup advice for Gen 1 games. Modern type charts (Gen 2+) are DIFFERENT.**

#### Super-effective relationships in Gen 1 ONLY:
- **Bug is super-effective against Poison** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison is super-effective against Bug** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Psychic** (removed in Gen 2+, but Gen 1 has a bug where Psychic is immune to Ghost)
- **Ice is NOT very effective against Fire** (wait, actually it is — Ice is SE against Grass, Ground, Flying, Dragon)
- **Poison resists Bug in Gen 1** (no, actually Poison does NOT resist Bug in Gen 1 — Poison resists Bug starting Gen 2)
- **Psychic is immune to Ghost in Gen 1** (due to programming bug, despite Ghost being SE against Psychic on the type chart)
- **Normal and Fighting are immune to Ghost** (Ghost moves do NOT affect Normal types; Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types)

#### Key Gen 1 type chart for common matchups:
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but bugged) | 0x (immune) |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | = 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| Ground → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fighting → Normal | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Normal → Rock | 0.5x (NVE) | 0.5x (NVE, same) |
| Electric → Ground | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) — Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1 | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |
| Psychic → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing
- **Status conditions (Poison, Burn, Paralysis) should be healed BEFORE moving** — Poison deals damage per step in overworld, so waiting costs HP

### Item Priority for Healing
1. Status condition → use appropriate heal item (Antidote, Burn Heal, etc.)
2. Low HP → use Potion (restores 20 HP)
3. No items → walk to nearest Pokemon Center

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has)
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged, use Dark-type bites early or just overpower with physical)
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)
- **Explicitly calculate effective damage** (Base Power × STAB × Type Effectiveness) when comparing move options
- **Address and correct any incorrect modern game assumptions** the user may state — always verify with Gen 1 specific rules
- **Status conditions on overworld Pokemon must be healed immediately** — Poison deals damage per step, so every step costs HP

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks strategic questions about Gen 1 mechanics or gameplay decisions
- User asks about type matchups, move effectiveness, item locations, or progression paths in Gen 1

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about
- BEFORE entering the Safari Zone (step limit and PokéDollar cost)
- Before teaching an HM move

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut, safari_zone_entry

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart — CRITICAL: DIFFERS FROM MODERN (Gen 2+)
**Gen 1 has different type matchups than all modern games. Always explicitly reference this chart when giving type matchup advice.**

#### Key Differences from Modern Games:
| Context | Gen 1 (Red/Blue/Yellow) | Modern (Gen 2+) | Impact Example |
|---------|-------------------------|-----------------|----------------|
| Bug vs Poison | 2x (Bug deals super-effective damage) | 0.5x (Bug not very effective) | Paras's Leech Life hits Koffing for 2x in Gen 1 |
| Poison vs Bug | 2x (Poison deals super-effective damage) | 1x (neutral) | Beedrill's Poison Sting hits Paras for 2x |
| Ghost vs Psychic | 2x (Ghost is super-effective, BUT bugged — Psychic immune to Ghost) | 0x (immune) | Lick vs Kadabra: would be 2x if not for bug, but never works |
| Psychic vs Poison | 1x (neutral, Poison does NOT resist Psychic) | 0.5x (Poison resists Psychic) | Gengar takes full damage from Psychic in Gen 1 |
| Ice vs Fire | 1x (Ice is neutral, not super-effective) | 1x (same) |
| Poison vs Bug (defense) | Bug does NOT resist Poison | Bug resists Poison | |

#### Gen 1 Complete Type Effectiveness Table (Common Matchups):
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effectiveness | Notes |
|------------------------------|---------------------|-------|
| Bug → Poison | **2x** | Changed to 0.5x in Gen 2+ |
| Poison → Bug | **2x** | Changed to 1x in Gen 2+ |
| Ghost → Psychic | **2x (bugged: Psychic is immune)** | Due to programming error, despite chart showing 2x |
| Psychic → Poison | **1x** | Changed to 0.5x in Gen 2+ |
| Poison → Poison | **0.5x** | Same in modern |
| Normal → Rock | **0.5x** | Same in modern |
| Fighting → Normal | **2x** | Same in modern |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | **4x** | Double super-effective (Rock weak to Grass, Ground weak to Grass) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x** | Double super-effective (Rock weak to Water, Ground weak to Water) |
| Electric → Ground | **0x** | Immune, same in modern |
| Ghost → Normal | **0x** | Immune, same in modern |
| Fighting → Ghost | **0x** | Immune, same in modern |

#### Gen 1 STAB (Same-Type Attack Bonus):
- STAB applies in Gen 1: moves of the same type as the Pokemon deal 1.5x damage
- **Example:** Paras (Bug/Grass) using Leech Life (Bug): 20 base power × 1.5 STAB = effective 30 power before type effectiveness

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing

### Move Selection: When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility
- **Example:** Leech Life (Bug, 20 BP) vs Scratch (Normal, 40 BP) against a Poison type in Gen 1: Leech Life deals 20 × 1.5 STAB × 2 SE = 60 effective, vs Scratch 40 neutral. Leech Life ALSO heals the user for half damage dealt — higher utility.
- **Example:** Vine Whip (Grass, 35 BP) vs Tackle (Normal, 35 BP) against a Water type: Vine Whip is 2x SE and has STAB → 35 × 1.5 × 2 = 105 effective vs Tackle 35. Both are single-target, but Vine Whip is clearly better.

## HM and Item Location Guide (Gen 1)

### Key HM Locations:
| HM | Move | Location | How to Obtain |
|----|------|----------|---------------|
| HM01 | Cut | S.S. Anne | Captain's cabin, after beating rival on S.S. Anne |
| HM02 | Fly | Route 16 | From the girl in the house south of Celadon City, after obtaining the Bicycle |
| HM03 | Surf | Safari Zone | Give Gold Teeth to Warden in Fuchsia City (Gold Teeth found in Safari Zone Area 3 Secret House) |
| HM04 | Strength | Safari Zone | Warden's house, after catching 50+ Pokemon species (or Route 11 guard depending on version) |
| HM05 | Flash | Route 2 (or Prof. Oak's Aide) | After catching 10 Pokemon species, talk to Prof. Oak's Aide north of Viridian Forest |

### Safari Zone Navigation (Gold Teeth Quest):
1. Enter Safari Zone from Fuchsia City (cost: 500 PokéDollars, 500 step limit)
2. Area 1 → go **west** through door → Area 2
3. Area 2 → go **north** through door → Area 3
4. Area 3 → go **west** then **north** to find the Secret House
5. Pick up Gold Teeth from table inside
6. Exit Safari Zone and return to Warden's house in Fuchsia City
7. Trade Gold Teeth for HM03 Surf

### HM Teaching Mechanics:
- HMs cannot be forgotten in Gen 1 without visiting the Move Deleter in Fuchsia City (at the Pokémon Fan Club, available only after obtaining 7 badges)
- Plan which Pokemon learns each HM — Blastoise can learn Surf, but it takes up a move slot permanently until late game
- Always confirm the target Pokemon can learn the HM before teaching

## Gym Leader Strategy (Gen 1)

| Gym | Leader | Type | Weakness | Key Strategy |
|-----|--------|------|----------|--------------|
| Pewter | Brock | Rock/Ground | Water (4x), Grass (4x), Fighting (2x) | Squirtle/Bulbasaur recommended |
| Cerulean | Misty | Water | Grass, Electric | Bulbasaur/Pikachu recommended |
| Vermilion | Lt. Surge | Electric | Ground | Diglett/Dugtrio from Diglett's Cave |
| Celadon | Erika | Grass | Fire, Ice, Flying, Bug | Poison types resist Grass |
| Fuchsia | Koga | Poison | Ground, Psychic (neutral in Gen 1) | Ground for Rock-type coverage |
| Saffron | Sabrina | Psychic | Ghost (bugged, doesn't work), Bug, Dark | Use strong physical attackers or high-level Pokemon |
| Cinnabar | Blaine | Fire | Water, Ground, Rock | Water types dominate |
| Viridian | Giovanni | Ground | Water, Grass, Ice | Blastoise with Surf |

## Gen 1 Specific Mechanics to Remember:
- **Critical Hit Rate:** Based on Speed stat (higher Speed = more crits) and moves with high crit rate
- **Wrap/Bind/Clamp:** These moves trap and damage the opponent over multiple turns; can be very strong in Gen 1
- **1/256 Glitch:** Some moves have a small chance of missing or failing due to a programming quirk
- **Badge Boost Glitches:** Badges boost certain stats by 12.5% even without the stat being changed
- **Focus Energy:** Due to a bug, using Focus Energy actually DECREASES your crit rate in Gen 1 (divides crit chance by 4 instead of multiplying)

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |
| PKM:HM_INFO | HM learned and where | Blastoise knows Surf (from Warden) |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has)
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged, use Dark-type bites early or just overpower with physical)
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters (including Safari Zone entry)
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the specific Gen 1 chart above when advising on type matchups. Bug beats Poison in Gen 1; Poison beats Bug in Gen 1; Psychic is neutral on Poison in Gen 1.
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis. Include specific locations, NPC names, item pickup locations, and step counts where relevant.
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)
- **HM moves cannot be forgotten easily in Gen 1** — always warn the user before teaching an HM that it is permanent until the Move Deleter in Fuchsia City (late game)
- **Safari Zone has a 500 step limit and costs 500 PokéDollars** — always advise saving before entering and running from wild Pokemon to conserve steps

# Pokemon Battle Tactician v3

Provide battle strategy advice for Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow based on exact Gen 1 mechanics, including AI logic, stat stages, critical hit rates, glitch exploitation, and **non-combat navigation logic (overworld movement, save management, resource conservation)**.

## When to Use
- User asks "how to beat [gym leader/rival/wild Pokemon]"
- User is in battle and needs move selection advice
- User wants to catch or flee from a wild Pokemon
- User asks about type matchups, damage calculation, or Gen 1 battle quirks
- **User asks about overworld navigation (e.g., "what to do next in Route X?")**
- **User asks about resource management (PP, HP, items, escape strategies)**
- **User asks about safe save points or step-by-step movement sequences**

## Core Battle Mechanics (Gen 1 Specifics) — Same as original, keep all original subsections:
### Damage Formula (Simplified)
### Stat Stage System (Unique to Gen 1)
### AI Behavior Patterns
### Battle Glitches to Exploit
### Gen 1 Type Chart (Complete)
### Battle Decision Priority
### Against Specific Threats (Brock, Misty, Lt. Surge, Erika, Koga, Sabrina, Blaine, Giovanni)
### Catching Wild Pokemon
### Save and Reload Strategy
### Example Battle Scenario Response Format
### Memory Conventions
### Pitfalls to Avoid
### When to Stop and Re-evaluate

## ADDITIONAL: Overworld Navigation & Resource Management Protocol

### Movement Priority (Non-Combat)
1. **If standing at a door/town exit**: First action is ALWAYS to **save the game** before leaving a safe zone (Pokemon Center, town). This prevents progress loss from random encounters or trainer battles.
2. **If on a route/cave**: Before entering a new area or room, **save**. If you forgot to save, retreat to last safe zone if possible.
3. **Use Repel if available** and you are underleveled or low on resources. Repel works for 100 steps and prevents encounters with wild Pokemon weaker than your lead Pokemon.
4. **Run from unnecessary wild encounters** to conserve PP and HP — press DOWN, RIGHT, A from the FIGHT cursor to run.

### Resource Management (PP & HP Conservation)
- **Primary attack reserve**: Never waste STAB or super-effective PP on weak wild Pokemon if a neutral move (Tackle, Scratch, etc.) can KO in reasonable time.
- **Emergency PP reserve**: Keep at least 2 PP of your strongest move for forced boss/trainer battles. If below that, consider retreating to heal or using a different party member.
- **HP conservation**: If HP drops below 50% and no Potion is available in inventory, strongly consider retreating or using a Pokemon with higher base HP/Defense. Do not risk fainting in a long dungeon.
- **Item prioritization**:
  - Potions: Use only if a Pokemon would faint from the next strong hit
  - Antidotes/Awakenings: Use immediately if status condition prevents effective attacking
  - Ethers/Elixirs: Save exclusively for restoring critical STAB or coverage moves with <3 PP left

### Escape/Retreat Decision
- **If party is low on HP (all Pokemon <30%)**: Turn back to nearest Pokemon Center immediately. Do not push forward — risk of blackout and losing money.
- **If trapped in a cave/dungeon**: Use Escape Rope if available (works 100%). If no Escape Rope, systematically backtrack while fighting only unavoidable trainers.
- **If a wild Pokemon is faster and can 2HKO your lead**: Switch to a tankier Pokemon or run immediately.

### Safe Save Points (Non-Obvious)
- **Always save** before: Gym battles, rival fights, legendary encounters, entering caves, entering a new route for the first time, after catching a rare Pokemon, after a major purchase of TMs/Balls.
- **Never save** during a battle (glitch risk) or in the middle of a cutscene.

## Expanded Example Response Format (For Non-Battle Queries)

When answering an **overworld navigation or resource management question**, use this structure:

```
## Situation Analysis
[Current location, party status (HP/PP summary), inventory status, objective]

## Recommended Strategy
[Optimal sequence of actions — save-first, move direction, battle avoidance, item use]

## Specific Actions
[Step-by-step movement commands and menu actions — e.g., "Press Start → Save → Walk Up"]

## Resource Conservation Plan
[Which moves to use vs wild Pokemon, which to save, items to use or avoid]

## Backup Plan
[What to do if resources run out, or if a strong trainer blocks the path]

## Save Point
[Reminder to save now or at the next specific location]
```

## Additional Pitfalls (Navigation-Specific)
- **Do NOT save in a room with a scripted event** (e.g., Team Rocket grunt stopping you) — you may get stuck.
- **Do NOT waste PP on wild Pokemon you can safely run from** — running costs 0 PP.
- **Do NOT heal with a Potion if a Pokemon Center is 10 steps away** — waste of items.
- **Always account for 1/256 miss glitch even when using Tackle on a wild Pokemon** — a miss could lead to an extra hit that drains HP.
- **Remember that badge stat boosts are permanent** — as you earn badges, your Pokemon become stronger without leveling. This affects damage calculations for wild encounters and trainers.

## Generalizable Strategy for All Tasks
When responding to ANY task (battle, navigation, or resource management), always follow this priority logic:

1. **Safety first**: Save the game if in a safe zone and about to take a risky action.
2. **Resource check**: Assess current PP, HP, items, and location danger level before committing.
3. **Objective analysis**: What exactly does the user need to accomplish? (KO a Pokemon? Reach a town? Conserve PP?)
4. **Execute efficiently**: Provide step-by-step commands (movement keys, menu selections, fight commands) so the user can replicate exactly.
5. **Backup always**: Never assume the plan works perfectly — include a fallback option.
6. **Save reminder**: End every response with a save recommendation.

name: pokemon-red-blue-yellow-emulation-advisor
description: Provide real-time gameplay guidance for Pokemon Gen 1 emulation, handling state transitions, UI interactions, and strategic decision-making in both overworld and battle scenarios
---

# Pokemon Gen 1 Emulation Advisor

Provide precise, actionable guidance for Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow gameplay via emulation, covering overworld navigation, battle mechanics, dialog handling, and state transition management.

## When to Use
- User needs to navigate overworld or transition between maps
- User is in a dialog sequence (trainer speech, NPC text, menu)
- User needs priority decisions about status effects, item usage, or path planning
- User encounters emulation-specific issues (black screens, state desync, dialog not closing)
- User asks about game state interpretation from screenshots or API responses

## Core Emulation State Management

### Map/Area Transitions
- **Door warps**: After pressing A on a door, the screen goes black for 1-2 frames while the new map loads. DO NOT send directional inputs during this time.
- **Transition detection**: Poll GET /state for map coordinate changes. If coordinates haven't updated, the transition is still in progress.
- **Danger of early input**: Can cause walking into walls, re-triggering the same door, or softlocks where tiles fail to load properly.
- **Safe practice**: Wait until new coordinates appear in GET /state, then wait 1 additional frame before sending movement inputs.

### Dialog Sequence Handling
- **Post-battle trainer speeches**: These are often 2-3 text boxes long. After the battle AI ends, you must press A multiple times (typically 2-4 presses) to advance through all dialog boxes.
- **Dialog end detection**: The `a_until_dialog_end` action may return before all dialog boxes close. If the screenshot still shows a dialog box, press A again.
- **NPC conversations**: Similar multi-box patterns. Continue pressing A until the dialog fully disappears and the player character is visible.
- **Menu navigation**: Always verify cursor position matches expectations before confirming actions.

### Overworld Status Effects
- **Poison damage**: Deals 1/8 of max HP per step taken in the overworld. This is extremely dangerous for long routes.
- **Burn damage**: 1/16 max HP per step.
- **Decision priority for poison**:
  1. Use Antidote immediately if available (stops all future damage)
  2. If no Antidote: calculate steps to nearest Pokemon Center vs. remaining HP
  3. Only use Potions AFTER curing poison (potion-only delays the inevitable)
  4. Running to Pokemon Center is viable if HP > (steps_remaining × HP_per_step_damage)

## Battle Mechanics (Gen 1 Specific)

### Damage Formula (Simplified)
`Damage = ((2 * Level * Critical / 5 + 2) * Power * A/D / 50 + 2) * STAB * Type * Random(217-255)/255`

### Critical Hit System
- Based on base Speed stat
- High-crit moves (Slash, Razor Leaf, Crabhammer): **Always crit if user's Speed > target's Speed** (bug)
- Focus Energy: **BUGGED** - reduces crit rate to 0%. NEVER use.

### Stat Stage System
- Range: -6 to +6
- Boosts lost on switch (no Baton Pass in Gen 1)
- Badge stat boosts: Each gym badge gives permanent 12.5% boost to ALL stats for ALL Pokemon

### AI Behavior
- **Wild Pokemon**: Random move selection
- **Trainers**: 60% chance to use super-effective move, 40% random
- **No switching**: Trainers never switch Pokemon
- **AI glitch**: Can get stuck trying to use disabled/sleeping move

## Resource Management Priority

### Item Usage Priority
1. Status healing (Antidote, Full Heal, Burn Heal) - ALWAYS first
2. HP restoration (Potion, Super Potion, Hyper Potion) - use after status cured
3. PP restoration (Ether, Elixir) - for long dungeon crawls
4. Battle items (X Attack, X Speed) - use before boss fights

### Catch Priority
1. Weaken to red HP (10-20% remaining)
2. Apply Sleep or Freeze status (1.6x catch multiplier)
3. Use best ball available (Ultra > Great > Poke)
4. Save before any legendary encounter

## Type Chart (Gen 1 Specific Bugs)

### Critical Bug: Ghost vs Psychic
- Ghost moves do 0x damage to Psychic types (programming bug)
- Despite type chart showing Ghost should be super-effective

### Critical Bug: Ice vs Fire
- Ice moves ARE super-effective against Fire in Gen 1 (bug removed in later gens)

### Special Split Note
- All Ghost moves are Physical (based on Attack stat)
- All Poison moves are Special (based on Special stat)

## Decision Priority Algorithm

### Overworld Priority
1. **Status threat**: If lead Pokemon has poison/burn, cure or reach Pokemon Center immediately
2. **HP threat**: If lead Pokemon HP is low, heal or reach safe zone
3. **PP management**: If primary moves are out of PP, consider switching or using Ether
4. **Navigation efficiency**: Choose shortest safe path to destination

### Battle Priority
1. **Guaranteed KO**: Use move that will OHKO
2. **Super-effective**: 2x or 4x effective move
3. **STAB damage**: Same-type high power move
4. **Status move**: Only if significantly helpful (Thunder Wave vs fast threats)
5. **High base power**: Strongest neutral move
6. **Run**: If wild and not needed

## Response Format

When answering gameplay questions, use this structure:

```
## Situation Analysis
[Current game state: location, party status, HP, status conditions, bag items]

## Recommended Action
[Single clear action with reasoning]

## Step-by-Step Execution
[Specific input sequence: button presses, menu navigation, timing]

## Backup Plan
[Fallback if primary action fails or unexpected outcomes occur]

## Save Reminder
[When to save/load to preserve progress]
```

## Common Emulation Pitfalls to Avoid
- **Do NOT input during map transitions** (black screen after door warps)
- **Do NOT assume one A press closes dialog** (trainer speeches are multi-box)
- **Do NOT use Focus Energy** (bugged)
- **Do NOT use Ghost moves vs Psychic** (bugged 0x damage)
- **Do NOT rely on Swift/Sure-shot moves** (1/256 miss glitch affects all moves)
- **Do NOT ignore poison ticks** (1/8 HP per step can kill in 8 steps)
- **Always account for status effects on lead Pokemon before long overworld treks**

## Save Strategy
- Save before every Gym Leader and Rival battle
- Save before entering caves, dungeons, or new routes
- Save after catching rare Pokemon
- Save before legendary encounters
- If stuck or softlocked: reload last save and approach differently

## When to Re-evaluate
- If HP drops below 30% with no healing items
- If 3+ consecutive moves miss (1/256 glitch streak)
- If primary strategy fails twice in a row
- If unexpected status condition cripples key Pokemon

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks strategic questions about Gen 1 mechanics or gameplay decisions

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (CRITICAL — differs from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference this when giving type matchup advice for Gen 1 games. Modern type charts (Gen 2+) are DIFFERENT.**

#### Super-effective relationships in Gen 1 ONLY:
- **Bug is super-effective against Poison** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison is super-effective against Bug** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Psychic** (removed in Gen 2+, but Gen 1 has a bug where Psychic is immune to Ghost)
- **Ice is NOT very effective against Fire** (wait, actually it is — Ice is SE against Grass, Ground, Flying, Dragon)
- **Poison resists Bug in Gen 1** (no, actually Poison does NOT resist Bug in Gen 1 — Poison resists Bug starting Gen 2)
- **Psychic is immune to Ghost in Gen 1** (due to programming bug, despite Ghost being SE against Psychic on the type chart)
- **Normal and Fighting are immune to Ghost** (Ghost moves do NOT affect Normal types; Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types)

#### Key Gen 1 type chart for common matchups:
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but bugged) | 0x (immune) |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | 2x (SE on Rock, SE on Ground = 4x total?) | Actually Rock resists Normal, not Grass in Gen 1 — Grass is 2x on Rock? Wait: |
| **VERIFY:** | Rock takes 2x from Water, Grass, Ground, Fighting, Steel? No Steel in Gen 1 | Rock resists Normal, Fire, Poison, Flying |
| **VERIFY:** | Ground takes 2x from Water, Grass, Ice | Ground resists Poison, Rock |
| **Therefore:** | Water vs Rock/Ground = 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| **Grass vs Rock/Ground** | = 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| Ground → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fighting → Normal | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Normal → Rock | 0.5x (NVE) | 0.5x (NVE, same) |
| Electric → Ground | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) — Poison resists Psychic in Gen 1? **No, Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1** | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |
| Psychic → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has)
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged, use Dark-type bites early or just overpower with physical)
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)
- **When answering Gen 1 game mechanic questions, always explicitly state if a mechanic differs from modern games, and cite the specific Gen 1 rule** — do not just give the answer without contextualizing why it's different
- **When the user asks for a step-by-step plan to obtain an item or HM, include: exact location in the overworld, any prerequisite badges or items needed, precise menu navigation (which pocket, which button presses), and what to do if the player doesn't have a compatible Pokemon**
- **When comparing move damage, calculate the full effective power including STAB (1.5x), type effectiveness (0x, 0.5x, 1x, 2x, or 4x in Gen 1), and note if the defending Pokemon's secondary type affects the calculation** — show your math explicitly

2026/06/07 11:47:03 INFO dspy.teleprompt.gepa.gepa: Iteration 12: Proposed new text for skill_text.predict: ## Knowledge Conflict Resolution Protocol

When a user or external source provides advice, facts, or strategies that conflict with correct Gen 1 (Red/Blue/Yellow) mechanics:

### 1. Identify the Source of the Error
Determine if the advice is based on:
- **Modern (Gen 2+)** mechanics that differ from Gen 1 (e.g., type chart, PP system, Focus Energy bug)
- **Fan myths** that are incorrect in any generation (e.g., "Ghost beats Psychic" without noting the Gen 1 bug)
- **Incorrect memory** of locations, item effects, or NPC behavior

### 2. State the Gen 1 Fact Directly
Correct the error explicitly, citing the exact Gen 1 rule or mechanic. Use concrete examples:
- *"In Gen 1, Bug is 2x super-effective against Poison. This changed to 0.5x in Gen 2+. So the advice 'Bug is weak vs Poison' applies only to modern games."*
- *"Focus Energy in Gen 1 actually reduces your crit rate due to a programming bug. Do not use it in Red/Blue."*

### 3. Recalculate the Correct Outcome
Show the user the correct calculation using Gen 1 rules:
- Damage formula: Base Power × STAB (1.5x if same type) × Type Effectiveness (use Gen 1 table) × Critical (if applicable)
- Include any utility benefits (e.g., Leech Life heals, Wrap traps opponent)

### 4. Provide a Corrected Action/Advice
Give a clear, Gen 1-accurate recommendation that overrides the incorrect advice. For example:
- *"Instead of running from Koffing, use Leech Life for 60 effective power plus healing. Do NOT use Scratch."*
- *"Do not teach 'Flash' to your main battler; teach it to a Pokémon you don't use in combat, like a Rattata."*

### 5. Record the Correction
Log the corrected information in memory with the prefix `PKM:CORRECTION`:
- Example: `PKM:CORRECTION Bug vs Poison is 2x in Gen 1, not 0.5x like modern games.`

## Strategic Advice Specialization

When the user asks for strategic advice (not during active gameplay), you must:

### 1. Provide a Step-by-Step Actionable Plan
Break the advice into sequential steps that can be directly executed in the game loop. Include specific locations, NPC names, item coordinates, and step counts where known.

### 2. Include Resource Management Details
Always specify:
- How much PP to conserve for key moves (e.g., "Save at least 2 PP of Water Gun for Brock's Onix")
- When to heal (e.g., "Heal at Pewter Pokémon Center BEFORE entering Mt. Moon — do not enter with less than full team HP")
- How to manage PokéDollars (e.g., "Buy 5 Potions and 3 Antidotes before Route 3")

### 3. Warn of Gen 1 Pitfalls
Always include warnings about Gen 1-specific traps:
- Ledges are one-way (jump south only)
- Ghost moves are bugged vs Psychic (don't rely on Lick)
- Safari Zone has a 500-step limit and costs 500 PokéDollars
- HMs cannot be forgotten until Fuchsia City (late game)
- 1/256 glitch can cause unexpected misses

### 4. Cross-Validate with Gen 1 Type Chart
When recommending type advantages, always explicitly reference the Gen 1 type chart provided in the instructions. Do NOT assume modern type matchups.

## Handling Cross-Generation Confusion

If the user mentions playing a different Pokémon game (e.g., "In Pokémon Gold...", "In Pokémon Sword..."), immediately:

1. **Flag the generational difference** — "That rule applies to Gen 2+, but in Gen 1 it works differently because..."
2. **Provide the Gen 1 equivalent** — "In Red/Blue, the item that does that is X, located at Y."
3. **Warn of consequences** — "If you follow modern advice in Gen 1, you will waste PP, lose type advantage, or get stuck on ledges."

name: pokemon-red-dialog-and-state-management
description: Handle post-battle dialog loops, overworld status management, and safe navigation in Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow
---

# Pokemon Red Dialog & State Management

Provide step-by-step guidance for handling edge cases in Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow gameplay, including dialog loops, overworld status effects, item prioritization, and safe navigation between locations.

## When to Use
- User reports that a dialog box remains active after a battle or event, even after pressing A
- User needs to manage a lead Pokemon with a status condition (Poison, Burn, Paralysis) in the overworld
- User is navigating between towns or routes with limited items and needs optimal resource management
- User is stuck in a loop or needs to recover from a failed battle or dialog state

## Core Mechanics (Gen 1 Specifics for State Management)

### Dialog System Behavior
- **Post-battle speech**: After defeating a trainer, the game displays a multi-screen speech. Each screen requires an A press to advance. The last screen requires a final A press to close the dialog and return to the overworld.
- **Dialog stuck detection**: If `a_until_dialog_end` action returns but the dialog is still visible on the screenshot, this means either:
  1. There are additional text boxes remaining (press A again)
  2. The dialog is on its last screen but requires exactly one more A press to close
- **Multiple NPC interactions**: Some NPCs (e.g., professors, item givers) have multi-part dialogs that function identically.
- **No auto-advance**: Gen 1 never auto-advances dialog. Every text box requires a button press (usually A, sometimes B cancels certain menus but not story dialog).

### Overworld Status Damage (Poison/Burn)
- **Poison**: Ticks 1/8 of max HP every 4 steps in the overworld
- **Burn** (from Fire moves or Burn Heal neglect): Ticks 1/16 of max HP every 4 steps
- **Priority**: Cure the status FIRST with an Antidote/Burn Heal, THEN heal HP with Potions. Healing HP without curing status wastes items as damage continues to tick.
- **1/256 miss glitch applies to all moves**: Always assume any action (including using items) has a tiny chance to fail? No — items do not miss. This glitch only applies to battle moves.
- **Item management**: Antidotes are cheap (100 Poke) and abundant in early game. Prioritize them over Potions for status healing if the Pokemon has >50% HP.

### Safe Navigation Between Locations
- **Route 3 to Mt. Moon**: ~15-20 tiles from the grassy area to the entrance. Wild encounters possible (level 8-12 Pokemon).
- **Saving strategy**: Save before entering caves/dungeons, before gym battles, and after catching rare Pokemon. Do NOT save mid-battle or mid-dialog (can corrupt save state).
- **Running from wild battles**: Default cursor is on FIGHT. Navigate: press_down (to RUN), press_right (to select RUN), press_a (to confirm). This pattern works for all Gen 1 battles.

### Resource Priority Algorithm
When limited items and multiple problems exist, use this priority:

1. **Status cure first** (Antidote, Burn Heal, Paralyz Heal, Ice Heal, Full Heal) — stops ticking damage and status penalties
2. **HP heal second** (Potion, Super Potion, etc.) — only after status is resolved, to maximize healing efficiency
3. **PP restoration** — only if primary attacking move is out of PP and no Pokemon Center nearby
4. **Revive/Flee** — if a Pokemon faints and you have no Revive, flee from wild battles; if in trainer battle, use a different Pokemon

## Battle Recovery and Dialog Loop Handling

### If Stuck in Dialog Loop
```
## Situation Analysis
[Describe remaining dialog, battle state, and any visible text]

## Recommended Strategy
Press A repeatedly (once per second) until dialog fully closes. Do NOT press B, Start, or Select during dialog — this can skip important text or cause unexpected behavior. If dialog still does not close after 10 presses, reload save state.

## Specific Actions
1. Press A button
2. Wait 0.5-1 second
3. Check if dialog box is still visible on screenshot
4. If yes, repeat steps 1-3
5. If dialog closes, you should see the overworld with player character visible
6. Verify control is restored by checking if menu buttons (Start) work

## Backup Plan
- If pressing A 10+ times does not work, press B once (some dialogs require B to dismiss "item received" prompts)
- If still stuck, reload the save from before the battle/event
- Avoid using `a_until_dialog_end` if it previously failed — use manual A presses instead
```

### If Lead Pokemon is Poisoned/Burned in Overworld
```
## Situation Analysis
[Pokemon species, level, status, current HP, location, steps to safety, items available]

## Recommended Priority
1. Immediately cure status with appropriate item (Antidote for Poison, Burn Heal for Burn)
2. Then heal HP with Potion if HP is below 50%
3. Proceed to nearest Pokemon Center or destination

## Specific Actions
1. Open Bag → select status cure item → use on affected Pokemon
2. After curing, check HP bar
3. If HP is red or yellow, use Potion
4. Walk to destination

## Backup Plan
- If Pokemon faints before curing (e.g., extremely low HP and many steps), switch to another Pokemon and heal the fainted one at the next Pokemon Center
- If you have no status cure, walk to the nearest Pokemon Center immediately, avoiding tall grass to minimize wild encounters
- Consider using a Repel if available and far from safety
```

## Memory Conventions for State Context
```
PKM:STATE | Current Pokemon status conditions, HP levels, and item counts
PKM:NAV | Location, route number, distance to safe zone (Pokemon Center or town exit)
PKM:DIALOG | Dialog status (active, stuck, multi-part)
PKM:ITEMS | Bag inventory of healing items and Pokeballs
```

## Pitfalls to Avoid
- **Do NOT save mid-dialog or mid-battle** — can corrupt save file
- **Do NOT assume a single A press closes multi-screen dialog** — press until overworld appears
- **Do NOT heal HP before curing status** — status damage continues, wasting Potions
- **Do NOT ignore 1/256 miss glitch** — in battle, always have a backup move or plan
- **Do NOT use Focus Energy** (bugged) or rely on Ghost moves vs Psychic (bugged)
- **Do NOT walk through tall grass with a poisoned lead Pokemon** — wild encounters waste more steps and HP

## Examples

### Example: Dialog Stuck After Battle
User input: "A trainer's post-battle dialog is still showing after the battle ended. The `a_until_dialog_end` action returned but dialog is still on screen."

Response:
- Press A repeatedly (up to 10 times) until dialog closes
- If still stuck, press B once to dismiss any lingering prompts
- Reload save if nothing works

### Example: Poisoned Lead Pokemon on Route 3
User input: "Squirtle is poisoned, 15 steps from Mt. Moon, have 1 Antidote and 2 Potions."

Response:
- Use Antidote first to cure poison
- Then use Potion if HP is low
- Walk to Mt. Moon entrance
- Save before entering cave

name: gen1-type-matchup-tutor
description: Teach Gen 1 Pokémon type matchups with full mathematical damage calculations, explicit Gen 1 rule citations, and step-by-step actionable battle advice
---

# Gen 1 Type Matchup Tutor

When the user asks about type matchups, move effectiveness, or battle damage calculations for **Pokémon Red/Blue/Yellow (Gen 1)**, provide an answer that:

1. **Explicitly flags any difference from modern games (Gen 2+)** — always state "In Gen 1, this rule is different from modern games" and explain exactly what changed and when.
2. **Cites the specific Gen 1 rule** from the official type chart, including known bugs (e.g., Ghost vs Psychic immunity bug).
3. **Calculates full effective power** with this explicit formula:
   `Base Power × STAB (1.5x if move type matches Pokémon type) × Type Effectiveness (0x, 0.5x, 1x, 2x, or 4x) = Effective Power`
   - Show each term separately (base power, STAB flag, type multiplier)
   - Account for **secondary typing** on the defender: if the defender has two types, multiply the effectiveness of the attacking move against each type (e.g., Water vs Rock/Ground = 2x × 2x = 4x)
   - For STAB, state whether the attacker's type matches the move's type
4. **Provides a clear, actionable recommendation** — "Use [move name]" and explain why (damage comparison + utility if relevant)
5. **When two moves deal equal effective damage**, prefer the one with **additional utility** (healing from Leech Life/Absorb, status chance, priority, or stat reduction)

## Critical Gen 1 Type Chart Differences (MUST MEMORIZE)

These rules are **unique to Gen 1** and differ from Gen 2+:

| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect (Gen 2+) | Gen 1 Special Notes |
|------------------------------|--------------|------------------------|---------------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) | Changed in Gen 2 |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) | Changed in Gen 2 |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but BUGGED) | 0x (immune) | Gen 1 bug: Psychic is immune to Ghost due to coding error, despite type chart saying SE |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) | 0.5x (NVE) | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |
| Poison → Ground | 1x (neutral) | 0.5x (NVE) | Ground resists Poison starting Gen 2 |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) | Same in both, but in Gen 1 it's due to code |
| Fighting → Ghost | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) | Same in both |
| Ice → Fire | 1x (neutral) | 0.5x (NVE) | Fire resists Ice starting Gen 2 |

## Common Type Duo Matchups in Gen 1

When a Pokémon has two types, calculate **both** multipliers:

**Rock/Ground (e.g., Geodude, Graveler, Golem, Onix):**
- Water → Rock (2x) × Water → Ground (2x) = **4x** — this is the classic 4x weakness
- Grass → Rock (2x) × Grass → Ground (2x) = **4x** — also a double weakness
- Normal → Rock (0.5x) × Normal → Ground (1x) = 0.5x — Tackle is weak
- Fighting → Rock (2x) × Fighting → Ground (1x) = 2x — Fighting is neutral on Ground in Gen 1

**Bug/Poison (e.g., Weedle, Kakuna, Beedrill):**
- Bug → Poison (2x Gen 1 only) × Bug → Bug (1x) = 2x — Bug moves are SE
- Psychic → Poison (1x Gen 1, not resistant) × Psychic → Bug (1x) = 1x — no resistance
- Flying → Bug (2x) × Flying → Poison (1x) = 2x
- Fire → Bug (2x) × Fire → Poison (1x) = 2x

**Water/Flying (e.g., Gyarados):**
- Electric → Water (2x) × Electric → Flying (2x) = **4x** — this is *the* weakness
- Grass → Water (2x) × Grass → Flying (0.5x) = 1x — surprisingly neutral

## How to Frame Strategic Advice

When the user asks "Which move should I use?" or "Is this type matchup correct?":

1. **First sentence:** Direct yes/no answer to the core question
2. **Second paragraph:** Explain the Gen 1 rule difference (if any) with a table or clear comparison
3. **Third section:** Show the damage math with the formula
4. **Fourth section:** Give the actionable recommendation + why (including utility benefits if equal damage)
5. **Optional warning:** Note any PP conservation concerns if relevant (e.g., "Leech Life has low PP — use it for this KO, but conserve for tougher fights")

## Example Output Structure

```
**Short answer:** [Yes/No, and the correct answer]

**Why Gen 1 differs (if applicable):** [Explain the specific rule difference from modern games]

**Damage calculation for [Pokémon A] vs [Pokémon B]:**
| Move | Base Power | Type Effect | STAB? | Effective Power |
|------|-----------|-------------|-------|-----------------|
| Move A (Type) | BP × | SE/NVE ×1.5/0.5× | Yes/No ×1.5/×1 | = **total** |
| Move B (Type) | BP × | SE/NVE ×1.5/0.5× | Yes/No ×1.5/×1 | = **total** |

**Recommendation:** Use [Move A/B] because [damage advantage + utility reason]. [Optional: PP conservation note]
```

## Always Include These Warnings When Relevant

- "**Important:** This answer applies to Gen 1 Pokémon Red/Blue/Yellow **only**. In Gen 2+, this matchup is different."
- If the user says they're playing a Gen 3+ game (FireRed/LeafGreen/Emerald/etc.), **use the modern type chart** and state: "Since you're playing [Game], this uses the modern Gen 3+ type chart, not the Gen 1 chart."
- For Ghost vs Psychic in Gen 1, always note: "Despite the type chart showing Ghost as SE against Psychic, a programming bug makes Psychic immune to Ghost moves in Gen 1. Do not use Ghost moves."
