name: pokemon-player-v2
description: Play Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow via headless emulator and RAM reads — optimized for spatial reasoning and warp handling
---

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (key matchups)
- Water beats Fire, Ground, Rock
- Fire beats Grass, Bug, Ice
- Grass beats Water, Ground, Rock
- Electric beats Water, Flying
- Ground beats Fire, Electric, Rock, Poison
- Psychic beats Fighting, Poison (dominant in Gen 1!)

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

### Stale Dialog Recovery
When a_until_dialog_end returns but dialog is still visually present:
1. The RAM dialog flag may have cleared prematurely while text was still scrolling or a partial text box remained.
2. **Immediately take a screenshot** to visually confirm the exact state: scrolling text, a completed text box, or a yes/no prompt.
3. **Use the hold_b_120 + press_a pattern** — this holds B for 2 seconds (speeds through remaining text scrolling) then presses A to advance.
4. **Send this sequence 2-3 times** repeatedly. Each hold_b_120 gets through slow-scrolling text segments, and press_a confirms the next chunk.
5. **After each 2-second cycle, take another screenshot** to verify dialog is fully cleared.
6. **If a yes/no prompt appears**, press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no".
7. **Once screenshot shows the overworld with no text box**, proceed with normal gameplay.
8. **Record the incident**: PKM:STUCK Post-battle/trade dialog at [location] — used hold_b_120 pattern to clear (a_until_dialog_end failed due to RAM unreliability).

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock) → use Water/Grass
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four — Champion!

## Key Item and HM Locations (Game Knowledge Reference)
- **HM01 Cut** — Required to progress past the Cerulean City cuttable tree. Obtain from the captain of the S.S. Anne (reward for helping him).
- **HM02 Fly** — Found in the Pokemon Mansion on Cinnabar Island. Requires Surf to access.
- **HM03 Surf** — Obtainable by:
  - Getting Gold Teeth in Safari Zone Area 3 (secret house), then trading them to the Safari Zone entrance building man.
  - OR defeating Koga (Fuchsia Gym Leader) — his assistant outside gives you HM03 Surf as a reward.
- **HM04 Strength** — Found in the Safari Zone (Area 2, hidden item). Requires Surf.
- **HM05 Flash** — Obtainable from Professor Oak's aide (after catching 10 Pokemon) on Route 2.
- **Poke Flute** — Awakens Snorlax blocking paths. Obtain from Mr. Fuji in Lavender Town after clearing Pokemon Tower.
- **Bicycle** — Obtainable from the Bike Shop in Cerulean City for 1,000,000 Pokedollars OR by showing the Bike Voucher (won at the Game Corner).
- **S.S. Ticket** — Receive from professor's aide in Cerulean City after earning Cascade Badge.

## Catching and Surfing Mechanics
- **Catching Pokemon**: Weaken HP (ideally red), inflict status (Sleep/Para best), throw Poke Ball. Great Balls/Ultra Balls improve catch rate.
- **Surfing**: Once Blastoise or another compatible Pokemon learns Surf, press A while facing a body of water to ride Surf. HM moves (Surf, Cut, Fly, etc.) can be taught to any compatible Pokemon and used outside battle without consuming PP.
- **STAB Bonus**: Same Type Attack Bonus — moves matching the user's type deal 1.5x damage. Example: Water-type Blastoise using Surf gets STAB.
- **Move Replacement**: If a Pokemon knows 4 moves and you teach a new move, you must forget one. Typical safe moves to drop: Tackle, Tail Whip, Growl, Leer. Keep STAB and coverage moves.

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- The a_until_dialog_end action can fail to clear text if RAM flag clears before visual text finishes — always use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern as fallback and verify via screenshot

### Loading on server startup

This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (CRITICAL — differs from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference this when giving type matchup advice for Gen 1 games. Modern type charts (Gen 2+) are DIFFERENT.**

#### Super-effective relationships in Gen 1 ONLY:
- **Bug is super-effective against Poison** (2x, removed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison is super-effective against Bug** (2x, removed in Gen 2+)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Psychic** (2x in chart, but Gen 1 has a bug where Psychic is immune to Ghost)
- **Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1** (Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2)
- **Psychic is immune to Ghost in Gen 1** (due to programming bug, despite Ghost being SE against Psychic on the type chart)
- **Normal and Fighting are immune to Ghost** (Ghost moves do NOT affect Normal types; Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types)

#### Key Gen 1 type chart for common matchups:
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but bugged → 0x) | 0x (immune) |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Ground → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fighting → Normal | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Normal → Rock | 0.5x (NVE) | 0.5x (NVE, same) |
| Electric → Ground | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) — Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1 | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Psychic → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Ice → Fire | 1x (neutral) — Ice is NOT NVE on Fire | 0.5x (NVE, changed in Gen 2+) |
| Ice → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |

#### Move Damage Calculation Template (MUST follow for ALL damage comparisons)
When comparing moves, ALWAYS show your math explicitly in this format:

| Move | Base Power | Type Effectiveness (Gen 1) | STAB? (1.5x if same type as user, otherwise 1x) | Effective Power |
|------|-----------|---------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|-----------------|
| [Move Name] (Type) | [BP] | [0x/0.5x/1x/2x/4x] | [Yes=1.5x, No=1x, Note type of Pokemon vs move type] | [BP × effectiveness × STAB] = **total** |

Key rules:
- STAB (Same Type Attack Bonus) = 1.5x multiplier if the move's type matches ANY of the Pokemon's types
- If the Pokemon has two types, it gets STAB if either type matches the move type (e.g., Paras is Bug/Grass → gets STAB on Bug and Grass moves, but NOT on Normal moves)
- Type effectiveness is multiplicative: if the target has two types, multiply the effectiveness against each type (e.g., Rock/Ground vs Water = 2x × 2x = 4x)
- **Always mention utility** of moves when effective damage is equal or close — e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has)
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged, use Dark-type bites early or just overpower with physical)
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)
- **When answering Gen 1 game mechanic questions, always explicitly state if a mechanic differs from modern games, and cite the specific Gen 1 rule** — do not just give the answer without contextualizing why it's different
- **When the user asks for a step-by-step plan to obtain an item or HM, include: exact location in the overworld, any prerequisite badges or items needed, precise menu navigation (which pocket, which button presses), and what to do if the player doesn't have a compatible Pokemon**
- **When comparing move damage, calculate the full effective power including STAB (1.5x), type effectiveness (0x, 0.5x, 1x, 2x, or 4x in Gen 1), and note if the defending Pokemon's secondary type affects the calculation** — show your math explicitly using the Move Damage Calculation Template
- **When the user challenges a Gen 1 mechanic based on knowledge from a later generation, ALWAYS correct them and explicitly cite the Gen 1 rule that differs** — do not just agree or provide a vague answer
- **STAB (Same Type Attack Bonus):** A Pokemon gets STAB (1.5x) on a move if the move's type matches ANY of its types. For dual-type Pokemon, check both types. Never assume a Normal-type move gets STAB unless the Pokemon is Normal-type.

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks strategic questions about Gen 1 mechanics or gameplay decisions

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot

- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center

Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

## CRITICAL: Dialog/Text Desynchronization Recovery (MUST FOLLOW)

### Root Cause
The `a_until_dialog_end` action relies on the RAM dialog flag (polling memory address [0xC6A0] or equivalent). However, this flag is unreliable for:
- **Scrolling text that is still animating** — the RAM flag can clear momentarily before the text finishes scrolling, causing a false "dialog done" return
- **Long post-battle speeches** — especially trainer defeat speeches that span multiple text boxes
- **Partial text boxes** — e.g., text that appears character-by-character
- **Yes/no prompts** — the RAM flag may not distinguish between text and prompt states
- **Nickname entry screens** — RAM flag can behave unexpectedly

### Recovery Protocol (EXACT ORDER — when `a_until_dialog_end` returned but screenshot still shows text)
1. **Send `hold_b_120`** — hold B for ~2 seconds (60 frames ≈ 1 second, so 120 frames ≈ 2 seconds). This accelerates remaining text scroll speed in Gen 1.
2. **Immediately send `press_a`** — advances to the next text box or closes the dialog.
3. **Take a screenshot** — visually confirm if dialog is fully cleared.
4. **If text is still visible on screen:** repeat `hold_b_120` + `press_a` again (up to 3-4 cycles).
5. **Once screenshot shows no dialog box:** call `GET /state` to confirm we're out of battle mode and free to move.
6. **Record the event in memory:** `PKM:PROGRESS - dialog desync recovered via B+A speed-through`

### Prevention Going Forward
- **After any battle, do NOT rely solely on `a_until_dialog_end`** for long text sequences (trainer speeches, story text, etc.)
- Instead, use manual sequence: `hold_b_120` + `press_a` x2-3, then screenshot check
- **Treat `a_until_dialog_end` as a FIRST ATTEMPT only** — always follow up with a visual screenshot check
- If dialog is still present after the recovery cycle, the game may be stuck in a menu (like a yes/no prompt) — use `press_b` to back out, then screenshot again

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (CRITICAL — differs from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference this when giving type matchup advice for Gen 1 games. Modern type charts (Gen 2+) are DIFFERENT.**

#### Super-effective relationships in Gen 1 ONLY:
- **Bug is super-effective against Poison** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison is super-effective against Bug** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Psychic** (removed in Gen 2+, but Gen 1 has a bug where Psychic is immune to Ghost)
- **Ice is NOT very effective against Fire** (wait, actually it is — Ice is SE against Grass, Ground, Flying, Dragon)
- **Poison resists Bug in Gen 1** (no, actually Poison does NOT resist Bug in Gen 1 — Poison resists Bug starting Gen 2)
- **Psychic is immune to Ghost in Gen 1** (due to programming bug, despite Ghost being SE against Psychic on the type chart)
- **Normal and Fighting are immune to Ghost** (Ghost moves do NOT affect Normal types; Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types)

#### Key Gen 1 type chart for common matchups:
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but bugged) | 0x (immune) |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| Ground → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fighting → Normal | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Normal → Rock | 0.5x (NVE) | 0.5x (NVE, same) |
| Electric → Ground | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) — Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1 | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |
| Psychic → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Electric → Water/Psychic (Starmie) | 2x (Water weak to Electric, Psychic neutral to Electric = still 2x total) | Same |
| Grass → Starmie | 2x (Water weak to Grass, Psychic does NOT resist Grass in Gen 1 — that was added Gen 2+) | Psychic resists Grass starting Gen 6? Actually, Psychic resists nothing in Gen 1 — Grass is 2x against Water/Psychic |

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

#### Move Math for Common Dungeon Encounters:
| Encounter | Type(s) | Tackle effectiveness | Water Gun effectiveness | Best Move to Use |
|-----------|---------|---------------------|------------------------|------------------|
| Zubat | Poison/Flying | 1x (Normal → Poison/Flying is neutral) | 1x (Water → Poison/Flying is neutral) | Tackle (preserve PP) |
| Geodude | Rock/Ground | 0.5x (Normal → Rock is NVE) | **4x** (Water SE vs Rock × Water SE vs Ground) | Water Gun only if ace/emergency |
| Paras | Bug/Grass | 1x (Normal is neutral) | **0.5x** (Water → Grass is NVE) | Tackle |
| Clefairy | Normal | 1x (Normal → Normal is neutral) | 1x (Water → Normal is neutral) | Tackle |

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has)
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged, use Dark-type bites early or just overpower with physical)
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually; the `a_until_dialog_end` action may return false-positive "done" during scrolling text (especially long post-battle speeches). Always follow up with visual verification. If dialog is still present, use `hold_b_120` + `press_a` manually to speed through remaining text.
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal. Show explicit move math for common dungeon encounters (Zubat, Geodude, Paras, Clefairy in Mt. Moon)
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)
- **When answering Gen 1 game mechanic questions, always explicitly state if a mechanic differs from modern games, and cite the specific Gen 1 rule** — do not just give the answer without contextualizing why it's different. For type matchups, always compare Gen 1 vs modern explicitly in a table where relevant
- **When the user asks for a step-by-step plan to obtain an item or HM, include: exact location in the overworld, any prerequisite badges or items needed, precise menu navigation (which pocket, which button presses), and what to do if the player doesn't have a compatible Pokemon**
- **When comparing move damage, calculate the full effective power including STAB (1.5x), type effectiveness (0x, 0.5x, 1x, 2x, or 4x in Gen 1), and note if the defending Pokemon's secondary type affects the calculation** — show your math explicitly
- **When giving gym prep advice, always specify the gym leader's exact team composition (Pokemon, levels, types), the move set of key threats (e.g., Starmie knows Recover), and Gen 1 specific type interactions** — e.g., Grass is 2x against Water/Psychic Starmie because Psychic does NOT resist Grass in Gen 1 (that resistance was added in Gen 6+)
- **If you receive a low score on a trajectory, review which specific Pitfall or protocol you may have missed** — common errors include: not providing explicit move math tables, not mentioning Gen 1 vs modern differences, and not giving step-by-step actionable plans

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks for game knowledge or game logic explanations (e.g., how to obtain an item, where to find a Pokemon, what to do in a specific situation)

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about
- Before executing any complex sequence (e.g., teaching an HM, using a rare item)

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut, before_teaching_surf

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (key matchups)
- Water beats Fire, Ground, Rock
- Fire beats Grass, Bug, Ice
- Grass beats Water, Ground, Rock
- Electric beats Water, Flying
- Ground beats Fire, Electric, Rock, Poison
- Psychic beats Fighting, Poison (dominant in Gen 1!)

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Game Knowledge Queries (NEW)

When the user asks a game knowledge question (e.g., "How do I get Surf?", "What Pokemon is good against Misty?", "Where is HM03?"), treat it as a PRIORITY over gameplay execution. Follow these rules:

### Step 1: Identify query type
- **Item/Obtainable query** — "How do I get [item/Pokemon/HM]?"
- **Location query** — "Where is [location/NPC/object]?"
- **Strategy query** — "What should I do about [boss/gym/status condition]?"
- **Game logic query** — "What happens when [action/event]?"

### Step 2: Provide clear, structured answer using game knowledge
- Always reference the current location if known (from memory or /state)
- Use the memory prefix PKM: for any new information that should be stored
- If the query involves an HM or key item, mention required progress (badges, items, NPCs)
- If teaching a move, mention the move limit (4 moves max, what to overwrite)

### Step 3: Offer to execute
- End the knowledge answer with: "Would you like me to actually execute this in the game? If so, say 'play pokemon' and I'll start the emulator and guide [player] through this!"

### Specific Game Knowledge Facts (for Pokemon Red/Blue):

#### HM Surf Locations:
- **Primary**: Safari Zone entrance building (Fuchsia City) — requires Gold Teeth found in Safari Zone Area 3
- **Alternative**: Defeat Koga (Fuchsia Gym Leader), then his assistant outside gives HM03
- **Teaching**: Select HM03 from Key Items pocket in bag, choose "Use", select compatible Pokemon (Water-type starters, many Water-types)

#### HM Cut Location:
- Route 25 (east of Cerulean City) — found by the river, requires walking through the route past the NPCs

#### Status Condition Healing:
- **Poison**: Use Antidote from bag, OR visit Pokemon Center (cures all status)
- **Overworld poison damage**: Ticks HP every step. Heal IMMEDIATELY before walking any distance
- **Priority**: Using an Antidote from bag is faster than walking to Pokemon Center if far away

#### Badge Progression Milestones:
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock) → use Water/Grass
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying

- Elite Four → Champion!

When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy — Gen 1 Specific Rules (CRITICAL)

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart — UNIQUE RULES (different from modern games)
The following are Gen 1 exclusive type mechanics. Users may give incorrect advice based on modern games. ALWAYS CORRECT them using these rules:

**Bug-type moves ARE super-effective against Poison-type in Gen 1.**
- This was removed starting Gen 2 (Gold/Silver).
- In Gen 1, Bug moves deal 2x damage to Poison types.
- Poison does NOT resist Bug in Gen 1.
- Example: A player might say "Bug moves are weak against Poison" — that is FALSE for Red/Blue.

**Ghost vs Psychic in Gen 1:**
- Ghost-type moves are NOT super-effective against Psychic in Gen 1 (glitch: intended immunity, actual code makes them ineffective).
- The only Ghost-type damaging move is Lick (20 base power) — never rely on it.

**Other Gen 1 unique type interactions:**
- Ice is super-effective against Fire in Gen 1 (removed Gen 2+).
- Normal and Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types in Gen 1 (Fighting has no effect on any Ghost; Normal has no effect).
- Poison is super-effective against Bug in Gen 1 (removed Gen 2+).

**Full Gen 1 Type Chart Reference:**
| Attacking Type | Super Effective vs | Not Very Effective vs | No Effect vs |
|---------------|-------------------|----------------------|-------------|
| Bug | Poison, Grass, Psychic | Fire, Fighting, Flying, Ghost*, Poison** | None |
| Grass | Water, Rock, Ground | Fire, Bug, Poison, Flying, Dragon | None |
| Water | Fire, Ground, Rock | Grass, Dragon | None |
| Fire | Grass, Bug, Ice, Rock | Water, Rock, Dragon | None |
| Electric | Water, Flying, Dragon | Grass, Ground | Ground |
| Psychic | Fighting, Poison | Psychic | Ghost* |
| Ground | Fire, Electric, Rock, Poison | Bug, Grass | Flying |
| Fighting | Normal, Ice, Rock | Poison, Bug, Flying | Ghost |
| Normal | None | Rock, Ghost | Ghost |
| Ghost | Ghost, Psychic* | None | Normal |
| *= Gen 1 specific quirks; **= Gen 1 Bug moves ARE SE vs Poison, but Poison is ALSO SE vs Bug — both are true |

When a user gives type advice that contradicts these Gen 1 rules, politely correct them and stick to the Gen 1 chart.

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Effective Damage Calculation (for move choice)
Calculate effective damage as: Base Power × Type Effectiveness Multiplier
- Super effective (2x) or (4x for double weakness) vs (1x for neutral) vs (0.5x) vs (0x immune)

If two moves have the same effective power, prioritize:
1. STAB (Same Type Attack Bonus — 1.5x in Gen 1)
2. Secondary effects (healing, stat drops)
3. PP remaining

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock) → use Water/Grass
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **GEN 1 TYPE RULES TRUMP MODERN TYPE RULES** — If a user gives type advice based on games after Gen 2, politely correct them with the Gen 1 specific rule and document it in memory as PKM:GEN1_FACT
- When a move has equal effective power to another, always check for secondary effects (healing, status) before choosing
- Effective power = base power × type multiplier (round down in Gen 1)

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks strategic questions about Gen 1 mechanics or gameplay decisions
- User asks about specific move damage calculations, type matchups, or location-based navigation
- User asks for step-by-step plans to obtain items/HMs or complete objectives

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)

6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (CRITICAL — differs from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference this when giving type matchup advice for Gen 1 games. Modern type charts (Gen 2+) are DIFFERENT.**

#### Super-effective relationships in Gen 1 ONLY:
- **Bug is super-effective against Poison** (2x, removed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison is super-effective against Bug** (2x, removed in Gen 2+)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Psychic** (2x in chart, but Gen 1 has a bug where Psychic is immune to Ghost)
- **Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1** (Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2)
- **Psychic is immune to Ghost in Gen 1** (due to programming bug, despite Ghost being SE against Psychic on the type chart)
- **Normal and Fighting are immune to Ghost** (Ghost moves do NOT affect Normal types; Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types)

#### Key Gen 1 type chart for common matchups:
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but bugged → 0x) | 0x (immune) |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Ground → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fighting → Normal | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Normal → Rock | 0.5x (NVE) | 0.5x (NVE, same) |
| Electric → Ground | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) — Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1 | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Psychic → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Ice → Fire | 1x (neutral) — Ice is NOT NVE on Fire | 0.5x (NVE, changed in Gen 2+) |
| Ice → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |

#### Move Damage Calculation Template (MUST follow for ALL damage comparisons)
When comparing moves, ALWAYS show your math explicitly in this format:

| Move | Base Power | Type Effectiveness (Gen 1) | STAB? (1.5x if same type as user, otherwise 1x) | Effective Power |
|------|-----------|---------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|-----------------|
| [Move Name] (Type) | [BP] | [0x/0.5x/1x/2x/4x] | [Yes=1.5x, No=1x, Note type of Pokemon vs move type] | [BP × effectiveness × STAB] = **total** |

Key rules:
- STAB (Same Type Attack Bonus) = 1.5x multiplier if the move's type matches ANY of the Pokemon's types
- If the Pokemon has two types, it gets STAB if either type matches the move type (e.g., Paras is Bug/Grass → gets STAB on Bug and Grass moves, but NOT on Normal moves)
- Type effectiveness is multiplicative: if the target has two types, multiply the effectiveness against each type (e.g., Rock/Ground vs Water = 2x × 2x = 4x)
- **Always mention utility** of moves when effective damage is equal or close — e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up

2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing

- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)
- **When answering Gen 1 game mechanic questions, always explicitly state if a mechanic differs from modern games, and cite the specific Gen 1 rule** — do not just give the answer without contextualizing why it's different
- **When the user asks for a step-by-step plan to obtain an item or HM, include: exact location in the overworld, any prerequisite badges or items needed, precise menu navigation (which pocket, which button presses), and what to do if the player doesn't have a compatible Pokemon**
- **When comparing move damage, calculate the full effective power including STAB (1.5x), type effectiveness (0x, 0.5x, 1x, 2x, or 4x in Gen 1), and note if the defending Pokemon's secondary type affects the calculation** — show your math explicitly using the Move Damage Calculation Template
- **When the user challenges a Gen 1 mechanic based on knowledge from a later generation, ALWAYS correct them and explicitly cite the Gen 1 rule that differs** — do not just agree or provide a vague answer
- **STAB (Same Type Attack Bonus):** A Pokemon gets STAB (1.5x) on a move if the move's type matches ANY of its types. For dual-type Pokemon, check both types. Never assume a Normal-type move gets STAB unless the Pokemon is Normal-type.
- **When a user reports being stuck at a specific obstacle (e.g., a ledge) and has already attempted the obvious solution multiple times (e.g., walking up from different positions), do NOT simply re-list the protocol steps generically. Instead, immediately infer the correct next action based on the obstacle geometry typical for that location in Gen 1. For ledges south of Pewter City, the gap is always on the east side — instruct the user to walk_right to find it.** This saves turns and demonstrates Gen 1 route knowledge. Always pair this with a request for visual confirmation but state the high-probability solution first.
