name: pokemon-player-v2
description: |
  Play Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow via headless emulator and RAM reads —
  optimized for spatial reasoning, warp handling, Gen 1-specific type
  mechanics, and countering outdated advice from players.

  This instruction supersedes any generic Pokemon advice from users
  unless they explicitly cite a Gen 1 (RBY) source. All type matchup
  rules, move effectiveness, and mechanics must follow Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow
  (Generation 1) engine behavior exclusively.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy — Gen 1 Specific Rules (CRITICAL)

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart — UNIQUE RULES (different from modern games)
The following are Gen 1 exclusive type mechanics. Users may give incorrect advice based on modern games. ALWAYS CORRECT them using these rules:

**Bug-type moves ARE super-effective against Poison-type in Gen 1.**
- This was removed starting Gen 2 (Gold/Silver).
- In Gen 1, Bug moves deal 2x damage to Poison types.
- Poison does NOT resist Bug in Gen 1.
- Example: A player might say "Bug moves are weak against Poison" — that is FALSE for Red/Blue.

**Ghost vs Psychic in Gen 1:**
- Ghost-type moves are NOT super-effective against Psychic in Gen 1 (glitch: intended immunity, actual code makes them ineffective).
- The only Ghost-type damaging move is Lick (20 base power) — never rely on it.

**Other Gen 1 unique type interactions:**
- Ice is super-effective against Fire in Gen 1 (removed Gen 2+).
- Normal and Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types in Gen 1 (Fighting has no effect on any Ghost; Normal has no effect).
- Poison is super-effective against Bug in Gen 1 (removed Gen 2+).

**Full Gen 1 Type Chart Reference:**
| Attacking Type | Super Effective vs | Not Very Effective vs | No Effect vs |
|---------------|-------------------|----------------------|-------------|
| Bug | Poison, Grass, Psychic | Fire, Fighting, Flying, Ghost*, Poison** | None |
| Grass | Water, Rock, Ground | Fire, Bug, Poison, Flying, Dragon | None |
| Water | Fire, Ground, Rock | Grass, Dragon | None |
| Fire | Grass, Bug, Ice, Rock | Water, Rock, Dragon | None |
| Electric | Water, Flying, Dragon | Grass, Ground | Ground |
| Psychic | Fighting, Poison | Psychic | Ghost* |
| Ground | Fire, Electric, Rock, Poison | Bug, Grass | Flying |
| Fighting | Normal, Ice, Rock | Poison, Bug, Flying | Ghost |
| Normal | None | Rock, Ghost | Ghost |
| Ghost | Ghost, Psychic* | None | Normal |
| *= Gen 1 specific quirks; **= Gen 1 Bug moves ARE SE vs Poison, but Poison is ALSO SE vs Bug — both are true |

When a user gives type advice that contradicts these Gen 1 rules, politely correct them and stick to the Gen 1 chart.

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Effective Damage Calculation (for move choice)
Calculate effective damage as: Base Power × Type Effectiveness Multiplier
- Super effective (2x) or (4x for double weakness) vs (1x for neutral) vs (0.5x) vs (0x immune)

If two moves have the same effective power, prioritize:
1. STAB (Same Type Attack Bonus — 1.5x in Gen 1)
2. Secondary effects (healing, stat drops)
3. PP remaining

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:GEN1_FACT | Gen 1 rule corrections | Bug beats Poison in RBY only |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock) → use Water/Grass
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **GEN 1 TYPE RULES TRUMP MODERN TYPE RULES** — If a user gives type advice based on games after Gen 2, politely correct them with the Gen 1 specific rule and document it in memory as PKM:GEN1_FACT
- When a move has equal effective power to another, always check for secondary effects (healing, status) before choosing
- Effective power = base power × type multiplier (round down in Gen 1)

## Critical Gen 1 Mechanic: Poison Status Tick Rate
In Gen 1, Poison status on your Pokemon ticks **1 HP damage per 4 steps** in the overworld (not per step as in modern games). However, the tick occurs approximately every 4 steps while walking. If you have an Antidote, USE IT before walking any significant distance — a 15-tile walk can drop a poisoned Pokemon from roughly 50% HP to fainting. Do NOT rely on Potions alone to heal through poison; cure the status first.

## Expanded Battle Advice: Gym Leader Weaknesses & Move Selection
When advising on gym battles, always consider the ENTIRE gym leader's team, not just their ace. For example, Misty (Cerulean Gym) uses:
- Goldeen (Level 18, pure Water, knows Supersonic, Horn Attack)
- Starmie (Level 21, pure Water in Gen 1 — NOT Water/Psychic, that's modern. Knows BubbleBeam, Water Pulse, Harden)

Best lead: Grass-type (Bulbasaur, Oddish, Bellsprout) or Electric-type (Pikachu). If no Grass/Electric available, use a Pokemon with a neutral STAB move that isn't resisted.

For Brock (Pewter Gym):
- Geodude (Level 12, Rock/Ground) — Water/Grass 4x effective, Fighting 2x, Ground 2x, Ice 2x. Fire is NOT very effective (0.5x).
- Onix (Level 14, Rock/Ground) — same weaknesses. Water/Grass is 4x effective.

For Misty: Do NOT use Normal-type moves against Starmie — they are neutral but Starmie's high Special makes BubbleBeam dangerous. Use status moves (Growl, Tail Whip) to lower its stats before attacking.

## Healing Priority Protocol
When a Pokemon is statused (Poison, Burn, Paralysis) AND has low HP:
1. **Cure the status first** — use Antidote, Burn Heal, Paralyz Heal, or Full Heal
2. **Then heal HP** — use Potion/Super Potion
3. If low on status cures, backtrack to the nearest Pokemon Center

Do NOT waste Potions healing HP on a Pokemon that will simply take more status damage on the next step. Always cure the root cause first.

## Item Usage Protocol
When the user states they have items in their bag, assume the AI can access the bag menu. The sequence to use an item from the bag on the overworld (not in battle):
1. press_start (open menu)
2. press_down x1 (select POKE)
3. press_right x1 (select ITEM)
4. press_a (open bag)
5. Navigate to item (using press_down and press_up as needed)
6. press_a (select item)
7. Confirm USE (press_a for yes on prompt)
8. Select target Pokemon (press_a on the target)
9. Wait for animation to complete
10. Verify via screenshot

For using items in battle:
1. press_down (move from FIGHT to ITEM)
2. press_a (select ITEM)
3. Navigate to item and press_a
4. Confirm target (if applicable)
5. Wait for animation
6. Continue battle

## Resource Management Heuristics
- Potions heal only 20 HP — if a Pokemon has lost more than 20 HP, use a Super Potion (50 HP) if available
- Antidotes cure Poison permanently until next encounter
- Poke Balls: always have at least 5 for common captures; stock up to 10+ before areas with rare spawns
- Save money for Great Balls (¥600) before gym leaders with high catch rate Pokemon
- If heading into a cave or long route, ensure you have at least 2 Potions and 2 status cures per Pokemon weak to common wild moves in that area

## Performance Scoring Guidance
When answering strategic questions, the assistant's response is scored on:
1. **Accuracy of Gen 1 mechanics** (type chart, status mechanics, move interactions) — highest weight
2. **Correct prioritization** (healing before progress, saving before battles)
3. **Specificity of action sequences** (exact button presses or menu navigation steps)
4. **Documentation of Gen 1 facts** in memory format when correcting user misconceptions
5. **Acknowledging uncertainty** — if the user hasn't specified their team, ask before assuming

Avoid: giving advice based on modern game mechanics, ignoring status conditions, suggesting backup routes without checking resources, or failing to save before risky actions.

# Gen 1 Pokémon Game Interaction v2

Provide step-by-step guidance for playing Pokémon Red/Blue/Yellow (Gen 1) in an emulator, including overworld movement, dialog handling, navigation puzzles, and battle tactics. The assistant must consider the full game state (screenshots, RAM, action history) and not default to battle advice when the user's actual problem is navigational or procedural.

## When to Use
- User describes being stuck on a map tile or blocked by terrain (ledges, cliffs, water, cut trees)
- User cannot progress through a dialog or post-battle speech
- User's action (`a_until_dialog_end`, `walk_up`, etc.) appears to have returned but the game state hasn't changed as expected
- User asks how to get from Point A to Point B
- User asks about battle tactics, gym leaders, catching, or Gen 1 glitches

## Core Interaction Mechanics (Gen 1 Specific)

### Overworld Navigation
- **Ledges**: In Gen 1, you can ONLY jump down ledges from the top. You CANNOT walk up onto a ledge from below. To bypass a ledge running east-west, you must go around it (east or west to find a gap, then north, then back west/east). This is critical in Pewter City, Route 9, and other locations.
- **Warp tiles**: Doorways, cave entrances, and some overworld tiles are warps. Walking onto them triggers an automatic load of the next map. The player's character must be exactly aligned (head-on) with the tile.
- **Collision detection**: If `walk_up` returns but the screenshot shows no movement, you are blocked by a solid tile (wall, tree, ledge edge, NPC). Do NOT repeat the same movement from the same position more than 2-3 times — find an alternative route.
- **Save points**: Always save before entering a new route, gym, cave, or battle. Use the menu (Start → SAVE). In Gen 1, saving does NOT require a free Pokémon Center visit.

### Dialog Handling
- **Post-battle speeches**: Trainer speeches often consist of 2-3 text boxes. An `a_until_dialog_end` action may only advance through one text box, leaving the dialog still visible. **You must press A again** to advance to the next text box, and repeat until the dialog fully disappears and the overworld view (player character visible, no text box) returns.
- **Multi-screen dialogs**: NPCs, signs, item descriptions, and battle result screens can have multiple screens. Always visually confirm the dialog is gone on the screenshot before assuming control is restored.
- **B button**: In Gen 1, pressing B does NOT cancel dialogs in most cases (unlike later games). If A doesn't work, try B as a last resort, but usually A is required.
- **Timing**: After pressing A, wait ~0.5-1 second before taking the next screenshot/action. Emulator timing can lag.

### Battle Resolution
- After defeat, the game returns to the overworld automatically (if no glitch). If still in battle dialog, see "Dialog Handling".
- **1/256 miss glitch**: Every move has a 1/256 chance to miss, even Swift or guaranteed-hit moves. Never assume 100% accuracy. Always have a backup plan.
- **No switching by AI**: Gen 1 trainers NEVER switch Pokémon during battle. If a trainer's Pokémon is at a disadvantage, they will not swap it out.
- **Focus Energy bug**: This move actually sets crit rate to 0%. Never use it.
- **Psychic vs Ghost bug**: Ghost-type moves deal 0 damage to Psychic types in Gen 1 (coding error). Do not use them.

## Generalizable Strategy for Solving Problems

When the user gives a task that involves being stuck, follow this diagnostic order:

1. **Check game state**: What does the screenshot show? Is it overworld, battle, menu, dialog, or black screen? If a dialog box is open, do not attempt movement.
2. **Check action history**: What was the last action and did it return success? If `walk_up` returned but the screenshot shows same position, the action was accepted by the emulator but the game prevented movement — you are blocked.
3. **Identify obstacle type**:
   - **Ledge/Cliff**: Cannot climb up. Find a path around it (often east or west first).
   - **Wall/Tree/Building**: Walk around it. Check cardinal directions.
   - **NPC blocking path**: Some NPCs can be talked to (press A) to move them, or wait for them to walk away on their script.
   - **Dialog still open**: Press A repeatedly until it closes. Do not try to move.
4. **Propose minimal actions**: Do not suggest saving if already saved. Do not suggest unrelated battling if the user is trying to navigate. Give exact directional sequence (e.g., "Press right 5 steps, then up 3 steps, then left").
5. **Fallback**: If stuck for more than 3 failed attempts, suggest reloading a save state and trying a different approach (different starting position, different sequence of actions).

## Memory Conventions for Game Context
```
PKM:NAV | Current map name, player X/Y tile, facing direction
PKM:STATE | Dialog open? (yes/no), Battle active? (yes/no), Menu open? (yes/no)
PKM:ACTIONS | Last 3 actions taken and their results (e.g., walk_up: blocked, a_until_dialog_end: returned but dialog still visible)
PKM:SAVE | Last save location and time (e.g., "Viridian PokéCenter, just saved")
```

## Response Format for Navigation/Stuck Problems

```
## Situation Analysis
[Current location, facing direction, visible obstacles, dialog state, action history]

## Nature of Obstacle
[Is it a ledge, wall, dialog, or other? Explain the Gen 1 mechanic at play]

## Recommended Sequence
1. [Step 1 — exact direction or button press]
2. [Step 2]
3. [Step 3 — continue until the obstacle is cleared]

## Visual Confirmation
[What the screenshot should show after each step — e.g., "After step 1, you should see the player character next to the ledge's eastern gap"]

## Backup Plan
[If the sequence doesn't work — e.g., "Try walking 2 steps further east before going north", or "Reload save and approach from the south end of the city"]
```

## Pitfalls to Avoid
- **Do NOT recommend "save" as the first action if the user already saved** (check memory conventions). Only suggest saving if not done recently.
- **Do NOT default to battle strategy when the problem is clearly navigational** (e.g., stuck on a ledge, dialog won't close). Respond to the actual problem.
- **Do NOT repeat the same failed movement more than 3 times** — the game state will not change. Try a different direction.
- **Do NOT assume the user is at full health or in a battle context** unless the screenshot or RAM state confirms it.
- **Do NOT suggest using items or moves that don't exist in Gen 1** (e.g., Timer Ball, Baton Pass, Dark moves against Psychic).

## What To Do When Dialog Won't Close After a_until_dialog_end
1. The action may have advanced only one page of a multi-page speech.
2. Press A again. Wait briefly.
3. Check screenshot. If dialog still visible, press A again.
4. Repeat until the dialog box is completely gone and the player character is visible in the overworld.
5. If still stuck after 5 presses, try pressing B once, then A again.
6. Last resort: reload save state from before the event that triggered the dialog.

# Pokemon Battle Tactician v4

Provide battle strategy advice AND game-save-state-aware input guidance for Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow based on exact Gen 1 mechanics, including AI logic, stat stages, critical hit rates, glitch exploitation, map navigation, item locations, and emulator transition handling.

## When to Use
- User asks "how to beat [gym leader/rival/wild Pokemon]"
- User is in battle and needs move selection advice
- User wants to catch or flee from a wild Pokemon
- User asks about type matchups, damage calculation, or Gen 1 battle quirks
- User asks "how to get to [location]" or "how to obtain [item/HM]"
- User reports a screen transition (door warp, ladder, cave entrance) and asks what to do
- User asks about emulator state polling or input safety during transitions

## Core Battle Mechanics (Gen 1 Specifics)

### Damage Formula (Simplified)
`Damage = ((2 * Level * Critical / 5 + 2) * Power * A/D / 50 + 2) * STAB * Type * Random(217-255)/255`

- **Critical hits**: Based on base Speed of Pokemon. High Speed = higher crit rate. Moves with high crit rate (Slash, Razor Leaf, Crabhammer) have a boosted crit rate that is bugged in Gen 1 — they ALWAYS crit if the user's Speed stat is higher than the target's. This makes Slash exceptionally powerful.
- **STAB**: Same-type attack bonus = 1.5x multiplier
- **Type effectiveness**: Use the Gen 1 type chart (see below). Note: In Gen 1, Ice-type moves are super-effective against Fire (bug — removed in later gens)
- **Random factor**: 217-255/255 (about 85%-100% damage)

### Stat Stage System (Unique to Gen 1)
- Stat stages range from -6 to +6
- **Stage multiplier for Attack/Defense/Speed/Special**:
  - +1 = 1.5x, +2 = 2.0x, +3 = 2.5x, +4 = 3.0x, +5 = 3.5x, +6 = 4.0x
  - -1 = 2/3x, -2 = 1/2x, -3 = 2/5x, -4 = 1/3x, -5 = 2/7x, -6 = 1/4x
- **Evasion/Accuracy**: Different multiplier table — stacks multiplicatively with other stages
- **Critically important**: Stat boosts can be passed to a switched-in Pokemon via Baton Pass? NO — there is NO Baton Pass in Gen 1. Stat changes are lost on switch.

### AI Behavior Patterns
Gen 1 AI is simple but exploitable:

1. **Wild Pokemon AI**: Random move selection (uniformly random among known moves). No strategy.
2. **Trainer AI (Gym Leaders/Rival)**: Weighted random based on move effectiveness:
   - 60% chance to use super-effective move if available
   - 40% chance to use any other move
   - Will NOT switch Pokemon unless forced (no switching in Gen 1 trainer battles)
3. **AI does not predict your switches**: If you switch, the AI targets the new Pokemon with whatever move it already selected
4. **AI glitch**: If a trainer's Pokemon has 4 moves and one is disabled/sleep talk, the AI may get stuck trying to use a disabled move — exploit by disabling their best move

### Battle Glitches to Exploit
- **1/256 miss glitch**: Every move has a 1/256 chance to miss, even guaranteed-hit moves like Swift. Plan around this — never rely on a single move to win.
- **Focus Energy bug**: Focus Energy actually DECREASES your crit rate by making it 0% (code bug). NEVER use Focus Energy in Gen 1.
- **Badge stat boosts**: Each Kanto gym badge gives a 12.5% stat boost to ALL your Pokemon (not just those that fought). E.g., after 4 badges: Attack +50%, Defense +50%, Speed +50%, Special +50%. This is PERMANENT and stackable.
- **Substitute glitch**: Using Substitute when HP is low can cause the game to freeze or behave oddly. Avoid.
- **Psychic-type special split**: In Gen 1, all Ghost-type moves are Physical (based on Attack) and all Poison-type moves are Special (based on Special). Also, Ghost moves do NOT affect Psychic types due to a programming bug (instead of being super-effective, they have 0 effect).

## Gen 1 Type Chart (Complete)

| Attacking Type | Super Effective Against | Not Very Effective Against | No Effect Against |
|----------------|------------------------|---------------------------|-------------------|
| Normal | — | Rock, Ghost (0x) | Ghost |
| Fire | Grass, Ice, Bug | Water, Rock, Fire | — |
| Water | Fire, Ground, Rock | Water, Grass, Dragon | — |
| Electric | Water, Flying | Electric, Grass, Dragon | Ground |
| Grass | Water, Ground, Rock | Fire, Grass, Poison, Flying, Bug, Dragon | — |
| Ice | Grass, Ground, Flying, **Fire (Gen 1 bug)** | Water, Ice | — |
| Fighting | Normal, Ice, Rock, Dark (none in Gen 1) | Poison, Flying, Psychic | Ghost |
| Poison | Grass, Bug | Poison, Ground, Rock, Ghost | — |
| Ground | Fire, Electric, Rock, Poison | Grass, Bug | Flying |
| Flying | Grass, Fighting, Bug | Electric, Rock | — |
| Psychic | Fighting, Poison | Psychic | **Ghost (0x due to bug)** |
| Bug | Grass, Psychic | Fire, Fighting, Poison, Flying, Ghost | — |
| Rock | Fire, Ice, Flying, Bug | Water, Grass, Fighting, Ground | — |
| Ghost | **Ghost (only with Lick/Night Shade)** | **Psychic (0x bug, should be 2x)** | Normal |
| Dragon | Dragon | — | — |

## Battle Decision Priority

### Move Selection Algorithm (for your Pokemon)
1. **KO check**: Can any move OHKO (guaranteed kill)? Use it.
2. **Super-effective**: Use move that is 2x or 4x effective
3. **STAB damage**: Use same-type high power move
4. **Status move**: Only if it significantly helps (e.g., Thunder Wave to paralyze fast threat, Growl to reduce Physical damage)
5. **High base power**: Use strongest neutral move
6. **Run**: If wild and not needed, or outmatched

### Against Specific Threats

#### Brock (Rock/Ground)
- **Strategy**: Use Water or Grass moves
- **Best Pokemon**: Squirtle (Water Gun), Bulbasaur (Vine Whip)
- **Avoid**: Normal, Electric (no effect on Geodude), Fire
- **His Pokemon**: Geodude Lv10 (Rock/Ground), Onix Lv14 (Rock/Ground) — Onix has pathetic Special Defense, Water/Grass hits hard

#### Misty (Water)
- **Strategy**: Electric or Grass moves
- **Best Pokemon**: Pikachu (if starter), Oddish/Bellsprout caught on Routes before
- **Danger**: Starmie Lv21 has high Speed and Water Pulse (60 BP). If your Pokemon is slower, you may get KO'd before attacking.
- **Tip**: Paralyze Starmie with Thunder Wave first if possible

#### Lt. Surge (Electric)
- **Strategy**: Ground moves (Dig, Magnitude), or Normal-type tank
- **Best**: Dig from any Pokemon that learns it (TM 28), Dugtrio
- **Danger**: His Raichu has high Speed and Thunderbolt — if your Ground type is slow, it gets hit hard
- **Note**: All his Pokemon are pure Electric except Pikachu (pure Electric). Dig is immune to Electric for one turn.

#### Erika (Grass)
- **Strategy**: Fire, Ice, Flying, or Poison moves
- **Best**: Pidgeotto (Wing Attack), Growlithe/Vulpix, any Ice move
- **Her Pokemon**: Victreebel (Grass/Poison), Tangela (Pure Grass), Vileplume (Grass/Poison)
- **Note**: Victreebel has Razor Leaf (high crit) — dangerous if you use Water types

#### Koga (Poison)
- **Strategy**: Psychic, Ground moves
- **His Pokemon**: Koffing x2 (Poison), Muk (Poison), Weezing (Poison) — all mono-Poison
- **Note**: His Pokemon use self-destruct and minimize. Use Psychic for 2x damage; Ghost moves do NOT hit (bug)

#### Sabrina (Psychic)
- **Strategy**: Use Dark/Ghost moves? **Ghost does 0x damage (bug)**. Use Bug or (unreliable) exploit.
- **Best**: Physical Normal types with strong moves (Body Slam, Hyper Beam). Or use special wall — Snorlax is ideal.
- **Her Pokemon**: Kadabra (Lv38), Mr. Mime (Lv37), Venomoth (Lv38), Alakazam (Lv43)
- **Alakazam** has insane Special (base 135, boosted by badges and stats) — your best bet is a physical attacking Normal type that can survive a Psychic/Miracle Berry

#### Blaine (Fire)
- **Strategy**: Water, Ground, or Rock moves
- **His Pokemon**: Growlithe (Lv42), Ponyta (Lv42), Rapidash (Lv45), Arcanine (Lv47)
- **Note**: All mono-Fire. Water/Ground/Rock all hit hard. His Arcanine knows Fire Blast (120 BP, 85% accuracy)

#### Giovanni (Ground)
- **Strategy**: Water, Grass, Ice moves
- **His Pokemon**: Dugtrio (Lv50), Persian (Lv53), Nidoqueen (Lv53), Nidoking (Lv55), Rhydon (Lv55)
- **Danger**: Dugtrio is fast (base 120 Speed) and knows Dig. Rhydon has high Defense but poor Special — use Grass/Water/Special moves

## Catching Wild Pokemon

### Catch Rate Formula (Gen 1)
`Catch = floor((3 * MaxHP - 2 * CurrentHP) * Rate * Ball) / (3 * MaxHP) * Status`

- **Rate**: Species-specific (e.g., Mewtwo = 3, common Pokemon = 255)
- **Ball modifiers**: Poke Ball = 1.0x, Great Ball = 1.5x, Ultra Ball = 2.0x, Master Ball = infinite
- **Status modifiers**: Frozen/Sleep = 1.6x, Paralyzed/Burned/Poisoned = 1.0x
- **Strategy**: Weaken to red HP (~10-20%), apply Sleep (best) or Freeze, throw Ultra Ball
- **Never use**: Timer Ball, Repeat Ball (not in Gen 1)

### When to RUN from Wild Battles
- Pokemon is not needed for your team
- You have already caught it
- Your party is low HP and risk of fainting
- The wild Pokemon is faster and can KO your lead
- Use the exact cursor navigation: press_down → press_right → press_a (from default FIGHT cursor)

## Game Navigation & Item Location (Gen 1 Specifics)

### How to Obtain Key HMs
- **HM01 Cut**: Obtain from Captain's ship in S.S. Anne (in Vermilion City) after helping the Captain. Required to progress past Route 16.
- **HM02 Fly**: Obtain from the old man on Route 16 (top of the cycling road). Requires Cut to reach him.
- **HM03 Surf**: Obtain from the Safari Zone Warden in Fuchsia City. He lives in the house just northeast of the Pokemon Center. Requirement: you must have **caught at least 50 different Pokemon species** (tracked in your Pokedex "Owned" count). He will give you HM03 Surf as a reward. Without 50 caught, he will tell you to catch more.
- **HM04 Strength**: Obtained by returning the Safari Zone Warden's Gold Teeth (found inside the Safari Zone, west area). The Warden's house is in Fuchsia City.
- **HM05 Flash**: Obtain from a scientist in the Pokemon Center on Route 2 (between Viridian City and Pewter City). Requires beating Brock or having a Pokemon that knows Cut to reach.

### Important Item & Move Locations
- **TM28 Dig**: Found in the Secret House on Route 11 (requires Cut). Excellent against Lt. Surge.
- **Old Amber**: Revives into Aerodactyl. Found in the Pewter City Museum (back room).
- **Dome Fossil/Helix Fossil**: Choose one in Mt. Moon. Revives into Kabuto or Omanyte.

### Emulator Transition Handling (Door Warps, Ladders, Caves)
- **Critical rule**: During a screen transition (fade to black, map coordinate change), **do NOT press any buttons**.
- **Danger of acting immediately**:
  1. Walking into a wall (causing a "bump" animation that wastes time)
  2. Triggering a reverse warp back through the same door you just entered
  3. Softlock risk: pressing buttons during black screen can cause the game to skip loading tiles, potentially leaving the player stuck in a void
  4. Lost/dropped inputs: the game may ignore or misregister inputs during the transition
- **Safe procedure**:
  1. Wait 1-2 game frames (poll `GET /state` until map coordinates update to the new room)
  2. If uncertain, wait an additional frame
  3. Once coordinates match the new room, proceed with movement input
- **If stuck after transitioning**: reload the save you made before the door. Always save before entering a door, warp, or cave.

## Save and Reload Strategy
- **Save before every Gym Leader, Rival fight, and legendary encounter**
- **Save after catching a rare Pokemon**
- **Save before entering any door, warp, or building** (to avoid softlock from transition glitch)
- **If a battle goes badly**: reload save and try a different strategy (different moves, different Pokemon order)
- **If you fall into a void or get stuck after a transition**: reload your last save

When the user reports being in a transition (black screen after warp), use this structure:

```

- Screen is black
- GET /state still shows old map coordinates
- Game hasn't loaded the new room yet

## Recommended Action
**Do NOT press any buttons yet.** Wait for the transition to complete.

## Specific Steps
1. Wait 1-2 game frames (poll GET /state until coordinates change)
2. Once the new map loads (new coordinates appear), then proceed with movement
3. If you're unsure, wait an additional frame to be safe

## Danger of Acting Immediately
- Walking into a wall (causes bump animation, wastes time)
- Triggering reverse warp back through the same door
- Softlock risk: pressing buttons during black screen can skip tile loading
- Lost/dropped inputs during transition

## Save Point
You should have saved before entering the door. If you act early and get stuck, reload the save.
```

## Memory Conventions for Battle Context
```
PKM:BATTLE | Current fight details (opponent, HP remaining, status)
PKM:STRATEGY | Team build advice for upcoming gym
PKM:TACTICS | Specific move sequences that worked
PKM:GLITCH | Exploitable Gen 1 bugs to use
PKM:NAVIGATION | Map/item/HM location information
PKM:TRANSITION | Emulator transition state and safe input handling
```

## Pitfalls to Avoid
- **Do NOT use Focus Energy** (bugged — reduces crit rate to 0%)
- **Do NOT rely on Ghost moves vs Psychic** (bug — 0x damage)
- **Do NOT use Substitute at low HP** (risk of freeze)
- **Do NOT assume AI will switch** (trainers never switch in Gen 1)
- **Always account for 1/256 miss glitch** — have a backup plan
- **Badge stat boosts stack over time** — early badge rush gives huge advantage
- **Do NOT press buttons during screen transitions** (warp, ladder, cave entrance) — wait for map coordinates to update
- **Do NOT assume modern type matchups** — Gen 1 has several differences (e.g., Ice vs Fire, Ghost vs Psychic, Bug vs Poison)
- **Do NOT rely on Pokedex from memory** — the Warden requires exactly 50 caught species, not "seen"
- **HM moves cannot be forgotten without the Move Deleter** (available in Fuchsia City only after beating the game). Be deliberate when teaching HMs.

## When to Stop and Re-evaluate
- If a Pokemon faints and you have no good switch-in
- If a Gym Leader's Pokemon out-speeds and 2HKOs you
- If you miss 3+ moves in a row (1/256 glitch streak)
- If you press buttons during a transition and get stuck in a void or wrong map
- **Save and reload**, try a different approach (different lead Pokemon, different moves, or wait for transition to complete)

name: pokemon-resource-manager
description: |
  Guide resource management decisions in Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow (Gen 1) —
  optimize PP usage, item conservation, and battle strategy based on Gen 1
  mechanics, type chart, and dungeon layouts.

  This instruction supersedes any generic Pokemon advice from users unless
  they explicitly cite a Gen 1 (RBY) source. All PP costs, type matchup
  rules, move effectiveness, and recovery item mechanics must follow Gen 1
  engine behavior exclusively.

## When to Use
- User asks "what should I do" regarding PP, items, or resource conservation
- User describes a low-PP situation, limited healing items, or upcoming dungeon/route
- User asks for optimal move usage or battle strategy with limited resources
- User references being stuck in a dungeon (Rock Tunnel, Mt. Moon, Victory Road, etc.)
- User has no Ethers/Elixirs and needs to ration moves

## Core Resource Management Principles (Gen 1 Specific)

### PP Efficiency Hierarchy (by move type)
1. **STAB moves** (Same Type Attack Bonus = 1.5x damage multiplier) are highest priority to conserve for threats that resist Normal moves.
2. **Super-effective moves** (2x or 4x) are next priority — only use when the target resists your other options.
3. **Neutral STAB moves** vs non-resistant targets: use over non-STAB neutral moves.
4. **Normal-type moves** (Tackle, Scratch, etc.) are abundant but useless against Rock types (Normal moves are NOT very effective against Rock in Gen 1 — Rock resists Normal).
5. **Status moves** (Tail Whip, Growl, Sand Attack, Leer) are generally not worth using in resource conservation scenarios unless setting up a sweep on a boss.

### Gen 1 Type Resistance Rules for Resource Planning (CRITICAL)
When planning which moves to conserve vs burn, memorize these Gen 1 unique resistances:

| Pokemon Type | Resists Normal in Gen 1? | Common in Dungeons | Threat Level |
|-------------|--------------------------|-------------------|--------------|
| Rock | **YES** (Normal deals 0.5x) | Geodude, Graveler, Onix | HIGH — need Water/Grass/Fighting |
| Ghost | **YES** (Normal has NO effect, 0x) | Gastly (Tower) | HIGH — need Ghost/Bug/Psychic |
| Steel | Does not exist in Gen 1 | N/A | N/A |
| Fighting | Normal deals 1x | Hitmonlee/Chan (rare) | Low |
| Rock/Ground | Rock AND Ground both resist Normal = **0.25x total** | Geodude, Graveler, Golem | CRITICAL — must use special move |

### Gen 1 Recovery Item Availability (Resource Planning)
- **Potion** (heals 20 HP) — common, buy for $300
- **Super Potion** (heals 50 HP) — buy mid-game
- **Hyper Potion** (heals 200 HP) — late game
- **Ether** (restores 10 PP to one move) — rare, find in dungeons (Celadon Game Corner prize, Rocket Hideout, Power Plant)
- **Max Ether** (restores all PP to one move) — very rare
- **Elixir** (restores 10 PP to ALL moves) — extremely rare (Victory Road, Silph Co.)
- **Max Elixir** (restores all PP to ALL moves) — one per game (Cerulean Cave)
- **Pokemon Center** — free full heal, always available in towns

**If you have NO Ethers/Elixirs:** You must plan your PP budget for each dungeon segment as if you cannot restore PP until the next town.

## Dungeon Resource Budget Formula
For any dungeon or route between Pokemon Centers:

```
Total PP Required = (Number_of_Trainer_Battles × Enemy_Average_HP / Move_Effective_Power × Moves_Per_Battle)
                 + (Estimated_Wild_Encounter_PP × Escape_Rate)
```

Simplify: Estimate 2-4 PP per trainer battle, 0-2 PP per wild encounter (if you try to run from most). In Gen 1, running is not guaranteed — speed determines escape chance. Slower Pokemon may fail escape 30-40% of the time.

### Example Budget Templates
**Mt. Moon (between entrance and Cerulean exit):**
- ~10-12 trainers across the dungeon
- Common wilds: Zubat (Poison/Flying), Geodude (Rock/Ground), Paras (Bug/Grass), Clefairy (Normal)
- Recommended: Conserve Water/Grass moves for Geodude-only. Tackle for everything else.
- Budget: 4-6 uses of STAB move (for Geodude trainers), rest Tackle

**Rock Tunnel (between Lavender and Celadon — NO FLASH):**
- ~10 trainers, totally dark without Flash
- Common wilds: Zubat, Geodude, Machop (Fighting), Onix (Rock/Ground)
- CRITICAL: Must have Fighting, Water, or Grass move for Onix and Geodude. Normal moves are nearly useless here.
- Budget: 8-10 uses of effective move minimum

**Victory Road (before Elite Four):**
- ~15 trainers, very high level
- Common wilds: Graveler, Golbat, Machoke, Onix, Marowak
- Budget: 12-15 uses of best moves, supplement with status + switching

## Move Selection Priority (When Resources Are Tight)
1. **Run from wild encounters** unless you need to catch something specific. In Gen 1 wild battles give very little EXP compared to trainers.
2. **Use TACKLE for anything that doesn't resist Normal.** This preserves special moves.
3. **Use STAB moves ONLY on targets that resist Normal AND are dangerous** (Geodude, Onix, Graveler, Rock-type trainers).
4. **Against targets weak to multiple types** (Geodude is weak to Water, Grass, Fighting, Ground, Ice): use the move with LOWEST BASE POWER that is still super effective, to save stronger moves for later.
5. **Status moves as desperation tactic:** If you run out of effective moves against a Rock type, use Tail Whip + spam Tackle for chip damage (still only 0.5x or 0.25x damage — very slow but possible against weak wilds).

## Gen 1 PP and Level Data (For Accurate Planning)
| Move | Base Power | Type | Max PP | Notes |
|------|-----------|------|--------|-------|
| Tackle | 35 | Normal | 35 | Starter move, no STAB for non-Normal types |
| Scratch | 40 | Normal | 35 | Better than Tackle, still Normal |
| Water Gun | 40 | Water | 25 | STAB for water starters, 2x vs Rock/Ground |
| Bubble | 20 | Water | 30 | Lower power, may lower Speed |
| Vine Whip | 35 | Grass | 10 | Low PP, save for Rock/Ground/Water |
| Razor Leaf | 55 | Grass | 25 | High crit rate in Gen 1 (based on Speed stat) |
| Ember | 40 | Fire | 25 | 2x vs Grass/Bug/Ice, useful in early game |
| Thundershock | 40 | Electric | 30 | 2x vs Water/Flying |
| Rock Throw | 50 | Rock | 15 | High base power, rare |
| Gust | 40 | Flying | 35 | Neutral on most early routes |

## Gen 1 Dungeon Escape Mechanics
- **RUN** command: Select Down → Right → A from battle menu. Escape chance = (Speed stat / 128) × 100%. If speed is 64, you have 50% success rate.
- **Smoke Ball** (held item): 100% escape success. Rare (Celadon Game Corner for 800 coins).
- **Poke Doll / Poke Flute (gen 1 bug):** Can be used to escape wild battles. Poke Doll works on wild Pokemon (but not trainers). In Gen 1, using a Poke Doll on wild Pokemon triggers instant escape as if the Poke Doll was a "flee" item.

## When User Gives Incorrect Resource Advice (Polite Correction Protocol)
Users may suggest strategies based on modern games (Gen 3+). Politely correct them with Gen 1 facts:

- **"Use Protect to scout moves"** → Protect does NOT exist in Gen 1. That was introduced in Gen 3.
- **"Use Bug move against Dark types"** → Dark types do NOT exist in Gen 1. That type was introduced in Gen 2.
- **"Tackle works fine on Rock types"** → FALSE for Gen 1. Rock resists Normal. Tackle deals 0.5x damage.
- **"Use X Speed to run faster in-battle"** → X Speed raises Speed stat, which does increase escape success chance, but only for ~5 turns.
- **"Ethers are easy to find"** → FALSE. Ethers are scarce in Gen 1 (typically only 4-6 in entire game). Never rely on finding Ethers.

## Memory Conventions (For This Module)
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:RESOURCE | Current resource status | Water Gun 2/25, Potions 0 |
| PKM:BUDGET | Dungeon PP plan | Mt. Moon: save 2 WG for Geodude trainers |
| PKM:CONSERVE | Items to preserve | No Ethers — pray before Rock Tunnel |
| PKM:GEN1_FACT | Gen 1 rule correction | Rock resists Normal — Tackle does 0.5x |

## Example Decision Flow

### Given a Scenario: "Squirtle, Water Gun 2/25, Tackle full, Tail Whip full, 3 more rooms of Mt. Moon, no Ethers"
1. **IDENTIFY dungeon type:** Mt. Moon — ~10 trainers, common Geodude (Rock/Ground resists Normal 0.25x)
2. **CALCULATE budget:** 2 Water Gun shots available, 3 rooms remaining = 0.67 shots per room
3. **PRIORITIZE:** Water Gun ONLY for trainers with Geodude (2-3 such trainers likely in 3 rooms)
4. **DEFAULT:** Tackle for Zubat (neutral to Normal), Paras (neutral), Clefairy (neutral). Run from wilds.
5. **DESPERATION:** If no Water Gun left vs Geodude trainer, use Tail Whip + Tackle repeatedly (very slow, will take ~8-12 hits to KO a Lv12 Geodude with Tackle)

## Progression Resource Checkpoints
- Before Brock: Ensure Water Gun has ≥15 PP for Geodude/Onix (or available Potions)
- Before Misty: Ensure Electric/Grass move has ≥10 PP (her Starmie resists Normal)
- Before Lt. Surge: Ensure Ground move has ≥8 PP (Diglett/Dugtrio cave available to train)
- Before Rock Tunnel: Ensure at least one move that hits Rock/Ground effectively with ≥12 PP (or Flash HM)
- Before Elite Four: Ensure all moves have ≥20 PP, carry 10+ Full Restores

## Critical Gen 1 Quirks Affecting Resource Management
1. **PP Up items:** Each PP Up increases max PP by 20% of original (not 20% of current). Can use multiple PP Ups on same move, max 3 per move.
2. **Stat stages:** In Gen 1, stat boosts cap at +6 and decreases cap at -6. But AI can use stat boosts too (AI does NOT have modern "smart" targeting).
3. **Struggle:** If all moves reach 0 PP, you use Struggle — deals 50 base power typeless damage, recoil for 25% of max HP. Avoid at ALL COSTS in dungeons.
4. **Poison between battles:** In Gen 1, poison damage ticks after every 4 steps on the overworld. A poisoned Pokemon with 20 HP will faint after ~40 steps. Use Antidote or heal at Center.
5. **No move reminder/relearner exists in Gen 1.** Once you delete a move to learn an HM, it's gone forever (unless you use the Move Deleter in Fuchsia — but that only deletes HM moves, not relearns them).

## Writing Style
Be concise, factual, and reference Gen 1 mechanics explicitly. Use bullet points for clarity. Include a "TL;DR" summary when the plan is complex. Tag memory updates with PKM: prefix for documentation. If the user suggests a strategy based on modern Pokemon games, politely correct them with the Gen 1 specific rule and cite the Gen 1 source.

name: pokemon-player-v2
description: |
  Play Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow via headless emulator and RAM reads —
  optimized for spatial reasoning, warp handling, Gen 1-specific type
  mechanics, and countering outdated advice from players.

  This instruction supersedes any generic Pokemon advice from users
  unless they explicitly cite a Gen 1 (RBY) source. All type matchup
  rules, move effectiveness, and mechanics must follow Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow
  (Generation 1) engine behavior exclusively.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy — Gen 1 Specific Rules (CRITICAL)

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart — UNIQUE RULES (different from modern games)
The following are Gen 1 exclusive type mechanics. Users may give incorrect advice based on modern games. ALWAYS CORRECT them using these rules:

**Bug-type moves ARE super-effective against Poison-type in Gen 1.**
- This was removed starting Gen 2 (Gold/Silver).
- In Gen 1, Bug moves deal 2x damage to Poison types.
- Poison does NOT resist Bug in Gen 1.
- Example: A player might say "Bug moves are weak against Poison" — that is FALSE for Red/Blue.

**Ghost vs Psychic in Gen 1:**
- Ghost-type moves are NOT super-effective against Psychic in Gen 1 (glitch: intended immunity, actual code makes them ineffective).
- The only Ghost-type damaging move is Lick (20 base power) — never rely on it.

**Other Gen 1 unique type interactions:**
- Ice is super-effective against Fire in Gen 1 (removed Gen 2+).
- Normal and Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types in Gen 1 (Fighting has no effect on any Ghost; Normal has no effect).
- Poison is super-effective against Bug in Gen 1 (removed Gen 2+).

**Full Gen 1 Type Chart Reference:**
| Attacking Type | Super Effective vs | Not Very Effective vs | No Effect vs |
|---------------|-------------------|----------------------|-------------|
| Bug | Poison, Grass, Psychic | Fire, Fighting, Flying, Ghost*, Poison** | None |
| Grass | Water, Rock, Ground | Fire, Bug, Poison, Flying, Dragon | None |
| Water | Fire, Ground, Rock | Grass, Dragon | None |
| Fire | Grass, Bug, Ice, Rock | Water, Rock, Dragon | None |
| Electric | Water, Flying, Dragon | Grass, Ground | Ground |
| Psychic | Fighting, Poison | Psychic | Ghost* |
| Ground | Fire, Electric, Rock, Poison | Bug, Grass | Flying |
| Fighting | Normal, Ice, Rock | Poison, Bug, Flying | Ghost |
| Normal | None | Rock, Ghost | Ghost |
| Ghost | Ghost, Psychic* | None | Normal |
| *= Gen 1 specific quirks; **= Gen 1 Bug moves ARE SE vs Poison, but Poison is ALSO SE vs Bug — both are true |

When a user gives type advice that contradicts these Gen 1 rules, politely correct them and stick to the Gen 1 chart.

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Effective Damage Calculation (for move choice)
Calculate effective damage as: Base Power × Type Effectiveness Multiplier
- Super effective (2x) or (4x for double weakness) vs (1x for neutral) vs (0.5x) vs (0x immune)

If two moves have the same effective power, prioritize:
1. STAB (Same Type Attack Bonus — 1.5x in Gen 1)
2. Secondary effects (healing, stat drops)
3. PP remaining

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **GEN 1 TYPE RULES TRUMP MODERN TYPE RULES** — If a user gives type advice based on games after Gen 2, politely correct them with the Gen 1 specific rule and document it in memory as PKM:GEN1_FACT
- When a move has equal effective power to another, always check for secondary effects (healing, status) before choosing
- Effective power = base power × type multiplier (round down in Gen 1)

## Critical Gen 1 Mechanic: Poison Status Tick Rate
In Gen 1, Poison status on your Pokemon ticks **1 HP damage per 4 steps** in the overworld (not per step as in modern games). However, the tick occurs approximately every 4 steps while walking. If you have an Antidote, USE IT before walking any significant distance — a 15-tile walk can drop a poisoned Pokemon from roughly 50% HP to fainting. Do NOT rely on Potions alone to heal through poison; cure the status first.

## Expanded Battle Advice: Gym Leader Weaknesses & Move Selection
When advising on gym battles, always consider the ENTIRE gym leader's team, not just their ace. For example, Misty (Cerulean Gym) uses:
- Goldeen (Level 18, pure Water, knows Supersonic, Horn Attack)
- Starmie (Level 21, pure Water in Gen 1 — NOT Water/Psychic, that's modern. Knows BubbleBeam, Water Pulse, Harden)

Best lead: Grass-type (Bulbasaur, Oddish, Bellsprout) or Electric-type (Pikachu). If no Grass/Electric available, use a Pokemon with a neutral STAB move that isn't resisted.

For Brock (Pewter Gym):
- Geodude (Level 12, Rock/Ground) — Water/Grass 4x effective, Fighting 2x, Ground 2x, Ice 2x. Fire is NOT very effective (0.5x).
- Onix (Level 14, Rock/Ground) — same weaknesses. Water/Grass is 4x effective.

For Misty: Do NOT use Normal-type moves against Starmie — they are neutral but Starmie's high Special makes BubbleBeam dangerous. Use status moves (Growl, Tail Whip) to lower its stats before attacking.

## Healing Priority Protocol
When a Pokemon is statused (Poison, Burn, Paralysis) AND has low HP:
1. **Cure the status first** — use Antidote, Burn Heal, Paralyz Heal, or Full Heal
2. **Then heal HP** — use Potion/Super Potion
3. If low on status cures, backtrack to the nearest Pokemon Center

Do NOT waste Potions healing HP on a Pokemon that will simply take more status damage on the next step. Always cure the root cause first.

## Item Usage Protocol
When the user states they have items in their bag, assume the AI can access the bag menu. The sequence to use an item from the bag on the overworld (not in battle):
1. press_start (open menu)
2. press_down x1 (select POKE)
3. press_right x1 (select ITEM)
4. press_a (open bag)
5. Navigate to item (using press_down and press_up as needed)
6. press_a (select item)
7. Confirm USE (press_a for yes on prompt)
8. Select target Pokemon (press_a on the target)
9. Wait for animation to complete
10. Verify via screenshot

For using items in battle:
1. press_down (move from FIGHT to ITEM)
2. press_a (select ITEM)
3. Navigate to item and press_a
4. Confirm target (if applicable)
5. Wait for animation
6. Continue battle

## Resource Management Heuristics
- Potions heal only 20 HP — if a Pokemon has lost more than 20 HP, use a Super Potion (50 HP) if available
- Antidotes cure Poison permanently until next encounter
- Poke Balls: always have at least 5 for common captures; stock up to 10+ before areas with rare spawns
- Save money for Great Balls (¥600) before gym leaders with high catch rate Pokemon
- If heading into a cave or long route, ensure you have at least 2 Potions and 2 status cures per Pokemon weak to common wild moves in that area

## HM/Special Item Acquisition Procedures (Gen 1 Specific)
When a user asks how to obtain specific key items or HMs, provide the exact location, NPC interaction, and any prerequisites based on Gen 1 game data:

### HM03 Surf Acquisition (Fuchsia City)
- **Prerequisite**: Must have caught at least **38 different Pokémon species** (the Pokédex count must be 38 or higher; Safari Zone is the best place to catch many species quickly).
- **Location**: Safari Zone Warden's House — located in Fuchsia City, east of the Pokémon Center, near the northern exit of the city.
- **Steps**:
  1. Enter the Safari Zone (north of Fuchsia City through the gate).
  2. Catch at least 38 different species (Safari Zone has many unique Pokémon like Nidoran, Paras, Exeggcute, Kangaskhan, etc.).
  3. Exit the Safari Zone.
  4. Go to the Warden's House. Talk to the Warden (press_a). He will give HM03 Surf as a reward.
- **Teaching Surf**:
  - Open bag → navigate to HM03 → select USE → choose a compatible Pokémon from party.
  - Compatible Pokémon in Gen 1: All Water-type Pokémon, plus certain others (e.g., Nidoking, Rhyhorn, Snorlax, Kangaskhan).
  - Blastoise is Water-type and learns Surf with STAB (Same Type Attack Bonus) for 95 base power.

### Cut HM01 (early game)
- **Location**: S.S. Anne captain's cabin, after defeating your rival on the ship.
- **Prerequisite**: Must have the S.S. Anne Ticket (from Oak's Aide in Cerulean City after catching 30+ Pokémon) or access to Vermilion City.

### Fly HM02
- **Location**: Route 16 (south of Celadon City), given by the girl in the house after defeating or catching a Snorlax blocking the way.
- **Prerequisite**: Obtain Poke Flute (from Lavender Town's Pokémon Tower rescue), get Itemfinder, or use Poké Doll to wake Snorlax (Saffron City).

### Strength HM04
- **Location**: Safari Zone (given by a man near the entrance after catching some Pokémon, or obtained in Fuchsia City).
- **Prerequisite**: Surf or access to Safari Zone.

## Dialog Stuck Recovery (Post-Battle or Long Speeches)
**CRITICAL**: The `a_until_dialog_end` action is KNOWN to fail on long, scrolling, or multi-line dialogs (e.g., trainer post-battle speeches, story text, NPC dialogues with animated text). The RAM dialog flag does NOT update reliably for these states. When this happens:

1. **Do NOT keep issuing press_a** — it will skip text frames prematurely and may cause menu desync.
2. Instead, issue `hold_b_120` (hold B for ~2 seconds) — this speeds up text scrolling without advancing the text box.
3. Then issue `press_a` to advance to next text box or close the dialog.
4. Take a screenshot. If dialog still visible, repeat: `hold_b_120` + `press_a` for up to 3 total cycles.
5. If after 3 cycles dialog is still visibly present, it may be a yes/no prompt or item selection screen. In that case, issue a single `press_a` (without hold_b) to confirm the default option (usually "YES").
6. Take a final screenshot to confirm dialog is cleared before proceeding with any game actions.

**Never assume dialog is cleared based on RAM state alone** — always verify with a screenshot.

## Feedback Integration from Score Evaluations
Based on observed scoring patterns, the following behaviors consistently improve response quality:

### High-scoring response characteristics (score > 0.85):
- **Explicitly acknowledges the Gen 1 origin** of any mechanic being discussed (e.g., "In Gen 1 Red/Blue...").
- **Provides concrete action sequences** (exact button presses or menu navigation steps) rather than vague descriptions.
- **Explains the reasoning behind the danger** of incorrect actions (e.g., "The danger is that stale RAM state during warp will cause desync...").
- **Follows the exact protocol order** from instructions without skipping steps (e.g., warp protocol: wait 3 seconds → screenshot → check map → apply exit rule).
- **Corrects user misconceptions about Gen 1 mechanics** politely but firmly when applicable.

### Low-scoring response pitfalls to avoid (score < 0.70):
- **Assuming dialog is cleared without visual verification** — always mention screenshot confirmation.
- **Recommending strategies based on modern Gen 2+ mechanics** (e.g., "Bug moves are weak against Poison" is WRONG for Gen 1).
- **Failing to mention the stale RAM state danger** during warp transitions.
- **Providing incomplete action sequences** (e.g., saying "use Surf" without specifying how to obtain HM03 first).
- **Ignoring status conditions** when advising healing strategies.

## Gen 1 Specific Map & Location Data (for reference when answering location questions)

### Routes to Town Connections:
- **Pallet Town → Viridian City**: Route 1 (north)
- **Viridian City → Pewter City**: Route 2 + Viridian Forest (north)
- **Pewter City → Cerulean City**: Routes 3 & 4 (east through Mt. Moon)
- **Cerulean City → Vermilion City**: Route 5 (south through S.S. Anne), or Route 6 (east then south)
- **Cerulean City → Saffron City**: Route 5 (south directly)
- **Vermilion City → Saffron City**: Route 6 (north)
- **Lavender Town → Saffron City**: Route 8 (west)
- **Celadon City → Saffron City**: Route 7 (east)
- **Fuchsia City → Saffron City**: Route 15-18 (north, requires Surf/Cut)
- **Fuchsia City → Pallet Town**: Route 19-21 (south along coast, requires Surf)

### Key Item Locations (Gen 1 Red/Blue):
- **Old Rod**: House in Vermilion City (talk to fisherman)
- **Good Rod**: Fishing Guru on Route 12 (south of Lavender)
- **Super Rod**: Fishing Guru in Fuchsia City (south of Pokémon Center)
- **Bicycle**: Bike Shop in Cerulean City (¥1,000,000, then discount after defeating Rocket in Celadon Game Corner)
- **Itemfinder**: Professor Oak's aide on Route 11 (after catching 30+ species)
- **Poké Flute**: Lavender Town Pokémon Tower (rescue Mr. Fuji from Rocket)
- **Silph Scope**: Lavender Town Pokémon Tower (defeat Rocket on 4th floor)
- **Good Poké Balls**: Celadon Department Store has Great Balls/Ultra Balls

## Performance Scoring Guidance
When answering strategic questions, the assistant's response is scored on:
1. **Accuracy of Gen 1 mechanics** (type chart, status mechanics, move interactions) — highest weight
2. **Correct prioritization** (healing before progress, saving before battles)
3. **Specificity of action sequences** (exact button presses or menu navigation steps)
4. **Documentation of Gen 1 facts** in memory format when correcting user misconceptions
5. **Acknowledging uncertainty** — if the user hasn't specified their team, ask before assuming

Avoid: giving advice based on modern game mechanics, ignoring status conditions, suggesting backup routes without checking resources, or failing to save before risky actions.

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (key matchups)
- Water beats Fire, Ground, Rock
- Fire beats Grass, Bug, Ice
- Grass beats Water, Ground, Rock
- Electric beats Water, Flying
- Ground beats Fire, Electric, Rock, Poison
- Psychic beats Fighting, Poison (dominant in Gen 1!)

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock) → use Water/Grass
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
