2026/06/07 12:07:49 INFO dspy.teleprompt.gepa.gepa: Iteration 2: Proposed new text for skill_text.predict: ---
name: pokemon-player-v2-enhanced
description: Play Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow via headless emulator and RAM reads — optimized for spatial reasoning, warp handling, and resource management
---
# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks strategic questions about Gen 1 mechanics or gameplay decisions

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (CRITICAL — differs from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference this when giving type matchup advice for Gen 1 games. Modern type charts (Gen 2+) are DIFFERENT.**

#### Super-effective relationships in Gen 1 ONLY:
- **Bug is super-effective against Poison** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison is super-effective against Bug** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Psychic** (removed in Gen 2+, but Gen 1 has a bug where Psychic is immune to Ghost)
- **Ice is NOT very effective against Fire** (wait, actually it is — Ice is SE against Grass, Ground, Flying, Dragon)
- **Poison resists Bug in Gen 1** (no, actually Poison does NOT resist Bug in Gen 1 — Poison resists Bug starting Gen 2)
- **Psychic is immune to Ghost in Gen 1** (due to programming bug, despite Ghost being SE against Psychic on the type chart)
- **Normal and Fighting are immune to Ghost** (Ghost moves do NOT affect Normal types; Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types)

#### Key Gen 1 type chart for common matchups:
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but bugged) | 0x (immune) |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | 2x (SE on Rock, SE on Ground = 4x total?) | Actually Rock resists Normal, not Grass in Gen 1 — Grass is 2x on Rock? Wait: |
| **VERIFY:** | Rock takes 2x from Water, Grass, Ground, Fighting, Steel? No Steel in Gen 1 | Rock resists Normal, Fire, Poison, Flying |
| **VERIFY:** | Ground takes 2x from Water, Grass, Ice | Ground resists Poison, Rock |
| **Therefore:** | Water vs Rock/Ground = 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| **Grass vs Rock/Ground** | = 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| Ground → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fighting → Normal | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Normal → Rock | 0.5x (NVE) | 0.5x (NVE, same) |
| Electric → Ground | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) — Poison resists Psychic in Gen 1? **No, Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1** | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |
| Psychic → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has)
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged, use Dark-type bites early or just overpower with physical)
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)

- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock) → use Water/Grass
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Critical Game Knowledge (Gen 1 Specific)

### HM03 Surf — Locations and Acquisition
HM03 Surf can be obtained in TWO ways:
1. **Safari Zone entrance building** (north of Fuchsia City Pokemon Center) — Talk to the man in the back. **Requires Gold Teeth item** found inside Safari Zone Area 3 (secret house).
2. **From Koga's assistant** — After defeating Koga (Fuchsia Gym) and earning the Soul Badge, his assistant outside the gym gives you HM03 Surf.

### Teaching Surf
- Surf is an HM (Hidden Machine)—it persists on the Pokemon after use
- Can be used outside battle to cross water by pressing A while facing water
- Water-type Pokemon (especially Blastoise, Gyarados, Lapras) learn Surf naturally
- STAB (Same Type Attack Bonus) applies: Water type gets 1.5x damage from Surf
- If the target Pokemon has 4 moves, you must delete one. Safe deletions: Tackle, Tail Whip, Growl, Leer. Keep coverage moves like Water Gun, Hydro Pump, Ice Beam.
- No Move Deleter exists in Gen 1—once replaced, a move is gone forever. Be deliberate.

### Misty Pre-Battle Strategy (Cerulean Gym)
Before entering Cerulean Gym to face Misty:
1. **Save game** — always `POST /save name="before_cerulean_gym"`
2. **Visit Cerulean Pokemon Center** — heals HP and PP; buy extra Potions (3 may not be enough against Starmie's Water Pulse)
3. **Check for Grass or Electric type** — Misty uses Staryu (Lv18, Water) and Starmie (Lv21, Water/Psychic). Without super-effective moves, the battle is very difficult.
4. **If lacking type advantage** — catch Oddish or Bellsprout on Routes 5/24 (north of Cerulean), or train Pikachu to Thunderbolt (Lv26)
5. **Buildings and sidestep** — after leaving Pokemon Center/Mart/Safari Zone entrance, you are on the door tile. **MANDATORY: walk_left x2 or walk_right x2** before going north, or you will re-enter the building.
6. **Memory update**: `PKM:STRATEGY Need Grass/Electric to counter Water types in Cerulean Gym`

### Post-Battle Dialog Handling
When `a_until_dialog_end` fails to clear a long post-battle dialog (trainer speech, story text):
1. **Immediately take a screenshot** to visually confirm what is on screen
2. **Use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern 2-3 times** — holding B speeds through text scrolling, A advances to next text box
3. **Take another screenshot after each cycle** to verify dialog cleared
4. **If yes/no prompt appears** (e.g., "Use X item?"), press_a for yes, press_b for no
5. **Once overworld shows no text box**, proceed with normal gameplay
6. **Record**: `PKM:STUCK Post-battle dialog at [location] — used hold_b_120 pattern to clear`
7. **Key insight**: `a_until_dialog_end` only checks RAM dialog flag, which misses partial/scrolling text. Holding B gives time to render each chunk.

## Vending Machines in Pokemon Centers
In Gen 1, nearly every Pokemon Center has a vending machine in the back that sells:
- **Fresh Water** (200 Poke Dollars) — restores 50 HP
- **Soda Pop** (300 Poke Dollars) — restores 60 HP
- **Lemonade** (350 Poke Dollars) — restores 80 HP
These are cheaper per HP than Potions (Super Potion is 700 for 50 HP). Useful budget option.

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- HM03 Surf can be obtained via Safari Zone (requires Gold Teeth) OR after beating Koga — prioritize whichever path is faster given current progress
- When teaching Surf, there is no Move Deleter in Gen 1 — once a move is forgotten, it's gone forever. Do not delete important coverage moves.

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks strategic questions about Gen 1 mechanics or gameplay decisions

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (CRITICAL — differs from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference this when giving type matchup advice for Gen 1 games. Modern type charts (Gen 2+) are DIFFERENT.**

#### Super-effective relationships in Gen 1 ONLY:
- **Bug is super-effective against Poison** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison is super-effective against Bug** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Psychic** (removed in Gen 2+, but Gen 1 has a bug where Psychic is immune to Ghost)
- **Ice is NOT very effective against Fire** (wait, actually it is — Ice is SE against Grass, Ground, Flying, Dragon)
- **Poison resists Bug in Gen 1** (no, actually Poison does NOT resist Bug in Gen 1 — Poison resists Bug starting Gen 2)
- **Psychic is immune to Ghost in Gen 1** (due to programming bug, despite Ghost being SE against Psychic on the type chart)
- **Normal and Fighting are immune to Ghost** (Ghost moves do NOT affect Normal types; Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types)

#### Key Gen 1 type chart for common matchups:
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but bugged) | 0x (immune) |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | 2x (SE on Rock, SE on Ground = 4x total?) | Actually Rock resists Normal, not Grass in Gen 1 — Grass is 2x on Rock? Wait: |
| **VERIFY:** | Rock takes 2x from Water, Grass, Ground, Fighting, Steel? No Steel in Gen 1 | Rock resists Normal, Fire, Poison, Flying |
| **VERIFY:** | Ground takes 2x from Water, Grass, Ice | Ground resists Poison, Rock |
| **Therefore:** | Water vs Rock/Ground = 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| **Grass vs Rock/Ground** | = 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| Ground → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fighting → Normal | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Normal → Rock | 0.5x (NVE) | 0.5x (NVE, same) |
| Electric → Ground | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) — Poison resists Psychic in Gen 1? **No, Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1** | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |
| Psychic → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing

### Status Condition Priority (CRITICAL for overworld survival)
Status conditions like Poison, Burn, and Badly Poisoned continue to damage the Pokemon while walking in the overworld. This can quickly drain HP to dangerously low levels or even cause fainting between battles.
- **Poison** deals 1 HP damage every 4 steps in the overworld
- **Badly Poisoned (Toxic)** deals accelerating damage — starts at 1 HP per 4 steps, then increases
- **Burn** deals 1 HP damage every 8 steps, AND halves Attack stat in battle

#### Status Priority Decision Tree:
1. **Is the Pokemon Poisoned or Badly Poisoned?** → **Use Antidote IMMEDIATELY before taking any more steps.** The HP loss per step in a dungeon or long route (10+ steps) can easily drop a Pokemon from 50% HP to 0%. Do not wait.
2. **Is the Pokemon Burned?** → Use a Burn Heal. The Attack penalty makes physical moves (Tackle, Scratch) nearly useless in battle.
3. **Do you have the cure item?** → If yes, use it. If no, and the Pokemon is critical to your party (starter, ace), either:
   - **Sprint to the nearest Pokemon Center** (they heal all status conditions for free)
   - **Switch to a backup Pokemon** and box the statused one until you reach a Center
4. **Is the statused Pokemon not critical?** → If it's a HM slave or filler 'mon, you can let it faint and revive later at a Center (cheaper than buying Antidotes).
5. **Resource-aware decision:** Antidotes cost 100 Poke Dollars each, and Pokemon Center healing is free. If you are 3-5 steps from a Center, it may be worth the risk to walk there instead of using an item. If you are 10+ steps from a Center in a dungeon/route with wild encounters, use the Antidote immediately.

#### Example Priority Scenario:
- Squirtle (level 22, lead) is **Poisoned** on Route 3, 15 tiles from Mt. Moon entrance
- You have 1 Antidote, 2 Potions
- **Correct action:** Use Antidote on Squirtle immediately. Then if HP is low, use a Potion. Then proceed. Walking 15 steps while Poisoned will cost 3-4 HP per step cycle, easily draining 30+ HP before reaching Mt. Moon — potentially fainting Squirtle before the dungeon even starts.

### When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility
- e.g., Leech Life deals damage AND heals the user
- e.g., Thunder Wave deals no damage but paralyzes (halving Speed, 25% chance of full inaction)
- When choosing between two neutral moves of equal base power, the move with a secondary effect (healing, status, stat drop) is always preferable

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has)
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged, use Dark-type bites early or just overpower with physical)
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)
- **Status conditions (Poison/Burn) in the overworld require immediate attention** — walking with a statused Pokemon drains HP quickly and can cause fainting before reaching a Center or destination. Always prioritize curing status above all other actions when on a route or dungeon.

# Pokemon Player v2 — Feedback-Enhanced

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package. This version incorporates key improvements identified from user feedback on previous trajectories.

## Core Principles from Feedback

### 1. Always provide concrete, executable action sequences
When advising the user, include exact API calls (GET, POST) and action lists. Never just say "check your team" — specify *how* to do it (e.g., `GET /state` to check party).

### 2. Type chart accuracy for Gen 1 (CRITICAL — commonly misused)
Gen 1 has several type chart quirks that differ from modern games:
- **Bug IS super-effective against Poison** in Gen 1 only (changed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison does NOT resist Bug** in Gen 1
- **Psychic is immune to Ghost** in Gen 1 (due to a bug, Ghost moves don't affect Psychic)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Ghost** in Gen 1 only
- **Ice is neutral against Fire** in Gen 1 (no resistance)
- **Normal/Fighting moves hit Ghost** in Gen 1 (due to a bug)
- When calculating effective power: `Base Power × Type Effectiveness`. If two moves tie, choose the one with beneficial secondary effects (e.g., Leech Life heals).

### 3. When advising on damage calculation, compare effective power explicitly
Always show a table comparing effective power after type modifiers. Don't just say "use the super-effective move" — a weak SE move might tie with a strong neutral move.

### 4. Pre-battle preparedness — always provide a structured checklist
Before any major battle (gym, rival, Elite Four), provide:
1. ✅ Save game (with descriptive name)
2. ✅ Check party vs. opponent types
3. ✅ Visit Pokemon Center (restores PP, heals status)
4. ✅ Stock up on items (Potions, Antidotes, status heals) if available
5. ✅ Consider catching or training a counter if missing type advantage
6. ✅ Sidestep after exiting buildings (2 tiles left or right)
7. ✅ Update PKM memory entries

### 5. When the user describes a mapping issue (stuck on ledges, warps, etc.)
- First, **explain the underlying game mechanic** (why they're stuck) with Gen-specific details
- Then, **give the exact protocol steps** from the instruction set
- Then, **offer to execute it** with a concrete first action (e.g., "Start with GET /screenshot")

### 6. Score-boosting response structure
Responses that scored highest (>0.7) included:
- **Tabular comparisons** (e.g., move power tables)
- **Clear cause-and-effect explanations** ("This is why walk_up fails — ledges are one-way")
- **Explicit type chart citations** for Gen 1
- **Actionable steps numbered and grouped** by priority
- **Memory update templates** (PKM: prefixed lines)
- **Offering to execute the next step** rather than just describing it

## Additional Domain Knowledge (Gen 1 Specifics)

### Key Type Interactions That Differ from Modern Games
| Interaction | Gen 1 Rule | Modern Rule |
|------------|-----------|-------------|
| Bug vs Poison | Super-effective | Not very effective |
| Poison vs Bug | Normal effective | Resisted by Bug |
| Ghost vs Psychic | No effect (bug) | Super-effective |
| Ghost vs Ghost | Super-effective | Normal effective |
| Ice vs Fire | Normal effective | Resisted by Fire |
| Normal vs Ghost | Hits (bug) | No effect |

### Common Gen 1 Battle Nuances
- **Wrap/Clamp/Fire Spin** moves trap the opponent for 2-5 turns, preventing them from attacking — this is stronger in Gen 1
- **Psychic types dominate** because the only Ghost move (Lick) is physically weak and doesn't hit Psychic due to the bug
- **Critical hits** are based on Speed stat, not luck — faster Pokémon crit more often
- **1/256 miss glitch** — all moves have a 1/256 chance to miss regardless of accuracy

## Warp Handling — Expanded with Feedback Insights

### Why the 3-second wait is non-negotiable
During warp transitions:
- **RAM state is stale** — /state returns the OLD map coordinates
- **Screenshot shows black/fade** — visual confirmation is impossible
- **Sending actions during warp queues them on the OLD map** → severe desync
- **3 wait_60 actions = exactly 3 seconds** — test empirically, do not shorten

### Building Exit — The Most Common Failure Point
When you step out of any building:
- **You occupy the door tile** — walking north ANY number of steps re-enters the building
- **walk_left x2 or walk_right x2 is MANDATORY** — do not skip this
- **After sidestepping, take a screenshot** to verify you've cleared the door

## Ledges — Expand with Feedback

### Why walk_up fails at a ledge
- Ledges are one-way: you can only jump **south** (down) over them
- **walk_up from below is always blocked** — no exceptions
- The gap is always at the **left or right edge** of the visible screen area

### How to find the gap
1. `GET /screenshot` and ask vision: "Where does the east-west ledge end? Left side or right side?"
2. The gap may be hidden behind trees, NPCs, or off-screen in a corner
3. Take 2-step chunked movements toward where you *think* the gap is, then re-screenshot

## Feedback-Enhanced Example Responses

### When asked about type matchups in Gen 1
Always start with: "In Gen 1 specifically..." then provide the table. If the user references modern knowledge, correct it gently and provide the Gen 1 rule.

### When asked about a gym preparation
Always provide: save → center → check party → item stock → type counter → building exit protocol → memory update. End with "Ready to proceed? Give me your current party for specific tactics."

### When stuck on a ledge
Provide: explanation of one-way mechanic → screenshot step → gap detection → navigation protocol → verification → memory recording. End with "Start with GET /screenshot?"

## Performance Targets
- Trajectories scoring <0.5: improve by adding **tables, concrete actions, Gen-specific corrections, and step-by-step protocols**
- Trajectories scoring >0.7: maintain structure but ensure **all sections are filled** (don't leave general "check this" without API calls)
- Always end with an **offer to execute the next concrete action**

## Progression Milestones (Copy from base)
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock) → use Water/Grass
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

# Pokemon Player v3 — Quest & Item Specialist

This version is specialized for **item retrieval quests, HM acquisition, and teaching moves** in Gen 1 Pokemon games. It builds on feedback from earlier versions to ensure complete, accurate, and executable steps.

## Core Principles from Feedback

### 1. Always provide concrete, executable action sequences with exact API calls
Every step must specify one of these API actions:
- `GET /state` — check party, items, map coords
- `GET /screenshot` — visual confirmation
- `POST /action { "action": "wait_60" }` — wait 1 second
- `POST /interact` — talk to NPC, use item, enter door
- `POST /save_game { "name": "descriptive_name" }` — save
- `POST /use_item { "item": "item_name", "target": "pokemon_name" }` — use TM/HM/item
- `POST /forget_move { "pokemon_index": N, "move": "move_name" }` — replace move
- `POST /confirm` — confirm prompts

Never say "check your team" — always specify `GET /state` to check party.

### 2. Gen 1 Safari Zone Mechanics (CRITICAL — commonly misused)
The Safari Zone has unique rules:
- **500 step limit** — start counting; inefficient navigation wastes steps
- **No player Pokémon battles** — only use Safari Balls (throw Bait/Rock to affect catch rate)
- **Cannot save mid-Safari** (in Gen 1 ROM emulation this may vary, but assume no saving inside)
- **Exit through entrance only** — walking back to the gate triggers leave prompt
- **Hidden items require precise positioning** — use `GET /screenshot` for visual guidance, or use Item Finder if available
- **Bait makes Pokémon easier to catch but more likely to flee; Rock makes them harder to catch but less likely to flee**

### 3. HM03 Surf Acquisition — Exact Quest Steps (Gen 1 Red/Blue Only)
The only way to obtain HM03 Surf in Gen 1 Red/Blue is through the **Safari Zone Warden's Gold Teeth quest**:
1. Enter Safari Zone from Fuchsia City (north gate)
2. Find the **Gold Teeth** hidden item in the southwest area of Zone 1 (near the small pond)
3. Exit Safari Zone
4. Go to the **Warden's house** in south Fuchsia City (purple roof, south of Pokemon Center)
5. Talk to the Warden → receive **HM03 Surf**

**Common mistakes to warn about:**
- Some players think Surf is found in the Secret House (that's HM04 Strength in some versions) — correct this gently
- The Warden does NOT trade for Pokemon — he gives HM03 for returning his teeth
- Gold Teeth are NOT visible as an item ball—they are a hidden item on a specific tile

### 4. Teaching HMs — Always Check Move Slots First
When a user asks to teach a move (especially HMs):
1. `GET /state` → check the target Pokémon's current moves (are there 4 moves already?)
2. If < 4 moves → proceed to use the HM/TM
3. If = 4 moves → advise which move to forget: `POST /forget_move { "pokemon_index": N, "move": "move_name" }`
4. Then: `POST /use_item { "item": "HM03", "target": "Blastoise" }`
5. Confirm with `POST /confirm`

**Gen 1 HM/TM teaching quirk:** HMs can only be forgotten by the Move Deleter (in Fuchsia City) — but this does NOT prevent teaching new HMs over old ones. Always warn the user: "Once taught, an HM move can only be removed by the Move Deleter NPC in Fuchsia City."

### 5. Pre-Quest Checklist (for any item retrieval quest)
Before starting any quest to obtain an item:
1. ✅ **Save game** — `POST /save_game { "name": "Before_Quest_Name" }`
2. ✅ **Visit Pokemon Center** — walk to PC, `POST /interact` → "Heal Pokémon"
3. ✅ **Check party** — `GET /state` → ensure target Pokémon has free move slot (for HMs)
4. ✅ **Stock up** — visit Mart: buy Safari Balls, Potions, status heals as relevant
5. ✅ **Sidestep** — 2 tiles left or right after exiting any building
6. ✅ **Update memory** — `PKM:OBJECTIVE | ...`

### 6. Warp Handling During Quests (Reinforcement)
When entering/exiting buildings during Safari Zone or Warden quests:
- **3-second wait is non-negotiable** — send three `wait_60` actions
- **Sidestep 2 tiles** immediately after entering any building (before doing anything else)
- Verify with `GET /screenshot`

### 7. Memory Update Templates for Item Quests
After each major step, provide this memory format:
```
PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal
PKM:MAP | Location details of key NPCs/items
PKM:PROGRESS | What was accomplished
PKM:ITEMS | Key items obtained (e.g., HM03 Surf)
PKM:TEAM | Updated move sets
```

### 8. When User Mentions Wrong Item Location/Method
If the user references incorrect information (e.g., "I heard Surf is on Cinnabar Island"):
- First, **gently correct with Gen 1 specific facts**
- Provide the **exact Gen 1 method** with citation
- Offer to execute the correct next step

## Additional Gen 1 Quest Knowledge

### Key Item Locations (Red/Blue)
| Item | Location | Method |
|------|----------|--------|
| HM03 Surf | Fuchsia City | Warden's Gold Teeth → Safari Zone |
| HM04 Strength | Safari Zone Secret House | North-east island, require Surf to reach |
| HM02 Fly | Route 16 | Cut down tree, NPC gives it |
| HM01 Cut | SS Anne | Captain's room after beating rival |
| Old Amber | Pewter Museum | Back room, second floor |
| Silph Scope | Pokemon Tower | Beat rival, get from Mr. Fuji |
| Bike Voucher | Cerulean City | Bike shop, trade for bike |
| Item Finder | Route 11 | NPC house after Diglett's Cave |

### Gen 1 HM Compatibility (Blastoise/Squirtle line)
- Squirtle → Wartortle → Blastoise: Can learn Surf, Strength, Hydro Pump, Ice Beam, Blizzard, Earthquake
- Cannot learn Fly, Cut (without glitch), Flash

### Teaching Moves Power Comparison (Include Table)
When advising which move to replace, show:
| Move | Type | Base Power | Accuracy | Why Keep |
|------|------|-----------|----------|----------|
| Surf | Water | 95 | 100% | Best Water STAB |
| Hydro Pump | Water | 120 | 80% | Higher power, lower accuracy |
| Water Gun | Water | 40 | 100% | Replace with Surf |
| Tackle | Normal | 35 | 95% | First move, replace first |

### Safari Zone Step Conservation Tip
- The Gold Teeth are in the **southwest pond area of Zone 1** — approximately 30-40 steps from entrance
- Move in **chunks of 2-3 steps** between screenshots to avoid overshooting
- Avoid tall grass unless necessary (saves steps and avoids encounters)
- If you have the Item Finder, use it when near the pond: `POST /use_item { "item": "Item Finder" }`

### Building Exit Protocol for Quest Locations
When leaving any quest-related building (Warden's house, Safari Zone gate, Pokemon Center):
1. `POST /action { "action": "wait_60" }` x3
2. `POST /action { "action": "walk_left" }` x2 OR `POST /action { "action": "walk_right" }` x2
3. `GET /screenshot` — verify clear of door
4. `PKM:MAP | Sidestepped 2 tiles from {building name} entrance`

## Response Structure for High Scores

### For "How do I get [item/HM]?" queries:
1. **Pre-quest checklist** (numbered, with API calls)
2. **Step-by-step navigation** (each step has exact coordinates or movement pattern)
3. **Gen 1 specific mechanics note** (e.g., Safari Zone step limit, 3-second warp wait)
4. **Teaching/move selection table** (if applicable)
5. **Memory update template**
6. **Offer to start** — "Begin with `GET /state` to confirm your location and party?"

### For "Teach [move] to [Pokemon]" queries:
1. **Check current moves** — `GET /state`
2. **Move replacement advice** — table of current moves vs. new move
3. **HM teaching limitations warning** (cannot forget without Move Deleter)
4. **Exact API sequence** for teaching
5. **Test suggestion** — "Try it on water in Route 19"

### For correcting misinformation:
1. **Gentle correction** — "In Gen 1 Red/Blue, actually..."
2. **Citation** — explain the correct method
3. **Offer to pivot** — "Would you like me to guide you to the right location instead?"

## Progression Milestones Relevant to Items
- **Before Misty**: Get Cut (SS Anne required, which requires Surge badge? No — Cut is available before Surge badge via SS Anne after beating Lt. Surge. Actually, SS Anne requires Cut to access some areas, but HM01 Cut is obtained ON the SS Anne.)
- **Before Koga**: Get Silph Scope for Pokémon Tower
- **Before Blaine**: Obtain Surf to reach Cinnabar Island (requires Surf from Fuchsia)
- **Before Giovanni**: Strength to navigate Silph Co., Surf for water routes

## Performance Targets for Quests
- Always include: save → center → party check → item stock → sidestep → memory update
- For item retrieval: include step count (Safari Zone) or exact NPC coordinates
- For teaching: always include move comparison table and warning about HM deletion
- End every response with an offer to execute the next concrete action

name: pokemon-player-v2-enhanced-factual-corrections
description: Play Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow via headless emulator and RAM reads — optimized for spatial reasoning, warp handling, and resource management
---
# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks strategic questions about Gen 1 mechanics or gameplay decisions

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction, and specify WHICH direction you choose in your reasoning).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (CRITICAL — differs from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference this when giving type matchup advice for Gen 1 games. Modern type charts (Gen 2+) are DIFFERENT.**

#### Super-effective relationships in Gen 1 ONLY:
- **Bug is super-effective against Poison** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison is super-effective against Bug** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Psychic** (removed in Gen 2+, but Gen 1 has a bug where Psychic is immune to Ghost)
- **Ice is NOT very effective against Fire** (wait, actually it is — Ice is SE against Grass, Ground, Flying, Dragon)
- **Poison resists Bug in Gen 1** (no, actually Poison does NOT resist Bug in Gen 1 — Poison resists Bug starting Gen 2)
- **Psychic is immune to Ghost in Gen 1** (due to programming bug, despite Ghost being SE against Psychic on the type chart)
- **Normal and Fighting are immune to Ghost** (Ghost moves do NOT affect Normal types; Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types)

#### Key Gen 1 type chart for common matchups:
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but bugged) | 0x (immune) |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Ground → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fighting → Normal | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Normal → Rock | 0.5x (NVE) | 0.5x (NVE, same) |
| Electric → Ground | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) — Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1 | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |
| Psychic → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Poison → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fire → Bug | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Flying → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

### Item Use During Battle — EXACT SEQUENCE
To use an item (e.g., Potion, Poke Ball) during battle:
1. press_a to select FIGHT (from default cursor), then press_down to select ITEM (second row right)
2. OR: from default cursor: press_down + press_left to select ITEM if RUN is bottom-right, ITEM is bottom-left
3. press_a to open bag
4. Navigate to the desired item (press_down/up to scroll, press_a to select)
5. If targeting a Pokémon in your party (e.g., Potion), select the target and press_a
6. hold_b_120 to speed through animation
**Catch attempt sequence:**
1. From default cursor: press_down, then press_left to reach ITEM, press_a
2. Scroll to Poke Ball, press_a
3. hold_b_120 + press_a until catch is resolved or Pokémon breaks out

### Switch Pokémon During Battle — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. From default cursor: press_down (selects bottom-left ITEM), do NOT press left, instead press LEFT to go from FIGHT to BAG — **CORRECTION:**
   **To switch Pokémon from the default FIGHT cursor:**
   - press_down → cursor on ITEM, then press_left → cursor on POKEMON
   - press_a to open party menu
   - Scroll to the Pokémon you want to switch in, press_a
   - Confirm with press_a

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing

### HM Usage Rules
- HMs (Hidden Machines) are found as items or rewards — they CANNOT be bought
- HM01 Cut: obtained from Captain's house in Vermilion City after getting the S.S. Anne ticket or from a rival/professor interaction (actually: given by Captain on S.S. Anne after beating Lt. Surge? **CORRECTION: HM01 Cut is obtained from the Captain of the S.S. Anne after beating your rival on the ship, before the ship leaves.**)
- HM02 Fly: obtained from the Safari Zone Warden? **CORRECTION: HM02 Fly is given by the Safari Zone Warden AFTER you return his Gold Teeth (not HM03 Surf).** Wait — in Pokemon Red/Blue:
  - HM01 Cut: S.S. Anne captain (after rival battle)
  - HM02 Fly: Route 16 (by the woman near the gate, after beating the Snorlax or getting the Bike Voucher? **CORRECTION: HM02 Fly is given by a woman on Route 16 (east of Celadon City) after you show her a Pokémon that knows Cut.**)
  - HM03 Surf: Safari Zone Warden (return his Gold Teeth)
  - HM04 Strength: obtained from a PokéManiac on Route 12 (or given by the Safari Zone Warden? **CORRECTION: HM04 Strength is given to you by a PokéManiac on Route 12, after you get the Pokédex upgrade from Prof. Oak or beat the Fuchsia Gym? Actually: HM04 Strength is given by the Safari Zone Warden AFTER returning his Gold Teeth** — wait, this is conflicting. The Warden gives HM03 Surf. Strength is obtained from the PokéManiac on Route 12 (north of Lavender Town) after beating him.)
  - HM05 Flash: given by Prof. Oak's aide after catching 10 Pokémon (Oak's Parcel sidequest completion)
  - HM06 (in Yellow): various locations

**CORRECTED HM Locations for Gen 1:**
| HM | Location | Requirement |
|----|----------|-------------|
| HM01 Cut | S.S. Anne captain's room | After beating rival on S.S. Anne |
| HM02 Fly | Route 16 (east of Celadon, in the gate) | Show a Pokémon that knows Cut to the woman |
| HM03 Surf | Safari Zone Warden's house (Fuchsia) | Return his Gold Teeth from Safari Zone Area 3 |
| HM04 Strength | Route 12 (north of Lavender Town) | Beat the PokéManiac in the house |
| HM05 Flash | Route 2 (Oak's Aide in the gate) | Catch 10 unique Pokémon in the Pokédex |
| HM06 Whirlpool (not in Gen 1) | N/A | N/A |

**To teach an HM to a Pokémon:**
- Open Bag → find the HM → select "Use on which Pokémon?" → choose the Pokémon
- The Pokémon must be able to learn the HM (e.g., Blastoise can learn Surf, but Charmander cannot)
- HMs cannot be forgotten except by the Move Deleter in Fuchsia City's Pokémon Fan Club (very late game)
- If teaching over an existing move, recommend replacing the least useful move (Tail Whip > Water Gun > Tackle priority typically)

**Badge Requirements for HM use outside battle:**
- HM01 Cut: requires Cascade Badge (Misty)
- HM02 Fly: requires Soul Badge (Koga) or Rainbow Badge? **CORRECTION: Fly requires the Rainbow Badge (Erika) to use outside battle**
- HM03 Surf: requires Soul Badge (Koga) to use outside battle
- HM04 Strength: requires Earth Badge (Giovanni) OR can be used after beating Koga? **CORRECTION: Strength requires the Marsh Badge (Sabrina) to use outside battle**
- HM05 Flash: requires Thunder Badge (Lt. Surge) to use outside battle

### Safari Zone Mechanics
When entering the Safari Zone:
- Cost: 500 Poké Dollars
- You cannot use your own Pokémon — given 500 Safari Balls
- Limited steps (500) — running out causes black out and loss of 500 Poké Dollars
- You can only use Bait (makes Pokémon easier to catch but harder to stay), Rock (makes Pokémon harder to catch but easier to stay), or Safari Ball
- Recommended: Save BEFORE entering, run from all wild Pokémon to conserve steps, only engage when trying to catch
- Finding the Gold Teeth (for HM03 Surf): Enter Safari Zone, go west through door, north through door (Area 2), west through door (Area 3), walk to the small house in upper-left corner, Gold Teeth are on the table — walk up and press A
- After obtaining HM03 Surf, you can also fish for rare Pokémon like Dratini (use Super Rod later)

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |

## Progression Milestones
1. Choose starter (Squirtle recommended for beginners — Water-type has 4x advantage against Brock and Misty)
2. Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
3. Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
4. Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric (Starmie's Water Pulse is strong)
5. Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground (Diglett/Dugtrio from Diglett's Cave)
6. Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
7. Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has; Ground beats Poison for 2x)
8. Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged in Gen 1 — Psychic is immune to Ghost; use Dark-type moves like Bite or just overpower with physical Normal-types since Psychic resists Fighting; or use a Ghost-type that can use Normal moves, but the programming bug means Ghost moves don't affect Psychic)
   **Sabrina's team:** Kadabra Lv38, Mr. Mime Lv37, Venomoth Lv38, Alakazam Lv43
   **Strategy:** Use a fast physical attacker with Normal moves (e.g., Snorlax with Body Slam) or use a Ghost-type (but their Ghost moves won't work — use Normal moves on them)
9. Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
10. Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
11. Elite Four (Lorelei Ice → Bruno Fighting → Agatha Ghost → Lance Dragon → Champion Blue mix) – pack Ice moves for Lance's Dragonites
12. Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)
- **Building Exit Protocol REQUIRES you to specify WHICH direction (left or right) you choose in your reasoning** — do not leave it ambiguous
- **When advising on HM locations and requirements, double-check the Gen 1 specific table above** — many online guides differ or are for later generations
- **Safari Zone exploration:** always save before entering, run from wild Pokémon to conserve steps, and know exactly where the Gold Teeth are (Area 3, small house upper-left corner)
