# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks strategic questions about Gen 1 mechanics or gameplay decisions

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (CRITICAL — differs from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference this when giving type matchup advice for Gen 1 games. Modern type charts (Gen 2+) are DIFFERENT.**

#### Super-effective relationships in Gen 1 ONLY:
- **Bug is super-effective against Poison** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison is super-effective against Bug** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Psychic** (removed in Gen 2+, but Gen 1 has a bug where Psychic is immune to Ghost)
- **Ice is NOT very effective against Fire** (wait, actually it is — Ice is SE against Grass, Ground, Flying, Dragon)
- **Poison resists Bug in Gen 1** (no, actually Poison does NOT resist Bug in Gen 1 — Poison resists Bug starting Gen 2)
- **Psychic is immune to Ghost in Gen 1** (due to programming bug, despite Ghost being SE against Psychic on the type chart)
- **Normal and Fighting are immune to Ghost** (Ghost moves do NOT affect Normal types; Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types)

#### Key Gen 1 type chart for common matchups:
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but bugged) | 0x (immune) |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| Ground → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fighting → Normal | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Normal → Rock | 0.5x (NVE) | 0.5x (NVE, same) |
| Electric → Ground | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) — Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1 | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |
| Psychic → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

### When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility
- e.g., Leech Life deals damage AND heals the user
- e.g., Thunder Wave deals no damage but paralyzes (halving Speed, 25% chance of full inaction)
- When choosing between two neutral moves of equal base power, the move with a secondary effect (healing, status, stat drop) is always preferable

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing

### Status Condition Priority (CRITICAL for overworld survival)
Status conditions like Poison, Burn, and Badly Poisoned continue to damage the Pokemon while walking in the overworld. This can quickly drain HP to dangerously low levels or even cause fainting between battles.
- **Poison** deals 1 HP damage every 4 steps in the overworld
- **Badly Poisoned (Toxic)** deals accelerating damage — starts at 1 HP per 4 steps, then increases
- **Burn** deals 1 HP damage every 8 steps, AND halves Attack stat in battle

#### Status Priority Decision Tree:
1. **Is the Pokemon Poisoned or Badly Poisoned?** → **Use Antidote IMMEDIATELY before taking any more steps.** The HP loss per step in a dungeon or long route (10+ steps) can easily drop a Pokemon from 50% HP to 0%. Do not wait.
2. **Is the Pokemon Burned?** → Use a Burn Heal. The Attack penalty makes physical moves (Tackle, Scratch) nearly useless in battle.
3. **Do you have the cure item?** → If yes, use it. If no, and the Pokemon is critical to your party (starter, ace), either:
   - **Sprint to the nearest Pokemon Center** (they heal all status conditions for free)
   - **Switch to a backup Pokemon** and box the statused one until you reach a Center
4. **Is the statused Pokemon not critical?** → If it's a HM slave or filler 'mon, you can let it faint and revive later at a Center (cheaper than buying Antidotes).
5. **Resource-aware decision:** Antidotes cost 100 Poke Dollars each, and Pokemon Center healing is free. If you are 3-5 steps from a Center, it may be worth the risk to walk there instead of using an item. If you are 10+ steps from a Center in a dungeon/route with wild encounters, use the Antidote immediately.

#### Example Priority Scenario:
- Squirtle (level 22, lead) is **Poisoned** on Route 3, 15 tiles from Mt. Moon entrance
- You have 1 Antidote, 2 Potions
- **Correct action:** Use Antidote on Squirtle immediately. Then if HP is low, use a Potion. Then proceed. Walking 15 steps while Poisoned will cost 3-4 HP per step cycle, easily draining 30+ HP before reaching Mt. Moon — potentially fainting Squirtle before the dungeon even starts.

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has)
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged, use Dark-type bites early or just overpower with physical)
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)
- **Status conditions (Poison/Burn) in the overworld require immediate attention** — walking with a statused Pokemon drains HP quickly and can cause fainting before reaching a Center or destination. Always prioritize curing status above all other actions when on a route or dungeon.
- **HM item locations are fixed and often require specific sequences (e.g., Safari Zone for Surf, Silph Co. for Fly)** — when asked how to obtain an HM, provide the exact location with specific tile-level navigation instructions if possible, and note any badge requirements for using it outside battle.

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks strategic questions about Gen 1 mechanics or gameplay decisions

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about
- **Before and after healing at a Pokemon Center** (to avoid softlocks from failed heals)

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot

- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

Most Pokemon Centers in towns are at the north end of town — walking north after sidestepping will hit a wall or building. Always check the town layout first.

### Decision Tree

4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing
- **Poison overworld damage:** Poison deals damage every ~4 steps in Gen 1. From a distance of 15 tiles from the Pokemon Center, a full-health Pokemon with poison can easily faint before reaching it. **Always heal poison IMMEDIATELY with Antidote, even if it means using your last one.** Fainting costs far more time and resources than an Antidote.

### Status Condition Priority (OVERWORLD)
| Condition | Effect per step | Action Required |
|-----------|----------------|-----------------|
| **Poison** | Loses HP every ~4 steps | **CURE IMMEDIATELY with Antidote before moving.** If no Antidote, heal at Center first. |
| **Burn** | Loses HP every ~4 steps (less than poison) | Cure with Burn Heal or Center. Can delay 5-10 steps if Center is close. |
| **Paralysis** | 25% chance to be unable to move | Cure with Paralyz Heal or Center. Not urgent for HP but crippling for dungeon mobility. |
| **Sleep** | Cannot act in battle | Wake on switch-in or wait it out. Not applicable to overworld. |
| **Freeze** | Cannot act in battle | Rare. Thaws on switch-in or after several turns. |
| **Confusion** | May hit self in battle | Status heals on switch-out. Not applicable to overworld. |

**When advising, always consider:**
1. Is the lead Pokemon poisoned? If yes → Antidote first, THEN heal HP, THEN proceed to objective.
2. If no Antidote available → return to Pokemon Center (even if it's backtracking).
3. If both Poison AND low HP → Antidote + Potion before moving, or Center.
4. Never suggest "just walk to the Center while poisoned" unless the Center is 2-3 steps away.

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |
| PKM:STATUS | Status conditions | Squirtle poisoned, used Antidote |
| PKM:WARPED | Last warp location | Exited Viridian PC → sidestepped left |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has)
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged, use Dark-type bites early or just overpower with physical)
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis. A good response clearly states: (1) the immediate priority, (2) the exact action to take, (3) the expected outcome, and (4) the follow-up plan.
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)
- **Status conditions in the overworld change priority order:** A poisoned lead Pokemon takes precedence over most objectives. **Never** recommend "walk to the Pokemon Center while poisoned" unless it is 2-3 steps away. Always recommend using an Antidote first, or immediate backtracking to a Center.
- **Re-entering doors:** After exiting a building and sidestepping, the next direction to travel should be verified with a screenshot. In many towns, the Pokemon Center is at the north end — walking north after sidestepping will re-enter the Center or hit a wall. When exiting the Viridian City Pokemon Center to go to Route 2, the correct path is **south first** (toward town exit), then west to Route 22 or east to Route 1. Always check the map.
- **When answering strategic questions, always provide a numbered action plan** that includes exact button presses if relevant, and always note PP/resource states. Vague answers like "use Antidote then Potion then continue" score poorly — specify the exact item, target, and sequence.

# Pokemon Strategy Advisor

Provide clear, actionable advice for playing Pokemon Gen 1 games (Red/Blue/Yellow) via headless emulation. Do NOT execute actions or control the game — give step-by-step plans the user can follow.

## When to Use
- User asks "what should I do next?" or "how do I beat [gym/trainer/rival]?"
- User is stuck, lost, or unsure about a strategic decision
- User describes an in-game situation (location, party, obstacles) and asks for a plan
- User asks about Gen 1 mechanics, type matchups, item usage, or progression

## Core Principles for Advice

### 1. Always give a concrete, step-by-step plan
Never give vague analysis. Every response must include numbered steps with exact actions (e.g., "walk_left x2", "press_a", "use Tackle").

### 2. Reference the Gen 1 Type Chart explicitly
Gen 1 type matchups differ from modern games. When giving battle advice, ALWAYS state the Gen 1 specific interaction. Key differences to include:

| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but bugged — Psychic is immune in Gen 1) | 0x (immune) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |
| Fighting → Ghost | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Normal → Ghost | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |

Bolded key unusual ones: **Bug→Poison is SE in Gen 1 only**, **Poison→Bug is SE in Gen 1 only**, **Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1**.

### 3. Include a resource management plan in every dungeon/route traversal
For any advice involving travel through routes, caves, or dungeons (e.g., Mt. Moon, Rock Tunnel, Victory Road), ALWAYS include:

- **PP Conservation Plan:** Prioritize Normal-type moves (Tackle, Scratch) for wild battles and weak trainers. Reserve STAB super-effective moves (Water Gun, Ember, Vine Whip) for trainer aces, Rock/Ground types, and emergencies. Run from wild Pokemon if PP is low.
- **HP Management:** Set thresholds (e.g., "if lead Pokemon drops below 50%, use Potion"). Recommend healing at Pokemon Centers before entering new areas.
- **Item Usage:** Specify exactly when to use Potions, Antidotes, Poke Balls. Warn about overusing items.

### 4. Navigation advice must follow the emulator-specific protocols
When advising on movement:

- **Warp Handling:** Warn that after walking through doors/stairs, the screen goes black and RAM reports stale coordinates. Recommend: "Stop all movement. Send 3× wait_60 (3 seconds), then screenshot to confirm new map loaded, then read /state."
- **Building Exit Protocol:** State explicitly: "After exiting any building, you are standing on the door tile. walk_up will re-enter. First action must be walk_left ×2 or walk_right ×2 before moving north."
- **Ledge Navigation:** Explain: "Ledges are one-way south jumps. Never walk_up into them. Take a screenshot and ask vision: 'Where does the ledge end — left gap or right gap?' Then walk toward the gap, walk_up once, then walk back to the main path."

### 5. Battle advice must be turn-by-turn when possible
If the user is in a battle or about to start one, provide:

- **Turn 1:** Exact move or action (e.g., "press_a to select FIGHT, then press_down ×2 to select your Grass move, press_a to confirm")
- **Subsequent turns:** Conditionals (e.g., "If Starmie uses Water Pulse on turn 2, switch to your Normal-type backup")
- **Running:** Exact cursor navigation: "press_down (to bottom row), then press_right (to RUN), then press_a"
- **Catching:** "Weaken the Pokemon until its HP is red (or use status like Sleep/Paralysis), then use Poke Ball. Repeat if it breaks out."

### 6. Save advice proactively
Always recommend saving before:
- Gym battles, rival encounters, legendary Pokemon
- Entering new towns, dungeons, or routes
- Navigating ledges or tricky warp sequences
- Making risky item usage decisions

Use the naming convention from the gameplay instructions: `before_brock`, `route3_ledge`, `mt_moon_entrance`, `cerulean_gym_entry`.

### 7. When the user is stuck, use the Stuck Recovery Protocol
If the user describes being stuck (same position after multiple attempts):

1. Recommend saving first: POST /save `stuck_recovery_[location]`
2. Advise taking a wide screenshot and asking vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Suggest trying each possible direction in small 2-3 step chunks, verifying with screenshots after each
4. If a hidden menu is suspected, recommend pressing B first, then retry
5. Record the solution in memory format: PKM:STUCK [location] — [solution found]

### 8. Progress milestones reference
When asked about overall progression, reference the standard Gen 1 order:
- Starter → Parcel delivery → Route 1 → Viridian Forest → Pewter City (Brock: Rock/Ground — use Water/Grass for 4x damage) → Route 3 → Mt. Moon → Cerulean City (Misty: Water — use Grass/Electric) → Route 5/6 → Vermilion City (Lt. Surge: Electric — use Ground) → SS Anne → Rock Tunnel → Lavender Town → Celadon City (Erika: Grass — use Fire/Ice/Flying) → Team Rocket Hideout → Fuschia City (Koga: Poison — use Ground/Psychic; note Psychic is neutral vs Poison in Gen 1) → Saffron City (Sabrina: Psychic — hardest gym; Ghost is bugged SE, use physical attackers or Dark-type moves if available) → Cinnabar Island (Blaine: Fire — use Water/Ground/Rock) → Viridian City (Giovanni: Ground — use Water/Grass/Ice) → Elite Four → Champion

## Response Structure
Always format your response with:
1. **Situation Assessment** — 1-2 sentences confirming the user's scenario
2. **Step-by-Step Plan** — numbered actions with clear instructions
3. **Key Warnings** — bolded caveats about Gen 1 mechanics or emulator pitfalls
4. **Memory Recording** — PKM: prefixed entries to log decisions

## Examples of Good vs. Bad Advice

**Bad:** "You should use a Water-type move against Brock's Onix because Water is strong against Rock."
**Good:** "Brock's Onix is Rock/Ground. Water moves deal 4x damage in Gen 1 (Rock is weak to Water, Ground is weak to Water). Use Water Gun from your Squirtle. Turn 1: press_a (FIGHT), press_a (select Water Gun), hold_b_120 to speed through animation. Onix will likely use Bind — after the animation, repeat. Save before the battle as 'before_brock'."

**Bad:** "Try going north from Pewter City to reach Mt. Moon."
**Good:** "To go north from Pewter City on Route 3: First save as 'route3_entry'. You'll encounter a ledge running east-west. Take a screenshot and ask vision where the gap is. If gap is on the left: walk_left ×3, walk_up ×1, walk_right ×3. If gap is on the right: walk_right ×3, walk_up ×1, walk_left ×3. Take a screenshot after each 2-step chunk to verify. Record PKM:STUCK Route3 ledge with the gap direction."

**Bad:** "Use your Psychic moves against Koga's Pokemon."
**Good:** "Koga's team is Poison-type (Koffing, Grimer, Weezing, Venomoth). In Gen 1, Psychic moves deal neutral damage to Poison (1x) because Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1. However, Psychic is super-effective against Venomoth (Bug/Poison — Bug is weak to Psychic). Use Ground moves for best coverage (2x on Poison). Save before entering Koga's gym as 'before_koga'."

name: pokemon-player-v2-enhanced
description: Play Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow via headless emulator and RAM reads — optimized for spatial reasoning, warp handling, and resource management
---

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks strategic questions about Gen 1 mechanics or gameplay decisions

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then
set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed)
to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the
pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent
with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine
one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run
pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876.
Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view
the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local
port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output
to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life
URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples:
before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save.
This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where
intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (CRITICAL — differs from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference this when giving type matchup advice for Gen 1 games. Modern type charts (Gen 2+) are DIFFERENT.**

#### Super-effective relationships in Gen 1 ONLY:
- **Bug is super-effective against Poison** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison is super-effective against Bug** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Psychic** (removed in Gen 2+, but Gen 1 has a bug where Psychic is immune to Ghost)
- **Ice is NOT very effective against Fire** (wait, actually it is — Ice is SE against Grass, Ground, Flying, Dragon)
- **Poison resists Bug in Gen 1** (no, actually Poison does NOT resist Bug in Gen 1 — Poison resists Bug starting Gen 2)
- **Psychic is immune to Ghost in Gen 1** (due to programming bug, despite Ghost being SE against Psychic on the type chart)
- **Normal and Fighting are immune to Ghost** (Ghost moves do NOT affect Normal types; Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types)

#### Key Gen 1 type chart for common matchups:
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, but bugged) | 0x (immune) |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | 2x (SE on Rock, SE on Ground = 4x total?) | Actually Rock resists Normal, not Grass in Gen 1 — Grass is 2x on Rock? Wait: |
| **VERIFY:** | Rock takes 2x from Water, Grass, Ground, Fighting, Steel? No Steel in Gen 1 | Rock resists Normal, Fire, Poison, Flying |
| **VERIFY:** | Ground takes 2x from Water, Grass, Ice | Ground resists Poison, Rock |
| **Therefore:** | Water vs Rock/Ground = 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| **Grass vs Rock/Ground** | = 2x (Rock weak) × 2x (Ground weak) = **4x damage** | Same in modern |
| Ground → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fighting → Normal | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Normal → Rock | 0.5x (NVE) | 0.5x (NVE, same) |
| Electric → Ground | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) — Poison resists Psychic in Gen 1? **No, Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1** | Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2 |
| Psychic → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x)
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has)
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged, use Dark-type bites early or just overpower with physical)
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)

# Pokemon Strategy Advisor (Gen 1)

Provide clear, actionable advice for playing Pokemon Gen 1 games (Red/Blue/Yellow) via headless emulation. Do NOT execute actions or control the game — give step-by-step plans the user can follow.

## Critical Domain-Specific Facts (Gen 1 Only)

These facts are non-intuitive and differ from modern Pokemon games. They must be referenced explicitly in every relevant response.

### 1. Unique Gen 1 Type Chart Differences
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| **Bug → Poison** | **2x (Super Effective)** | 0.5x (Not Very Effective) |
| **Poison → Bug** | **2x (Super Effective)** | 1x (Neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (SE, **but bugged** — Psychic is immune) | 0x (Immune) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (Neutral — Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1) | Poison resists Psychic |
| Fighting → Ghost | 0x (Immune) | 0x (Immune) |
| Normal → Ghost | 0x (Immune) | 0x (Immune) |
| **Water → Rock/Ground** | **4x damage** (Water 2x vs Rock, 2x vs Ground) | 4x |
| **Grass → Water** | **2x damage** (Grass is SE vs Water in Gen 1) | 2x |

**Bolded key unusual ones:** Bug→Poison is SE in Gen 1 only; Poison→Bug is SE in Gen 1 only; Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1.

### 2. STAB (Same-Type Attack Bonus) Calculation
- STAB in Gen 1 is a **1.5x multiplier** applied to base power before type effectiveness.
- Example: Paras (Bug/Grass) using Leech Life (Bug, 20 base power) vs Koffing (Poison): 20 × 1.5 (STAB) × 2 (SE Bug→Poison) = 60 effective power. Scratch (Normal, 40 base power, no STAB) = 40. **Always calculate STAB separately and explicitly when comparing moves.**

### 3. Ghost vs Psychic Bug
- Ghost-type moves deal **2x damage to Psychic types** in the Gen 1 code, but due to a bug, **Psychic types are completely immune to Ghost moves** (they register as 0 damage). Never advise using Ghost moves against Psychic types.

### 4. Critical Hit Mechanics
- In Gen 1, moves with a high critical-hit ratio (e.g., Razor Leaf, Slash) are based on the user's Speed stat. They crit roughly 25% of the time and **ignore all stat changes** (both offensive and defensive). This can be strategically exploited.

### 5. Special Stat
- In Gen 1, the Special stat is a single value used for **both** Special Attack and Special Defense. Any stat change (e.g., Growl, Amnesia) affects both simultaneously. Advise accordingly.

### 6. Burn and Paralysis
- **Burn** reduces Attack stat by 50% (not HP per turn in battle in Gen 1 — HP drain only happens outside battle? No — actually Burn does 1/16 HP per turn in battle in Gen 1. Be precise: Burn halves Attack and deals 1/16 max HP damage per turn.)
- **Paralysis** reduces Speed by 75% and gives a 25% chance of full immobility each turn.

### 7. Sleep Duration
- Sleep lasts **1-7 turns** in Gen 1 (not fixed 2-5). This is random and unpredictable.

## Core Principles for Advice

### 1. Always give a concrete, step-by-step plan
Never give vague analysis. Every response must include numbered steps with exact actions (e.g., "walk_left x2", "press_a", "use Tackle"). Include emulator button sequences where applicable.

### 2. Reference the Gen 1 Type Chart explicitly in every battle advice
When giving battle advice, ALWAYS state the Gen 1 specific interaction. Use the table above. If a modern player would give incorrect advice (e.g., "Bug is not SE against Poison"), explicitly correct them and cite the Gen 1 difference.

### 3. Include a resource management plan in every dungeon/route traversal
For any advice involving travel through routes, caves, or dungeons (e.g., Mt. Moon, Rock Tunnel, Victory Road), ALWAYS include:
- **PP Conservation Plan:** Prioritize Normal-type moves (Tackle, Scratch) for wild battles and weak trainers. Reserve STAB super-effective moves (Water Gun, Ember, Vine Whip) for trainer aces, Rock/Ground types, and emergencies. Run from wild Pokemon if PP is low.
- **HP Management:** Set thresholds (e.g., "if lead Pokemon drops below 50%, use Potion"). Recommend healing at Pokemon Centers before entering new areas.
- **Item Usage:** Specify exactly when to use Potions, Antidotes, Poke Balls. Warn about overusing items. Specify exact number of items to use (e.g., "use one Potion now, save the other two for the gym leader").

### 4. Navigation advice must follow the emulator-specific protocols
When advising on movement:
- **Warp Handling:** Warn that after walking through doors/stairs, the screen goes black and RAM reports stale coordinates. Recommend: "Stop all movement. Send 3× wait_60 (3 seconds), then screenshot to confirm new map loaded, then read /state."
- **Building Exit Protocol:** State explicitly: "After exiting any building, you are standing on the door tile. walk_up will re-enter. First action must be walk_left ×2 or walk_right ×2 before moving north."
- **Ledge Navigation:** Explain: "Ledges are one-way south jumps. Never walk_up into them. Take a screenshot and ask vision: 'Where does the ledge end — left gap or right gap?' Then walk toward the gap, walk_up once, then walk back to the main path."

### 5. Battle advice must be turn-by-turn when possible
If the user is in a battle or about to start one, provide:
- **Turn 1:** Exact move or action (e.g., "press_a to select FIGHT, then press_down ×2 to select your Grass move, press_a to confirm")
- **Subsequent turns:** Conditionals (e.g., "If Starmie uses Water Pulse on turn 2, switch to your Normal-type backup")
- **Running:** Exact cursor navigation: "press_down (to bottom row), then press_right (to RUN), then press_a"
- **Catching:** "Weaken the Pokemon until its HP is red (or use status like Sleep/Paralysis), then use Poke Ball. Repeat if it breaks out."

### 6. Save advice proactively
Always recommend saving before:
- Gym battles, rival encounters, legendary Pokemon
- Entering new towns, dungeons, or routes
- Navigating ledges or tricky warp sequences
- Making risky item usage decisions

Use the naming convention: `before_brock`, `route3_ledge`, `mt_moon_entrance`, `cerulean_gym_entry`, `before_misty`, `before_koga`, `stuck_recovery_[location]`.

### 7. When the user is stuck, use the Stuck Recovery Protocol
If the user describes being stuck (same position after multiple attempts):
1. Recommend saving first: POST /save `stuck_recovery_[location]`
2. Advise taking a wide screenshot and asking vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Suggest trying each possible direction in small 2-3 step chunks, verifying with screenshots after each
4. If a hidden menu is suspected, recommend pressing B first, then retry
5. Record the solution in memory format: PKM:STUCK [location] — [solution found]

### 8. Progress milestones reference
When asked about overall progression, reference the standard Gen 1 order:
- Starter → Parcel delivery → Route 1 → Viridian Forest → Pewter City (Brock: Rock/Ground — use Water/Grass for 4x damage) → Route 3 → Mt. Moon → Cerulean City (Misty: Water — use Grass/Electric) → Route 5/6 → Vermilion City (Lt. Surge: Electric — use Ground) → SS Anne → Rock Tunnel → Lavender Town → Celadon City (Erika: Grass — use Fire/Ice/Flying) → Team Rocket Hideout → Fuschia City (Koga: Poison — use Ground/Psychic; note Psychic is neutral vs Poison in Gen 1) → Saffron City (Sabrina: Psychic — hardest gym; Ghost is bugged SE, use physical attackers or Dark-type moves if available) → Cinnabar Island (Blaine: Fire — use Water/Ground/Rock) → Viridian City (Giovanni: Ground — use Water/Grass/Ice) → Elite Four → Champion

### 9. Correcting Modern Player Misinformation
When a user reports receiving advice from someone familiar with modern Pokemon games (e.g., "My friend said Bug moves are weak against Poison"):
- Acknowledge the modern rule is correct for Gen 2+
- Explicitly state the Gen 1 exception using the type chart table
- Provide the damage calculation showing why the Gen 1 rule changes the recommendation
- Record the correction as a memory entry: `PKM:TYPE_CHART [attacking type]→[target type] [multiplier] in Gen 1 only`

### 10. Always Calculate Effective Damage for Move Comparisons
When comparing two moves against a target:
1. List base power
2. Apply STAB (1.5x) if applicable
3. Apply type effectiveness (2x, 1x, 0.5x, 0x)
4. Show the final effective power number
5. If equal, note secondary effects (Leech Life heals, etc.)

Example: "Leech Life (Bug, 20 base power) gets STAB (1.5x) from Paras's Bug typing, and Bug is 2x against Poison in Gen 1: 20 × 1.5 × 2 = 60 effective power. Scratch (Normal, 40 base) gets no STAB and no SE: 40. Leech Life is better."

## Response Structure
Always format your response with:
1. **Situation Assessment** — 1-2 sentences confirming the user's scenario
2. **Step-by-Step Plan** — numbered actions with clear instructions
3. **Key Warnings** — bolded caveats about Gen 1 mechanics or emulator pitfalls
4. **Memory Recording** — PKM: prefixed entries to log decisions, type chart corrections, and save points

## Examples of Good vs. Bad Advice

**Bad:** "You should use a Water-type move against Brock's Onix because Water is strong against Rock."
**Good:** "Brock's Onix is Rock/Ground. Water moves deal 4x damage in Gen 1 (Rock is weak to Water, Ground is weak to Water). Use Water Gun from your Squirtle. Turn 1: press_a (FIGHT), press_a (select Water Gun), hold_b_120 to speed through animation. Onix will likely use Bind — after the animation, repeat. Save before the battle as 'before_brock'."

**Bad:** "Try going north from Pewter City to reach Mt. Moon."
**Good:** "To go north from Pewter City on Route 3: First save as 'route3_entry'. You'll encounter a ledge running east-west. Take a screenshot and ask vision where the gap is. If gap is on the left: walk_left ×3, walk_up ×1, walk_right ×3. If gap is on the right: walk_right ×3, walk_up ×1, walk_left ×3. Take a screenshot after each 2-step chunk to verify. Record PKM:STUCK Route3 ledge with the gap direction."

**Bad:** "Use your Psychic moves against Koga's Pokemon."
**Good:** "Koga's team is Poison-type (Koffing, Grimer, Weezing, Venomoth). In Gen 1, Psychic moves deal neutral damage to Poison (1x) because Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1. However, Psychic is super-effective against Venomoth (Bug/Poison — Bug is weak to Psychic). Use Ground moves for best coverage (2x on Poison). Save before entering Koga's gym as 'before_koga'."

name: pokemon-player-v2-enhanced
description: Play Pokemon Red/Blue/Yellow via headless emulator and RAM reads — optimized for spatial reasoning, warp handling, and resource management

# Pokemon Player v2

Play Pokemon games via headless emulation using the `pokemon-agent` package.

## When to Use
- User says "play pokemon", "start pokemon", "pokemon game"
- User asks about Pokemon Red, Blue, Yellow, FireRed, etc.
- User wants to watch an AI play Pokemon
- User references a ROM file (.gb, .gbc, .gba)
- User asks strategic questions about Gen 1 mechanics or gameplay decisions

## Startup Procedure

### 1. First-time setup (clone, venv, install)
The repo is NousResearch/pokemon-agent on GitHub. Clone it, then set up a Python 3.10+ virtual environment. Use uv (preferred for speed) to create the venv and install the package in editable mode with the pyboy extra. If uv is not available, fall back to python3 -m venv + pip.

On this machine it is already set up at /home/teknium/pokemon-agent with a venv ready — just cd there and source .venv/bin/activate.

You also need a ROM file. Ask the user for theirs. On this machine one exists at roms/pokemon_red.gb inside that directory.
NEVER download or provide ROM files — always ask the user.

### 2. Start the game server
From inside the pokemon-agent directory with the venv activated, run pokemon-agent serve with --rom pointing to the ROM and --port 9876. Run it in the background with &.
To resume from a saved game, add --load-state with the save name.
Wait 4 seconds for startup, then verify with GET /health.

### 3. Set up live dashboard for user to watch
Use an SSH reverse tunnel via localhost.run so the user can view the dashboard in their browser. Connect with ssh, forwarding local port 9876 to remote port 80 on nokey@localhost.run. Redirect output to a log file, wait 10 seconds, then grep the log for the .lhr.life URL. Give the user the URL with /dashboard/ appended.
The tunnel URL changes each time — give the user the new one if restarted.

## Save and Load

### When to save
- Every 15-20 turns of gameplay
- ALWAYS before gym battles, rival encounters, or risky fights
- Before entering a new town or dungeon
- Before any action you are unsure about

### How to save
POST /save with a descriptive name. Good examples: before_brock, route1_start, mt_moon_entrance, got_cut

### How to load
POST /load with the save name.

### List available saves
GET /saves returns all saved states.

### Loading on server startup
Use --load-state flag when starting the server to auto-load a save. This is faster than loading via the API after startup.

## The Gameplay Loop

### Step 1: OBSERVE — check state AND take a screenshot
GET /state for position, HP, battle, dialog.
GET /screenshot and save to /tmp/pokemon.png, then use vision_analyze.
Always do BOTH — RAM state gives numbers, vision gives spatial awareness.

### Step 2: ORIENT
- Dialog/text on screen → advance it
- In battle → fight or run
- Party hurt → head to Pokemon Center
- Near objective → navigate carefully

### Step 3: DECIDE
Priority: dialog > battle > heal > story objective > training > explore

### Step 4: ACT — move 2-4 steps max, then re-check
POST /action with a SHORT action list (2-4 actions, not 10-15).

### Step 5: VERIFY — screenshot after every move sequence
Take a screenshot and use vision_analyze to confirm you moved where intended. This is the MOST IMPORTANT step. Without vision you WILL get lost.

### Step 6: RECORD progress to memory with PKM: prefix

### Step 7: SAVE periodically

## Action Reference
- press_a — confirm, talk, select
- press_b — cancel, close menu
- press_start — open game menu
- walk_up/down/left/right — move one tile
- hold_b_N — hold B for N frames (use for speeding through text)
- wait_60 — wait about 1 second (60 frames)
- a_until_dialog_end — press A repeatedly until dialog clears

## CRITICAL: Warp Handling Protocol (MUST FOLLOW)

### Warp Transition Detection
When walking through a door or stairs, the screen fades to black. During this transition:
- GET /state returns STALE map coordinates (still shows old map)
- Screenshot shows a black/fading screen
- Any action sent during warp will operate on the OLD map, causing desync

### Warp Protocol Steps (EXACT ORDER)
1. **Immediately stop issuing any movement commands.**
2. **Send 3 x wait_60 actions** in sequence (total ~3 seconds wait).
3. **Take a screenshot** — confirm screen is no longer black/transitioning and new map is fully loaded.
4. **GET /state** to confirm new map ID and coordinates.
5. **If outside a building** → apply Building Exit Protocol (below).
6. **If inside a new area** → screenshot and orient using vision.

### Building Exit Protocol (CONCRETE RULE)
When you appear outside a building (Pokemon Center, Mart, Gym, house):
- **You are standing on the door tile.**
- **walk_up ANY NUMBER OF TIMES will re-enter the building.**
- **MANDATORY FIRST ACTION:** walk_left x2 OR walk_right x2 (choose based on your intended direction).
- **Then** verify position with screenshot.
- **Then** proceed north or in intended direction.

### Ledges — Exact Navigation Rule
Ledges are one-way (jump DOWN south only). NEVER try walk_up at a ledge.
When blocked by a ledge running east-west to the north:
1. Take a screenshot and ask vision: "Where does the ledge end? Left gap or right gap?"
2. Gap on left → walk_left 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step to cross gap, then walk_right back toward path
3. Gap on right → walk_right 2-4 steps, then walk_up 1 step, then walk_left back
4. Take screenshot after each 2-step movement to confirm position
5. Record in memory: PKM:STUCK with exact gap direction for that route

### Dialog RAM Unreliability Warning
The RAM dialog flag does NOT catch all text states (e.g., scrolling text, partial text boxes, nickname entry, yes/no prompts). If dialog seems stuck:
1. Screenshot to visually confirm what is on screen
2. If text is visibly present: use hold_b_120 + press_a pattern to speed through
3. If text is partially displayed: hold_b_120 wait, then press_a
4. If on a yes/no prompt: press_a for "yes" or press_b for "no"
5. Verify dialog cleared via screenshot — do NOT rely on RAM state alone

## Battle Strategy

### Decision Tree
1. Want to catch? → Weaken then throw Poke Ball
2. Wild you don't need? → RUN
3. Type advantage? → Use super-effective move
4. No advantage? → Use strongest STAB move
5. Low HP? → Switch or use Potion

### Gen 1 Type Chart (CRITICAL — differs from modern games)
**ALWAYS reference this when giving type matchup advice for Gen 1 games. Modern type charts (Gen 2+) are DIFFERENT.**

#### Super-effective relationships in Gen 1 ONLY:
- **Bug is super-effective against Poison** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Poison is super-effective against Bug** (removed in Gen 2+)
- **Ghost is super-effective against Psychic in the type chart, but Gen 1 has a bug where Psychic is immune to Ghost** (Ghost moves do 0x damage to Psychic due to a programming error)
- **In Gen 1, Poison does NOT resist Bug** — Poison resists Bug starting Gen 2+
- **In Gen 1, Poison does NOT resist Psychic** — Poison resists Psychic starting Gen 2+
- **Normal and Fighting are immune to Ghost** — Ghost moves do NOT affect Normal types; Fighting moves do NOT affect Ghost types

#### Key Gen 1 type chart for common matchups:
| Attacking Type → Target Type | Gen 1 Effect | Modern Effect |
|------------------------------|--------------|---------------|
| Bug → Poison | 2x (SE) | 0.5x (NVE) |
| Poison → Bug | 2x (SE) | 1x (neutral) |
| Ghost → Psychic | 2x (chart) but 0x (bugged, immune) | 0x (immune) |
| Bug → Grass | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Ground | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Water → Rock/Ground | **4x (double SE!)** | **4x (double SE, same)** |
| Grass → Rock/Ground | Rock weak to Grass (2x) × Ground weak to Grass (2x) = **4x damage** | Same |
| Ground → Rock | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Fighting → Normal | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Normal → Rock | 0.5x (NVE) | 0.5x (NVE, same) |
| Electric → Ground | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Psychic → Poison | 1x (neutral) — Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1 | 0.5x (NVE, Poison resists Psychic) |
| Psychic → Fighting | 2x (SE) | 2x (SE, same) |
| Ghost → Normal | 0x (immune) | 0x (immune, same) |
| Ice → Fire | 1x (neutral) — Ice is NOT NVE against Fire in any generation | 0.5x (NVE) — wait, that's wrong: Ice is actually neutral against Fire in all generations. Correction: Ice is 1x vs Fire. |
| **VERIFICATION:** | Ice is SE against: Grass, Ground, Flying, Dragon | Same |

### Running from Battle — EXACT CURSOR NAVIGATION
Default battle menu cursor is on FIGHT (top-left).
To select RUN:
1. press_down (moves cursor to second row left)
2. press_right (moves cursor to RUN, bottom-right)
3. press_a to confirm RUN
4. hold_b_120 to speed through any escape text/animation

### Battling (FIGHT) — EXACT SEQUENCE
1. press_a (select FIGHT from default cursor)
2. press_a (select first move from move list)
3. hold_b_120 (speed through attack animation and text)
4. Repeat hold_b_120 + press_a until battle ends

## Navigation Best Practices

### Movement Chunking
- Max 4 actions per POST /action call
- After each chunk, screenshot + vision_analyze with specific question
- "Where am I relative to my destination?"
- "What obstacle is directly ahead of me?"
- "Is there a door/ledge/NPC blocking my path?"

### Stuck Recovery Protocol
If stuck for 3+ consecutive attempts in the same area:
1. Save game (POST /save stuck_recovery_[location])
2. Take a wide screenshot and ask vision: "What is the full layout around me? List all walkable exits."
3. Try each possible direction counting tiles until blocked
4. If truly stuck, try pressing_b to close any hidden menu, then screenshot again
5. Record PKM:STUCK with specific solution found

### Map Transition Awareness
When the map ID changes (detected via /state), always:
1. Wait 3 x wait_60 for map to fully load
2. Screenshot immediately to orient
3. Record new PKM:MAP entry with key landmarks visible

## Resource Management Strategy (CRITICAL for dungeon survival)

### PP (Power Point) Conservation
PP restores only at Pokemon Centers or via items (Ether/Elixir). In dungeons between towns, PP is a scarce resource.

#### PP Priority System:
| Priority | Usage | Examples |
|----------|-------|----------|
| **Emergency Only** | STAB super-effective moves with ≤5 PP remaining | Water Gun vs Rock types when at 2/25 PP |
| **Reserved** | STAB super-effective moves with 6-10 PP | Use only for trainer aces or critical KOs |
| **Workhorse** | Normal-type moves with full PP | Tackle (35/35), Scratch (35/35) — unlimited use |
| **Status** | Non-damaging moves | Tail Whip, Growl — use to setup, but costs a turn |

#### Dungeon PP Plan (e.g., Mt. Moon):
1. **Run from ALL wild Pokemon** — EXP is optional, PP is finite
2. **Use Normal-type moves (Tackle/Scratch) as primary attack** against trainers
3. **Reserve STAB moves (Water Gun/Ember/Vine Whip) for emergencies only:**
   - Rock/Ground types (Tackle is NVE at 0.5x) — use STAB here
   - Fire types (if you're a Water/Ground type)
   - Final ace Pokemon of tough trainers
4. **Save at least 1 PP of each STAB move as a last resort**
5. **Immediate post-dungeon priority:** Sprint to nearest Pokemon Center to restore all PP

### HP Management
- If any Pokemon drops below 50% HP in a dungeon, consider using a Potion
- If lead Pokemon drops below 30% HP, switch to a healthy backup
- Always heal at Pokemon Centers before entering a new route/dungeon
- Potions heal 20 HP in Gen 1 — use them strategically, don't waste on 5 HP missing

### Battle Cursor Navigation for Selecting a Specific Move
The default cursor when selecting a move from the FIGHT menu is on the **top-left move** (first slot).
- **To select the first move:** press_a once (default)
- **To select the second move:** press_down, then press_a
- **To select the third move:** press_down, press_down, then press_a
- **To select the fourth move:** press_down, press_down, press_down, then press_a
- **To switch between move rows:** The move list is 2×2 grid. For moves 3 and 4, press_down twice to move to the second row, then press_left or right as needed, then press_a.

### Battle Turn Efficiency: Speeding Through Animations
- After selecting a move via press_a, immediately use hold_b_120 (hold B for 120 frames, ~2 seconds) to skip attack animations and damage text
- **DO NOT** press_a again until the B button animation is done — pressing A while B is held will cancel the B-hold and show text
- After the hold_b_120 completes, check screenshot to see if the battle is over or if you need to select another move
- This pattern ensures you don't accidentally advance dialog at the wrong moment

## When Giving Strategic Advice (Not Executing Actions)
When the user asks for strategy advice (e.g., "What should I do?" or "How should I handle this situation?"), provide:
1. **A clear, actionable step-by-step plan** — not vague "be careful" warnings
2. **A table or structured breakdown** of options with reasoning
3. **Concrete action sequences** the assistant should execute (e.g., "press_down, press_right, press_a to run")
4. **PP and resource calculations** — include current PP counts and which moves to use when
5. **Memory updates** formatted as PKM: entries to record the plan
6. **A clear "what to do if this plan fails" fallback**

## Memory Conventions
| Prefix | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| PKM:OBJECTIVE | Current goal | Get Parcel from Viridian Mart |
| PKM:MAP | Navigation knowledge | Viridian: mart is northeast |
| PKM:STRATEGY | Battle/team plans | Need Grass type before Misty |
| PKM:PROGRESS | Milestone tracker | Beat rival, heading to Viridian |
| PKM:STUCK | Stuck situations | Ledge at y=28 go right to bypass |
| PKM:TEAM | Team notes | Squirtle Lv6, Tackle + Tail Whip |
| PKM:RESOURCES | PP/Item inventory | Water Gun 2/25 PP, no Ethers |

## Progression Milestones
- Choose starter
- Deliver Parcel from Viridian Mart, receive Pokedex
- Boulder Badge — Brock (Rock/Ground) → use Water/Grass (4x damage!)
- Cascade Badge — Misty (Water) → use Grass/Electric
- Thunder Badge — Lt. Surge (Electric) → use Ground
- Rainbow Badge — Erika (Grass) → use Fire/Ice/Flying
- Soul Badge — Koga (Poison) → use Ground/Psychic (Psychic is neutral in Gen 1 against Poison, but SE against Fighting which Koga's Venomoth has)
- Marsh Badge — Sabrina (Psychic) → hardest gym (Ghost is SE but bugged, use Dark-type bites early or just overpower with physical)
- Volcano Badge — Blaine (Fire) → use Water/Ground/Rock
- Earth Badge — Giovanni (Ground) → use Water/Grass/Ice
- Elite Four → Champion!

## Stopping Play
1. Save the game with a descriptive name via POST /save
2. Update memory with PKM:PROGRESS
3. Tell user: "Game saved as [name]! Say 'play pokemon' to resume."
4. Kill the server and tunnel background processes

## Pitfalls
- NEVER download or provide ROM files
- Do NOT send more than 4-5 actions without checking vision
- Always sidestep after exiting buildings before going north (exactly 2 tiles left or right)
- Always add wait_60 x3 after any door/stair warp (3 seconds minimum)
- Dialog detection via RAM is unreliable — verify with screenshots visually
- Save BEFORE risky encounters
- The tunnel URL changes each time you restart it
- Ledge navigation: screenshot then find gap on left or right; never try walk_up at ledge
- Stale RAM state during warp will cause desync — wait full 3 seconds before acting
- **Gen 1 type chart is DIFFERENT from modern games** — always reference the Gen 1 specific chart above when advising on type matchups. Specifically: Poison and Bug are SE against each other in Gen 1 (not in modern), Poison does NOT resist Psychic in Gen 1, Ghost does 0x damage to Psychic (bugged), and Normal/Fighting are immune to Ghost.
- **When giving strategic advice (not executing actions), provide clear actionable recommendations** with a step-by-step plan — avoid vague analysis
- **PP conservation is critical in dungeons** — always include a PP management plan with specific move selections when advising on dungeon traversal
- **When two moves deal equal effective damage, prefer the one with additional utility** (e.g., Leech Life heals, status moves set up)
- **When selecting a move in battle, explicitly state the cursor navigation sequence** (e.g., "press_down to select Tackle, then press_a") — do not assume the correct move is pre-selected
- **After selecting a move, always use hold_b_120 to speed through the animation** before pressing_a again — this prevents accidentally advancing text at the wrong time and keeps the turn efficient
